Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Overview of Topics in Bab Sifat al-Salah
Table of contents for Bab Sifat al-Salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major topics in Bab Sifat al-Salah and anticipate the key Hanafi rulings and points of ikhtilaf covered in the chapter.

Core Idea
Prayer's description covers obligations, duties, and detailed rulings on every posture with noted Hanafi positions.

This passage is the table of contents for the chapter on the description of prayer (Bab Sifat al-Salah). It lists every topic that will be discussed, from the obligations and duties to the method of each action, including where the Hanafi school holds distinct positions and where differences with other schools are presented. Studying this TOC gives you a roadmap for the entire chapter.

Guided Path
1
Identify major sections
Look for headings like فرائض (obligations), واجبات (duties), and the method (طریقہ). These break the chapter into large units.
The TOC starts with 'نماز کے فرائض' and 'نماز کے واجبات'.
2
Locate recurring patterns
Notice the frequent phrase 'اقوال فقہاء' (statements of jurists) and 'دلائل' (proofs). This signals where the author will present different scholarly opinions and their evidence.
Topics like رفع یدین, قرأت فاتحہ, and آمین include these patterns.
3
Spot Hanafi specific issues
Certain topics are classic Hanafi distinctives, such as whether takbir tahrimah is a shart, the ruling on raf' yadayn, and the posture for women in sajdah.
The TOC explicitly lists 'تکبیر تحریمہ شرط ہے یا نہیں' and 'رفع یدین کا حکم'.
4
Anticipate the fiqh sequence
The chapter follows the actual sequence of prayer: from opening takbir to salutation. Use the TOC to mentally rehearse each step of salah.
Items appear in order: takbir, folding hands, thana', ta'awwudh, recitation, ruku', sujud, qa'dah, tashahhud, salam.

Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents for Bab Sifat al-Salah (Chapter on the Description of Prayer) from Ashraf al-Hidayah, an Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah. It lists the topics discussed in the chapter, including the obligations (farā'iz) and duties (wājibāt) of prayer, the rulings on raising hands (raf' yadayn), recitation (qirā'ah), bowing (rukū'), prostration (sujūd), sitting (qa'dah), and concluding with salām. The table also notes where differences of opinion (aqwāl fuqahā) and their proofs are presented. This provides a roadmap for the reader, indicating which rulings and disputes will be covered in the chapter.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbīr taḥrīmah): The opening 'Allahu Akbar' that initiates the prayer and prohibits worldly actions.
رفع یدین (raf' yadayn): The act of raising both hands up to the shoulders or ears during the opening takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Navigating the Chapter on Imamate
An overview of the chapter on Imamate listing topics and page numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate the chapter on Imamate (باب الامامة) by identifying the key topics listed and their sequence.

Core Idea
A chapter's table of contents is a roadmap for mastering its legal rulings.

This lesson introduces the table of contents (TOC) for the chapter on Imamate from Ashraf al-Hidayah, a Hanafi commentary. The TOC lists over 30 topics, from intention in salām to rulings on following an imam in different states. Understanding this structure helps you locate specific rulings efficiently and grasp the chapter's scope before diving into details.

Guided Path
1
Survey the TOC headings
Scan the list to identify the major sections: intention in salām, recitation (qira'ah), who is most entitled to lead, alignment (muḥādhāt), and rulings on following an imam with different states.
The TOC groups related topics, e.g., recitation (jah r and sirr) appears consecutively.
2
Locate a specific ruling
Choose a topic of interest, e.g., 'Ruling on alignment (muḥādhāt)'. Find its position in the list; note the page numbers given (though they may be garbled).
Page numbers allow quick reference to the full discussion.
3
Connect TOC entries to fiqh categories
Recognize that each topic corresponds to a fiqh ruling or dispute, e.g., 'Loud recitation in which prayers?' covers the rule of jahr for Fajr, Maghrib, 'Ishā', Jumu'ah, and 'Eid.
This connects the TOC to the detailed rulings you will study.
4
Assess the TOC's function
Understand that the TOC does NOT provide rulings; it is a navigational aid. The actual proofs and detailed positions are found on the indicated pages.
Avoid mistaking the TOC for a summary.

Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents (front matter) for the chapter on Imamate (باب الامامة) in Ashraf al-Hidayah, an Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, the seminal Hanafi fiqh work by al-Marghinani. It lists over 30 topics with their page numbers, providing an overview of the rulings to be discussed. The topics cover: the intention in salām, loud vs. silent recitation (jahr/ikhfā') in various prayers, the minimum required recitation, recitation in travel and residence, the amounts for each prayer, leading others in prayer (imamah), who is most entitled to lead, issues of alignment (muḥādhāt) of women, following an imam who is in different states (standing/seated, gestures, etc.), and following one in a different category (obligatory/voluntary, literate/illiterate). This TOC serves as a roadmap for the reader, allowing quick navigation to specific rulings. The page numbers likely refer to the original Arabic/Urdu pagination of the commentary.

Key Terms
امامت (imāmah): The position or act of leading the congregational prayer; the chapter heading under which the listed topics fall.
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayer, as opposed to silent (sirr). The TOC indicates that jahr applies to specific prayers (Fajr, Maghrib, 'Isha' first two rak'ahs, Jumu'ah, 'Eid) and for an individual in certain conditions.
مفصل (al-mufaṣṣal): A portion of the Quran from Sūrah Qāf to Sūrah al-Nās, divided into long (ṭiwāl), medium (awāsiṭ), and short (qiṣār) parts for recommended recitation in different prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the table of contents, which of the following topics is explicitly listed?
A) The conditions for wudu to be valid

C) The number of rak'ahs in each obligatory prayer
D) The ruling on wiping over socks

Key Takeaway
A table of contents is a navigational tool that lists topics and page numbers; it does not replace the detailed rulings found in the body of the chapter.

Chapter Overview: Invalidators and Disliked Acts in Prayer
Table of contents listing topics on prayer invalidators and disliked acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given act belongs to the mufsidat (invalidators) or makruhat (disliked acts) of prayer based on the Hanafi classification.

Core Idea
The chapter divides prayer-related acts into those that invalidate (mufsid) and those that are disliked (makruh) but do not break the prayer.

This lesson introduces the table of contents for the chapter on invalidators and disliked acts in prayer from the Hanafi work Ashraf al-Hidayah. Understanding this division helps you navigate the detailed rulings and remember the core categories. The TOC lists specific examples under each category, forming a mental map for future study.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Two Categories
The chapter is split into two main sections: Mufsidat (acts that invalidate prayer) and Makruhat (acts that are disliked but do not invalidate). Identify the Arabic headings in the TOC that signal each category.
The title includes 'ma yufsid al-salah' (what invalidates prayer) and 'ma yukrah fiha' (what is disliked in it).
2
List Key Examples from the TOC
Scan the TOC and pick out at least three examples under Mufsidat (e.g., speaking intentionally, crying from pain, eating/drinking) and three under Makruhat (e.g., cracking fingers, iltafat, sitting like a dog).
These examples will serve as anchors when studying the detailed proofs later.
3
Distinguish Between Invalidators and Disliked Acts
Understand the practical consequence: if a mufsid occurs, the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated; if a makruh occurs, the prayer is valid but deficient in reward. The TOC helps you classify new acts by analogy.
For instance, responding to a sneeze is listed as mufsid, while playing with clothes is makruh.

Chapter: What invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it. Whether speaking in prayer intentionally or forgetfully breaks prayer; sayings of jurists and proofs. Whether crying and weeping in prayer, whether from fear or pain, invalidates prayer; ruling on coughing with or without excuse, similarly sneezing and burping. Responding to a sneeze in prayer invalidates prayer. Ruling on the one praying prompting someone other than his imam. Ruling on a follower prompting his imam; if he hurries in prompting and the imam moves to another verse, ruling on the prompter's prayer. Ruling on responding to someone with 'La ilaha illallah'. If one recites kalima or a verse to alert another that he is in prayer, by consensus the prayer is not invalidated. After praying one rak'ah of Zuhr, then starting 'Asr or nafl, Zuhr prayer becomes invalid. After one rak'ah of Zuhr, starting Zuhr again, the first rak'ah counts. Whether reciting from the mushaf in prayer invalidates; sayings of jurists. If one looks at a written thing and understands it, by consensus it does not invalidate. A woman passing in front of a praying person does not invalidate. It is mustahabb for one praying in the open (field) to set up a sutra. How to set up the sutra close to the praying person. The imam's sutra suffices for the follower. Consideration is given to planting the sutra; placing it down or drawing a line is not sufficient. In the absence of a sutra, the praying person repels a passerby. Disliked acts of prayer. Playing with clothes or body and frivolous acts are makruh; ruling on turning pebbles. Cracking fingers and placing hands on hips is makruh; turning the neck left and right (iltafat) is makruh. Sitting like a dog and spreading arms on the ground are also makruh; ruling on responding to salam in prayer. Ruling on sitting cross-legged and braiding hair. Folding clothes and wearing them loosely (sadl) is makruh. Eating or drinking intentionally or forgetfully invalidates prayer. It is not makruh for the imam to stand inside the mosque and perform sajdah inside the mihrab; standing entirely inside the mihrab is makruh. It is not makruh to pray facing the back of someone sitting and talking. No harm if a mushaf or sword is placed in front of the praying person. Praying on a mat with a picture is not makruh. If above the head, in front, or to the right or left there are pictures, it is makruh. Pictures of the head or chest are not in the same ruling. Praying on a pillow or mat with a picture is not makruh. Praying in clothes with pictures is makruh. Pictures of non-sentient beings are not makruh. Ruling on killing harmful animals during prayer.

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (fihrist) for the chapter 'What invalidates prayer and what is disliked in it' from the Hanafi fiqh work Ashraf al-Hidayah, an Urdu commentary on Al-Hidayah. It lists the topics covered in this chapter, providing a succinct overview of the rulings. The chapter is divided into two main sections: mufsidat (invalidators) and makruhat (disliked acts). The first part discusses invalidators such as speaking, crying, coughing, responding to sneezes, prompting, reciting from the mushaf, eating/drinking, and various situations of niyyah and transition between prayers. The second part covers disliked acts including fidgeting, cracking fingers, sitting postures, praying facing pictures, and others. The page numbers (not included here) guide the reader to the full discussions in the book. This listing is useful for students to memorize the structure of the rulings before delving into detailed proofs and differences.

Key Terms
مفسد صلوٰۃ (mufsid al-salah): An act that invalidates the prayer entirely, requiring repetition if done deliberately or forgetfully under certain conditions.
مکروہ (makruh): An act that is disliked and contrary to the preferred practice, but does not invalidate the prayer.

Navigating a Classical Fiqh Text: The Fihrist of Ashraf Ul Hadaya Vol. 2
Table of contents listing chapter headings and topics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to use the fihrist (table of contents) of Ashraf Ul Hadaya Vol. 2 to locate specific Hanafi rulings on salah, including nawafil, qada, and sajda sahw.

Core Idea
The fihrist is the map to the Hidayah's fiqh treasure — master it to find any ruling quickly.

Before diving into the detailed legal discussions, a scholar must know the layout of the text. The fihrist (table of contents) of Ashraf Ul Hadaya Vol. 2 provides a structured overview of the topics covered, from supererogatory prayers to prostration of forgetfulness. This lesson will help you understand how to use this fihrist to navigate the book efficiently, so you can locate Hanafi rulings and intra-madhhab disputes without getting lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major sections
Scan the fihrist to see the main subject headings. In this volume, the topics are organized around salah: nawafil, congregation (idrak), missed prayers (qada), and sajda sahw. Note the order and grouping.
The headings often indicate a chapter (bab) or a specific ruling (mas'alah).
2
Recognize the types of entries
Entries may be fatwa topics (e.g., 'Rule of praying nafl while sitting after standing'), intra-madhhab disputes (e.g., 'Sayings of the jurists'), or definitions (e.g., 'Meaning of conditional invalidation'). Each gives a clue to the content.
Look for phrases like 'بالا جماع' (by consensus) or 'اقوال فقہاء' (sayings of the jurists) to identify areas of agreement or ikhtilaf.
3
Map key fiqh terminology
Cross-reference technical terms such as 'مدراک الفريضة' (idrak al-farida) and 'سجدہ سہو' (sajda sahw) to their corresponding pages. Understanding these terms helps in searching for specific rulings.
Bookmark these terms for quick lookup during study.
4
Use the fihrist to plan your study
Decide which topic you need to study first. For example, if you miss a prayer, locate the section on 'باب قضاء الفوائت' (chapter on making up missed prayers) and note its subheadings on order and timing.
The fihrist often includes cross-references to related discussions.

Table of contents: Rule of making up (qada) after invalidating a supererogatory prayer (nafl) after starting it; Started four rak'ahs of nafl, recited in first two and performed first sitting, then invalidated the last two rak'ahs – how many rak'ahs must he make up?; Prayed four rak'ahs and did not recite in any – how many rak'ahs must he repeat? Sayings of the jurists; Recited in the first two rak'ahs, not in the last two – by consensus, the last two must be made up; Recited in the last two, not in the first two – by consensus, the first two must be made up; Recited in one of the first two and one of the last two – similarly; Recited in one of the first two and one of the last two – similarly; Recited in one of the first two and one of the last two – how many rak'ahs must he make up?; Recited in only one rak'ah – how many rak'ahs must he make up? Sayings of the jurists; Rule of praying nafl while sitting after standing; Started nafl standing, then completed it sitting without excuse – rule, sayings of the jurists; Rule of praying nafl on an animal outside; Started nafl on an animal, then dismounted and continued – rule; Similarly, dismounted and prayed one rak'ah, then mounted again – he must start anew; Chapter on standing in Ramadan; Congregation for witr is recommended, number of rak'ahs for tarawih; Legal status of congregation for witr; Catching the obligatory prayer; What is the rule for a worshiper if the congregation for an obligatory prayer starts while he is praying?; I had already prayed, then the congregation started – rule of joining the fourth rak'ah; I had prayed one rak'ah, then the congregation started; Rule of leaving the mosque after praying; If one has prayed zuhr and isha, there is no harm in leaving the mosque; Rule of praying sunna of fajr during fajr congregation; If the sunna of fajr are missed, should they be made up after sunrise?; Someone caught one rak'ah of the zuhr congregation – will he be considered as having prayed zuhr with the congregation?; In a mosque where the fard prayer has already been performed, may a later arrival pray supererogatory prayers before the fard?; The one who did not catch the imam in ruku' did not catch that rak'ah; The one who caught the imam in ruku' caught that rak'ah; Time for making up missed prayers; Chapter on making up missed prayers; Order between missed and current prayers; If one advanced a missed prayer despite time constraint, what is the rule?; Rule of order among missed prayers; Missed prayers are old and new – method of performing them; If the number of missed prayers reduces due to performing them, does the order return? Sayings of the jurists; Rule of praying asr even though one remembered not having prayed zuhr – sayings of the jurists; Meaning of 'asr prayer will be valid subject to conditional invalidation'?; Rule of praying fajr without having prayed witr; When is prostration of forgetfulness (sajda sahw) obligatory and how is it performed?; Chapter on prostration of forgetfulness; Prostration of forgetfulness becomes necessary due to an addition that is of the same genus as prayer but not a part of prayer; Abandoning a sunna act necessitates prostration of forgetfulness (application of sunna act); Abandoning surat al-fatiha, qunut, or takbirs of Eid makes prostration of forgetfulness obligatory; Similarly, reciting softly in a loud prayer and loudly in a quiet prayer makes prostration of forgetfulness obligatory.

Key Terms

Rulings on Prayer While Ill
Summarizes multiple rulings for prayer during illness and changing conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on prayer during illness for six different scenarios and apply the condition of change in ability.

Core Idea
When ability changes during prayer, the ruling depends on when and how the change occurs.

This lesson presents several key rulings from the Hanafi school regarding prayer when one's physical ability changes mid-prayer. These scenarios cover starting healthy then falling ill, starting ill then recovering, and other situations like praying in a boat or experiencing unconsciousness. These rulings highlight the principle that prayer must be performed according to one's current ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read each ruling in the passage and identify the specific change in condition (e.g., healthy to ill, ill to healthy, unconsciousness).
2
State the ruling
For each scenario, state what the Hanafi ruling is: complete sitting, start anew, makruh, or qada required.
Memorize these as concise shari'ah rules.
3
Note the authority level
Determine if the ruling is by consensus (ittifaq) or if there is ikhtilaf (disagreement). The passage mentions 'by consensus' for the gesture-to-ability scenario and 'statements of jurists' for others.
Consensus rulings are more binding.
4
Apply to a new situation
Given a similar scenario (e.g., starting standing, then becoming unable to stand but able to gesture), determine the ruling using the pattern from this passage.
This develops practical fiqh application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تندرست نے نماز کھڑے ہو کر شروع کی پھر مرض لاحق ہو گیا بیٹھ کر مکمل کرے حالت مرض میں بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھی اور رکوع سجدہ اشارہ سے کیا پھر تندرست ہو گیا کھڑے ہو کر پہلی نماز پر بنا کرسکتا ہے یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء نماز کی کچھ رکھتیں اشارے سے پڑھیں پھر رکوع سجدہ پر قادر ہوگیا بالاتفاق نئے سرے سے نماز پڑھے نقل کھڑے ہر کر شروع کئے پھر ٹیک لگالی تو کیا حکم ہے بغیر عذر کے بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنا مکروہ ہے کشتی میں بغیر عذر کے بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھنے کا حکم اقوال فقہاء پانچ یا پانچ سے کم نمازوں میں بے ہوشی طاری رہی تو قضا ہے اور اس سے زیادہ میں نہیں
A healthy person started prayer standing, then fell ill; he should complete it sitting. During illness, he prayed sitting and did ruku and sujood by gesture, then recovered; can he build on the first prayer? (Statements of jurists). He prayed some rak'ahs by gesture then became able to do ruku and sujood; by consensus he should pray anew. Report: He started standing then leaned; what is the ruling? Praying sitting without excuse is makruh. Ruling on praying sitting in a boat without excuse (statements of jurists). If unconsciousness occurred for five or fewer prayers, they are to be made up; if more than that, no.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage collects several rulings related to prayer during illness and changing conditions. The first ruling: if a healthy person starts prayer standing and then becomes ill during the prayer, he should continue sitting. The second addresses someone who started in illness with gestures and then recovered; there is ikhtilaf among the fuqaha (the passage does not specify which position is mufta bihi). Third: if someone did some rak'ahs by gesture and then gained ability, the unanimous ruling is to start anew. Fourth: if one starts standing and then leans without excuse, it is makruh. Fifth: praying sitting in a boat without excuse is discussed. Sixth: unconsciousness for five or fewer prayers requires qada; for more, not. These rulings reflect the Hanafi school's detailed treatment of prayer during illness.

Key Terms
بنا (bina'): Building upon a previous prayer when condition changes.
اشارہ (ishara): Gesture for ruku and sujood when unable to perform physically.
کرہ (karaha): Disliked (makruh) act, not sinful but against preferred practice.
قضا (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person starts prayer standing and becomes ill during the prayer, what should he do according to the Hanafi ruling in this passage?
A) Continue standing despite illness
B) Sit down and complete the prayer
C) Break the prayer and restart later
D) Make gestures from lying down

Key Takeaway
Prayer must be completed according to current ability; when ability improves after gestures, consensus says restart; unconsciousness lasting ≤5 prayers requires qada.

Number of Sajda al-Tilawa Places and General Obligation
Establishes number, proof, and basic obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the 14 places of sajda al-tilawa, identify the Hanafi proof (Uthmani mushaf), and apply the obligation to reciter and listener in various prayer contexts.

Core Idea
Sajda al-Tilawa is wajib in 14 places, proven by the companions' consensus via the Uthmani mushaf.

This lesson establishes the foundational ruling of sajda al-tilawa: its number, its proof, and who is obligated. You will learn why the Hanafi school relies on the Uthmani mushaf as evidence and how this obligation applies to both reciter and listener, especially within prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
State what sajda al-tilawa is and its legal status (wajib).
2
Extract the number and proof
From the passage, find the number of sajda places and the source of evidence (Uthmani mushaf).
The author of Hidayah deduces 14 places from the Uthmani mushaf.
3
Understand obligation for reciter and listener
The text states that both the reciter and the listener are obliged to perform sajda in all these places.
امام ومقتدی پر سجدہ تلاوت ہے
4
Analyze follower's recitation
If the follower recites a sajda verse in prayer, the obligation is not to perform sajda immediately but outside prayer.
اگر مقتدی نے آیت سجدہ تلاوت کی تو سجدہ کا حکم نماز سے باہر
5
Apply to hearing from a non-praying person
If a person in prayer hears a sajda verse from someone not in his prayer, performing sajda within prayer does not suffice; he must repeat it after prayer.
نماز میں سجدہ کر لیا تو یہ سجدہ کافی نہیں

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في سجدة التلاوة قرآن کریم میں کل کتنے سجدے ہیں اور کون کون سی سورت میں ہیں صاحب ہدایہ نے ان چودہ مواضع سجدہ پر مصحف عثمان سے استدلال کیا ہے اور مصحف عثمان ہی معتمد ہے ان تمام مواضع میں قاری اور سامع پر سجدہ تلاوت ہے امانجیت سجدہ تلاوت کی تو امام ومقتدی پر سجدہ تلاوت ہے اگر مقتدی نے آیت سجدہ تلاوت کی تو سجدہ کا حکم نماز سے باہر آیت سجدہ سننے والے پر سجدہ تلاوت لازم ہے نماز میں کسی تیسرے شخص سے سجدہ تلاوت کی آیت سنی جو ان کے ساتھ نماز میں نہیں ہے نماز میں یا نماز کے بعد سجدہ کریں گے یا نہیں نماز میں سجدہ کر لیا تو یہ سجدہ کافی نہیں سجدہ کا اعادہ لازم ہے نماز کا اعادہ نہیں امام نے آیت سجدہ کی تلاو کیے اور ایسے شخص نے سنی جونماز میں نہیں تھا امام کے سجدہ کر لینے کے بعد نماز میں داخل ہوا اس پر سجدہ نہیں ہر وہ سجدہ جو نماز میں واجب ہوا غیر نماز میں سجدہ کرنا کافی نہیں ہوگا آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کی اور جدہ نہیں کہ پر کیا نماز میں داخل ہوکر دوبارہ وہی آیت پڑھی اور سجدہ کیا پینجوہ دونوں تلاوتوں سے کفایت کرے گا آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کی پھر سجدہ کیا نماز میں دوبارہ آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کی اب پہلے والا سجدہ کافی نہیں ایک مجلس میں کئی بار آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کی تو ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے سامع کی مجلس بدل گئی تلاوت کرنے والے کی مجلس نہیں بدلی تو سامع پر مکر سجدہ ہے نہ کہ تلاوت کرنے والے پر سجدہ کرنے کا طریقہ نماز یا غیر نماز میں سورۃ پڑھنے کے دوران آیت سجدہ ، چھوڑ نا مکروہ ہے
Chapter on prostration of recitation. How many prostrations are in the Quran and in which surahs? The author of Hidayah deduced these fourteen places of prostration from the Uthmani mushaf, and the Uthmani mushaf is relied upon. In all these places, the reciter and listener have sajda al-tilawa. If the imam recites a sajda verse, then imam and follower have sajda al-tilawa. If the follower recited a sajda verse, the ruling (is that it is out of prayer). A person who hears a sajda verse from someone not in his prayer, in prayer or after prayer, will he perform sajda? If he performed sajda in prayer, that sajda is not sufficient; repeating the sajda is necessary, not repeating the prayer. If the imam recited a sajda verse and a person who was not in prayer heard it and entered prayer after the imam performed sajda, he does not have to perform sajda. Every sajda that becomes wajib in prayer, performing it outside prayer is not sufficient. He recited a sajda verse and did not perform sajda, then entered prayer and recited the same verse again and performed sajda; then (if) the two recitations (will suffice). He recited a sajda verse then performed sajda, then in prayer recited a sajda verse again; now the first sajda is not sufficient. If he recited a sajda verse multiple times in one gathering, one sajda is sufficient. If the listener's gathering changed but the reciter's gathering did not change, then the listener must repeat the sajda, not the reciter. The method of performing sajda. It is makruh to skip an ayah of sajda while reciting a surah in or out of prayer.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Sajda al-Tilawa addresses several rulings. First, it states that there are 14 places of prostration in the Quran, based on the Uthmani mushaf (the compiled Quran under Caliph Uthman), which is the authoritative source. The reciter and the listener are both obliged to perform prostration. If the imam recites such a verse in prayer, both imam and followers perform it. If a follower recites it, the ruling differs. A person who hears a sajda verse from someone not in his prayer must perform sajda after prayer? If he performs it within prayer, it does not suffice; he must repeat the sajda (outside prayer). If the imam recites the verse and a latecomer enters after the imam's sajda, he is not obligated. A sajda that becomes wajib in prayer cannot be fulfilled outside prayer. If one recites twice in one gathering, one sajda suffices. If the listener's gathering changes, he must repeat the sajda. Skipping a sajda verse during recitation is makruh.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran.
مصحف عثمان (mushaf al-uthmani): The standard compilation of the Quran under Caliph Uthman.
مواضع سجدہ (mawadi' al-sajda): Places (verses) where prostration is prescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 15
B) 14
C) 13
D) 11

Key Takeaway
Sajda al-Tilawa is wajib in 14 places as per the Uthmani mushaf, and both reciter and listener are obligated, with specific rules for prayer contexts.

Detailed Rulings on Sajda al-Tilawa: Repetition, Gathering Change, and Method
Details on repetition, gathering change, and etiquette

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules for repeated sajda recitation in one gathering, determine when a listener must repeat sajda due to a change in gathering, and state the ruling of skipping a sajda verse during recitation.

Core Idea
One sajda suffices for multiple recitations in one gathering; changing the listener's gathering requires a new sajda, but not the reciter's.

This lesson tackles the finer points of sajda al-tilawa when verses are repeated or when the listener's situation changes. You will learn the principle of sufficiency in one gathering, the effect of a change in the listener's gathering, and the ruling on intentionally skipping a sajda verse during recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on repeated recitation in one gathering
The passage states that if a sajda verse is recited multiple times in the same gathering, one sajda suffices.
مکر میں کئی بار آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کی تو ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے
2
Determine the effect of a change in the listener's gathering
If the listener's gathering changes but the reciter's does not, the listener must repeat the sajda, but the reciter does not.
سامع کی مجلس بدل گئی ... تو سامع پر مکر سجدہ ہے نہ کہ تلاوت کرنے والے پر
3
Analyze the case of missing sajda then reciting again in prayer
If one recites a sajda verse without performing sajda, then enters prayer and recites it again and performs sajda, the two recitations (i.e., the new sajda) suffice? The text is ambiguous but implies the second sajda covers both.
آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کی اور سجدہ نہیں کیا، پھر نماز میں داخل ہو کر دوبارہ وہی آیت پڑھی اور سجدہ کیا، تو دونوں تلاوتوں سے کفایت کرے گا
4
Understand the ruling on performing sajda after already having done so in prayer
If one recites a sajda verse, performs sajda, then later in prayer recites another sajda verse, the first sajda does not suffice for the second.
آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کی پھر سجدہ کیا، نماز میں دوبارہ آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کی، اب پہلے والا سجدہ کافی نہیں
5
State the ruling on skipping a sajda verse during recitation
It is makruh (disliked) to skip an ayah of sajda while reciting a surah, whether in or out of prayer.
آیت سجدہ چھوڑنا مکروہ ہے

Travel Distance and Onset of Traveler Status
Defines travel distance and onset of traveler status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of travel distance and identify when a person becomes a traveler for prayer.

Core Idea
Travel status begins when one leaves the built-up area and covers about three marhalah (approx 48 miles).

This lesson focuses on the foundational definition of travel (safar) in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding what constitutes a valid journey is essential to determine when qasr becomes obligatory. The passage defines the minimum distance and clarifies how speed is considered differently on land and sea.

Guided Path
1
Define the minimum travel distance
Identify the distance that qualifies as travel: three days' journey at moderate pace (大约 48 miles). This is the Hanafi standard.
Moderate pace means walking, not riding fast.
2
Differentiate land and sea speed
Note that on sea, the speed of land travel is not considered; only the distance traveled matters.
The ruling ensures the distance criterion remains constant.
3
Identify when qasr begins
Qasr starts when one leaves the built-up area of the city. Until then, even if you intend to travel, you pray full.
This is the point of actual departure.
4
Apply to a real scenario
Consider a person who leaves the city limits intending to travel 50 miles. He is a traveler and must begin qasr from that point.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage summarizes key rulings of the chapter on traveler's prayer. It defines travel distance according to Sharia (about 48 miles or three days journey at moderate pace). Speed considered is the average walking speed; in sea, land speed is irrelevant. Qasr (shortening four-rak'ah prayers to two) is the legal ruling for a traveler; if one completes instead, there is a ruling (it is valid but makruh tahrimi in Hanafi school). Qasr begins when one leaves the built-up area of the city. To become a resident (muqeem), one must intend to stay 15 days (Hanafi view). If one intends to leave but ends up staying two years, he still prays qasr if he never intended 15 days. For an army in dar al-harb, intention of residence is not considered due to instability, but in dar al-Islam attacking rebels, it is considered. A traveler may follow a resident imam and must complete his prayer? A traveler may lead residents and should say 'Complete your prayer, for I am a traveler.' If a traveler enters a city without intending residence, he prays complete? Actually, according to the text, if he enters a city, he prays complete even without intention of residence (this is a ruling: if he enters his hometown or a city he intends to stay? The text says 'shahr mein dakhil ho jaye' likely means entering his hometown or a city of residence. The last line: 'watan iqamat watan iqamat se batil ho jata hai' means the domicile of residence is invalidated by another domicile of residence (i.e., when one takes a new residence, the old one no longer counts).

Key Terms
مسافت سفر (masafat al-safar): The minimum travel distance: three days' journey at moderate pace (approx 48 miles).
قصر (qasr): Shortening four-rak'ah prayers to two.
اقامت (iqamat): Intention to reside for 15 days or more, nullifying traveler status.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi travel status requires a minimum distance of three marhalah and begins when leaving the city limits.

The Obligation of Qasr and Its Rulings
States the legal status of qasr and the consequence of completing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasr (wajib) and explain the consequence of completing the prayer instead of shortening.

Core Idea
Qasr is wajib for the traveler; completing four rak'ahs is makruh tahrimi but the prayer is valid.

This lesson zooms into the central ruling of the chapter: the legal status of qasr. The passage explicitly asks about the ruling if one completes (instead of shortening). In Hanafi school, qasr is an obligation (wajib), not just a concession. Understanding this difference impacts how one views the traveler's prayer. We'll also touch on the Shafi'i difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on qasr
Identify that qasr (shortening four-rak'ah prayers) is wajib for the traveler. This is the default rule.
It is not optional; it is a legal requirement.
2
Analyze the case of completing instead
The passage asks: if he completes (prays four), what is the ruling? In Hanafi, the prayer is valid but makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
Validity vs. sin: the obligation is not like fard, but one who completes is sinful.
3
Compare with Shafi'i school
Shafi'i: qasr is a sunnah muakkadah; completing is better. This is a key cross-madhhab difference.
The practical effect: a Hanafi traveler must shorten; a Shafi'i traveler may choose.
4
Note the start point for qasr
Qasr begins immediately upon becoming a traveler (leaving built-up area), not after covering certain distance.
The first prayer after leaving city is performed as qasr.

Residency Intent and Its Legal Effects
Lists rules on residency duration and army exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that intent to stay 15 days makes one a resident, and identify exceptions for armies.

Core Idea
Intent to stay 15 days or more changes a traveler into a resident; without intent, even years of stay keep traveler status.

This lesson examines the rules on residency intent (iqamat). The passage asks: how many days of intent make one a resident? It also addresses the unique situations of a person who intends to leave but stays for two years, and an army in enemy or rebel territory. Understanding these rules is critical for determining when to pray full or short.

Guided Path
1
Identify the duration for residency
The Hanafi rule: if one intends to stay 15 days or more in a place, he becomes a resident (muqeem) and must pray full prayers.
The counting begins from the moment of arrival.
2
Apply the rule to indefinite stay
If a person intends to leave 'today or tomorrow' but ends up staying two years, he remains a traveler as long as he never intended 15 days.
Actual duration is irrelevant; intention is key.
3
Analyze the army scenarios
For an army in dar al-harb (enemy territory), intention of residence is not considered because of instability; they remain travelers. For an army in dar al-Islam fighting rebels, if they intend residence, it is considered.
The difference is based on the security of the area.
4
Note the effect of entering a city
If a traveler enters a city (his destination or hometown), he prays complete even without intending residence? The passage says: 'If a traveler enters a city, he will pray complete even if he did not intend residence.' This refers to entering the city of his watan (permanent home).
Watan asli overrides traveler status.

Wasf vs Sifah and the Meaning of 'Sifah' in the Chapter Title
Defines terms and discusses interpretations of 'sifah'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between wasf and sifah according to Hanafi mutakallimun and state the three scholarly interpretations of 'sifah' in the chapter title.

Core Idea
Sifah is the inherent attribute, wasf is the verbal description — this distinction shapes the chapter's legal analysis.

In the Hanafi legal tradition, precision in terminology is foundational. This passage opens the chapter on the description of prayer by first clarifying a key linguistic and theological distinction: the difference between wasf and sifah. Understanding this distinction is not merely academic; it determines how the subsequent rulings on prayer are categorized. The author then presents three scholarly interpretations of what 'sifah' itself means in the chapter title, each of which affects the scope of the content to follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
Locate the terms 'wasf' and 'sifah' in the passage. Note that lexicographers treat them as synonyms, but Hanafi theologians differentiate them.
2
Distinguish lexical vs technical usage
Understand that lexicographically they are synonymous verbal nouns, but in Hanafi theology (mutakallimun), 'wasf' is the describer's speech, while 'sifah' is the attribute inhering in the subject.
Example: 'Zayd is knowledgeable' (wasf) vs. the knowledge (sifah) within Zayd.
3
Locate the three interpretations of 'sifah'
Find the three views: (1) from al-'Inayah: the overall state derived from pillars and accidents; (2) the matters mentioned in the chapter (obligatory, sunnah, etc.); (3) an implied genitive: 'description of the parts of prayer', meaning their legal qualities.
Each interpretation changes what rulings are included in the chapter.
4
Evaluate the implications
Consider how each interpretation affects the structure of the chapter and the classification of prayer's components. Which view is most practical for legal derivation?
The author does not choose one, implying all are valid perspectives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفۃ الصلوة
بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمـنِ الرَّحِيمِ .
باب صفة الصلوة
ترجمہ (یہ) باب نماز کی صفت ( کے بیان میں ) ہے
تشریح اب تک نماز کے وسائل اور مقدمات کا بیان تھا، اب یہاں سے مقصود یعنی نماز کو ذکر کریں گے۔
اہل لغت کے نزدیک وصف اور صفت دونوں مترادف ہیں اور دونوں مصدر ہیں جیسے وعد اور عدہ۔ اور متکلمین میں سے ہمارے علماء کے نزدیک وصف واصف کا کلام ہے اور صفت و معنی ہے جو موصوف کے ساتھ قائم ہوتا ہے۔ پس زید عالم زید کا وصف ہے نہ کہ صفت اور اس کا علم جو اس کے ساتھ قائم ہے صفت ہے نہ کہ وصف ۔
رہا یہ کہ یہاں صفت سے کیا مراد ہے۔ سو اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے کہا کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ صفت سے مراد نماز کی وہ بہت ہے جو اس کے ارکان اور عوارض سے حاصل ہو اور بعض کا خیال یہ ہے کہ صفت سے مراد وہ امور ہیں جو اس باب میں مذکور ہیں مینی واجبات، فرائض سنن اور مندوبات، پس اس صورت میں صفت کی اضافت صلوۃ کی طرف اضافت جزالی الکل کے قبیلہ سے ہوگئی کیونکہ صفات مذکورہ میں سے ہر صفت نماز کا جز ہے۔ اور بعض نے کہا کہ یہاں مضاف محذوف ہے تقدیری عبارت ہے باب صفتہ اجزاء الصلوۃ اس صورت میں صفت سے مراد کیفیت ہوگی یعنی یہ باب نماز کے اجزاء کی کیفیت (وجوب فرضیت وغیرہ) کے بیان میں ہے۔
نماز کے فرائض
فرائض الصلاة ستة: التحريمة لقوله تعالى و رَبَّكَ فَكَبَرُ والمراد به تكبيرة الافتتاح والقيام لقوله تعالى و قَوْمُوا لِلَّهِ قَانِتِينَ والقراءة لقوله تعالى فَاقْرَءُ وا مَاتَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرآنِ والركوع والسجود لقوله تعالى واركعوا راسجدوا والقعدة في آخر الصلوة مقدار التشهد لقوله عليه السلام لابن مسعود حين علمه التشهد اذا قلت هذا او فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلاتك علق التمام بالفعل قرأ اولم يقرأ
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Chapter on the description of prayer. Translation: This chapter is about the description of prayer. Explanation: Until now, the discussion was about the means and preliminaries of prayer; from here we will mention the objective, i.e., prayer. According to lexicographers, 'wasf' and 'sifah' are synonyms and both are verbal nouns like 'wa'd' and 'iddah'. According to our scholars among the theologians, 'wasf' is the speech of the describer, and 'sifah' is the meaning that subsists in the described. So 'Zayd is knowledgeable' is a 'wasf' of Zayd, not a 'sifah', and his knowledge that subsists in him is a 'sifah', not a 'wasf'. As for what is meant by 'sifah' here, there is disagreement. The author of al-'Inayah said that apparently what is meant by 'sifah' is that state of prayer that is obtained from its pillars and accidents. Some hold the opinion that 'sifah' refers to the matters mentioned in this chapter, i.e., the obligatory, necessary, sunnah, and recommended acts. In that case, the addition of 'sifah' to 'salah' is an addition of part to the whole, because each of the mentioned descriptions is a part of prayer. Some said that there is an omitted genitive construction; the implied expression is 'chapter on the description of the parts of prayer'. In that case, 'sifah' means quality, i.e., this chapter is about the quality (obligatoriness, etc.) of the parts of prayer. The obligatory elements of prayer: The obligatory elements of prayer are six: (1) Tahrimah, because Allah Almighty said: 'And magnify your Lord.' And what is meant by it is the opening takbir. (2) Standing, because Allah Almighty said: 'And stand before Allah with devotion.' (3) Recitation, because Allah Almighty said: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran.' (4) Bowing and (5) Prostration, because Allah Almighty said: 'Bow and prostrate.' (6) The sitting at the end of prayer to the extent of the tashahhud, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Ibn Mas'ud when he taught him the tashahhud: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete.' He made completion contingent on the action, whether he recited or did not recite.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage from 'Ashraf al-Hidayah' begins the chapter on the description of prayer. It first provides a lexical and technical distinction between 'wasf' and 'sifah', two terms that are often used interchangeably but have different connotations in Islamic theology. Lexicographers consider them synonyms, but the Hanafi scholars (mutakallimun) differentiate: 'wasf' is the statement of the describer (e.g., saying 'Zayd is knowledgeable'), while 'sifah' is the actual attribute that inheres in the subject (e.g., the knowledge within Zayd). The author then discusses the various interpretations of what 'sifah' means in the chapter title. One view, from the author of al-'Inayah, is that it refers to the overall state of prayer derived from its pillars and incidental conditions. Another view is that it refers to all the specific rulings mentioned in the chapter—obligations, necessities, sunan, and recommended acts—making the term an instance of 'part-to-whole' addition. A third view posits an omitted word, so the meaning is 'the description of the parts of prayer,' i.e., their legal qualities like obligation. The passage then lists the six obligatory elements (fara'id) of prayer according to the Hanafi school: (1) the opening takbir (tahrimah), (2) standing (qiyam), (3) recitation (qira'ah), (4) bowing (ruku'), (5) prostration (sujud), and (6) the final sitting (qa'dah) for the duration of the tashahhud. Each is supported by a Quranic verse or a hadith. The proof for the final sitting is a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ told Ibn Mas'ud that reciting the tashahhud completes the prayer, indicating its obligation. The author notes that the completion is attached to the action itself, regardless of whether one recited or not, emphasizing that the sitting is a distinct obligatory act.

Key Terms
صفة (sifah): In this passage, sifah refers to the description or quality of prayer, either as the overall state or as the specific components.
وصف (wasf): The verbal description of a quality; according to Hanafi mutakallimun, it is the speech of the describer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mutakallimun, what is the relationship between 'wasf' and 'sifah'?
A) They are perfect synonyms in all contexts.
B) Wasf is the inherent attribute; sifah is the verbal description.
C) Wasf is the verbal description; sifah is the inherent attribute.
D) Wasf refers to attributes of Allah; sifah refers to attributes of created beings.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between wasf (verbal description) and sifah (inherent attribute) is crucial for understanding the chapter's focus on the essential qualities of prayer.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
The Six Obligatory Elements of Prayer (Fara'id al-Salah)
Lists the six fara'id of prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six fara'id of prayer according to the Hanafi school and state the proof (dalil) for each from the Qur'an or Sunnah.

Core Idea
Six acts are fard in prayer: takbir, standing, recitation, bowing, prostration, and final sitting — omission invalidates.

Having clarified the terminology of the chapter, the author now proceeds to enumerate the core obligatory elements of prayer. This is a foundational list in Hanafi fiqh, establishing the minimum required for a valid prayer. Each fard is supported by a clear textual proof from the Qur'an or a hadith, demonstrating the school's reliance on scriptural evidence. This lesson will help you memorize and understand the proofs behind each of the six fara'id.

Guided Path
1
Identify the list
Locate the six items enumerated in the passage. Note the order: tahrimah, qiyam, qira'ah, ruku', sujud, qa'dah.
The passage labels them as 'fara'id' (obligatory).
2
Match each to its proof
For takbir, standing, recitation, bowing and prostration, find the Quranic verses cited. For the final sitting, find the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.
The Quranic verses are: 'And magnify your Lord' (takbir), 'And stand before Allah with devotion' (qiyam), 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' (qira'ah), 'Bow and prostrate' (ruku' and sujud).
3
Analyze the hadith proof for qa'dah
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete.' The Hanafis interpret 'do this' as the sitting, making it obligatory.
The phrase 'or do this' indicates the action of sitting, not the recitation, is the condition for completion.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may count different numbers of fara'id. For example, al-Shafi'i includes the opening takbir as a rukn but counts the basmalah as wajib. The Hanafi list is specifically six.
This ikhtilaf is noted in the hanafi_position_box.
5
Summarize the ruling
The six fara'id are fard 'ayn on every praying person. Omitting any one invalidates the prayer unless compensated by sajdah al-sahw in some cases (e.g., recitation omission may be compensated, but takbir and standing cannot be).
The passage does not detail compensation; that is covered in later lessons.

Source Text

باب صفۃ الصلوة
بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمـنِ الرَّحِيمِ .
باب صفة الصلوة
ترجمہ (یہ) باب نماز کی صفت ( کے بیان میں ) ہے
تشریح اب تک نماز کے وسائل اور مقدمات کا بیان تھا، اب یہاں سے مقصود یعنی نماز کو ذکر کریں گے۔
اہل لغت کے نزدیک وصف اور صفت دونوں مترادف ہیں اور دونوں مصدر ہیں جیسے وعد اور عدہ۔ اور متکلمین میں سے ہمارے علماء کے نزدیک وصف واصف کا کلام ہے اور صفت و معنی ہے جو موصوف کے ساتھ قائم ہوتا ہے۔ پس زید عالم زید کا وصف ہے نہ کہ صفت اور اس کا علم جو اس کے ساتھ قائم ہے صفت ہے نہ کہ وصف ۔
رہا یہ کہ یہاں صفت سے کیا مراد ہے۔ سو اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ صاحب عنایہ نے کہا کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ صفت سے مراد نماز کی وہ بہت ہے جو اس کے ارکان اور عوارض سے حاصل ہو اور بعض کا خیال یہ ہے کہ صفت سے مراد وہ امور ہیں جو اس باب میں مذکور ہیں مینی واجبات، فرائض سنن اور مندوبات، پس اس صورت میں صفت کی اضافت صلوۃ کی طرف اضافت جزالی الکل کے قبیلہ سے ہوگئی کیونکہ صفات مذکورہ میں سے ہر صفت نماز کا جز ہے۔ اور بعض نے کہا کہ یہاں مضاف محذوف ہے تقدیری عبارت ہے باب صفتہ اجزاء الصلوۃ اس صورت میں صفت سے مراد کیفیت ہوگی یعنی یہ باب نماز کے اجزاء کی کیفیت (وجوب فرضیت وغیرہ) کے بیان میں ہے۔
نماز کے فرائض
فرائض الصلاة ستة: التحريمة لقوله تعالى و رَبَّكَ فَكَبَرُ والمراد به تكبيرة الافتتاح والقيام لقوله تعالى و قَوْمُوا لِلَّهِ قَانِتِينَ والقراءة لقوله تعالى فَاقْرَءُ وا مَاتَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرآنِ والركوع والسجود لقوله تعالى واركعوا راسجدوا والقعدة في آخر الصلوة مقدار التشهد لقوله عليه السلام لابن مسعود حين علمه التشهد اذا قلت هذا او فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلاتك علق التمام بالفعل قرأ اولم يقرأ
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Chapter on the description of prayer. Translation: This chapter is about the description of prayer. Explanation: Until now, the discussion was about the means and preliminaries of prayer; from here we will mention the objective, i.e., prayer. According to lexicographers, 'wasf' and 'sifah' are synonyms and both are verbal nouns like 'wa'd' and 'iddah'. According to our scholars among the theologians, 'wasf' is the speech of the describer, and 'sifah' is the meaning that subsists in the described. So 'Zayd is knowledgeable' is a 'wasf' of Zayd, not a 'sifah', and his knowledge that subsists in him is a 'sifah', not a 'wasf'. As for what is meant by 'sifah' here, there is disagreement. The author of al-'Inayah said that apparently what is meant by 'sifah' is that state of prayer that is obtained from its pillars and accidents. Some hold the opinion that 'sifah' refers to the matters mentioned in this chapter, i.e., the obligatory, necessary, sunnah, and recommended acts. In that case, the addition of 'sifah' to 'salah' is an addition of part to the whole, because each of the mentioned descriptions is a part of prayer. Some said that there is an omitted genitive construction; the implied expression is 'chapter on the description of the parts of prayer'. In that case, 'sifah' means quality, i.e., this chapter is about the quality (obligatoriness, etc.) of the parts of prayer. The obligatory elements of prayer: The obligatory elements of prayer are six: (1) Tahrimah, because Allah Almighty said: 'And magnify your Lord.' And what is meant by it is the opening takbir. (2) Standing, because Allah Almighty said: 'And stand before Allah with devotion.' (3) Recitation, because Allah Almighty said: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran.' (4) Bowing and (5) Prostration, because Allah Almighty said: 'Bow and prostrate.' (6) The sitting at the end of prayer to the extent of the tashahhud, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to Ibn Mas'ud when he taught him the tashahhud: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete.' He made completion contingent on the action, whether he recited or did not recite.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage from 'Ashraf al-Hidayah' begins the chapter on the description of prayer. It first provides a lexical and technical distinction between 'wasf' and 'sifah', two terms that are often used interchangeably but have different connotations in Islamic theology. Lexicographers consider them synonyms, but the Hanafi scholars (mutakallimun) differentiate: 'wasf' is the statement of the describer (e.g., saying 'Zayd is knowledgeable'), while 'sifah' is the actual attribute that inheres in the subject (e.g., the knowledge within Zayd). The author then discusses the various interpretations of what 'sifah' means in the chapter title. One view, from the author of al-'Inayah, is that it refers to the overall state of prayer derived from its pillars and incidental conditions. Another view is that it refers to all the specific rulings mentioned in the chapter—obligations, necessities, sunan, and recommended acts—making the term an instance of 'part-to-whole' addition. A third view posits an omitted word, so the meaning is 'the description of the parts of prayer,' i.e., their legal qualities like obligation. The passage then lists the six obligatory elements (fara'id) of prayer according to the Hanafi school: (1) the opening takbir (tahrimah), (2) standing (qiyam), (3) recitation (qira'ah), (4) bowing (ruku'), (5) prostration (sujud), and (6) the final sitting (qa'dah) for the duration of the tashahhud. Each is supported by a Quranic verse or a hadith. The proof for the final sitting is a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ told Ibn Mas'ud that reciting the tashahhud completes the prayer, indicating its obligation. The author notes that the completion is attached to the action itself, regardless of whether one recited or not, emphasizing that the sitting is a distinct obligatory act.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates prayer and makes prohibited what was permissible outside prayer.
قعدة (qa'dah): The sitting at the end of the prayer for the duration of the tashahhud, considered a fard in the Hanafi school.
فرائض (fara'id): Obligatory acts; the six listed are considered fard in prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the six fara'id of prayer mentioned in the passage?
A) Takbir (tahrimah)
B) Standing (qiyam)
C) Saying 'Ameen' after al-Fatiha
D) Final sitting (qa'dah)

Key Takeaway
The six fara'id of prayer—takbir, standing, recitation, bowing, prostration, and final sitting—are each established by a clear textual proof and must be performed for the prayer to be valid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Six Obligatory Acts (Faraid) of Prayer and Their Proofs
Lists the six faraid with proofs and clarifies fiqh terminology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six faraid of prayer according to the Hanafi school, cite the primary proof for each, and explain why Takbir Tahrimah is considered a condition rather than a pillar.

Core Idea
Six acts are fard in prayer: each proven by a Quranic command or Prophetic practice; the opening takbir is a condition, not a pillar.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, the author lays out the six obligatory acts (faraid) of the prayer, each supported by a definitive proof from the Quran or Sunnah. You will not only memorize the list but also understand why the Hanafi school uses the term 'faraid' instead of 'arkan', and why the opening takbir is treated as a condition for validity rather than an integral pillar. This distinction is crucial for correctly classifying obligations and their legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six faraid of prayer
Read the passage carefully and list the six obligatory acts: Takbir Tahrimah, Qiyam, Qiraah, Ruku, Sujud, and Qadah Akhirah.
The Arabic text: التحريمة، القيام، القراءة، الركوع والسجود، القعدة.
2
Locate the primary proof for each obligation
For each fard, find the Quranic verse or hadith cited. Note that the opening takbir is supported by Surah Al-Muddaththir 74:3, standing by Surah Al-Baqarah 2:238, recitation by Surah Al-Muzzammil 73:20, bowing and prostration by Surah Al-Hajj 22:77, and the final sitting by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.
The proofs are mostly imperative verbs, which in Hanafi usul indicate obligation.
3
Understand the terminology: fard vs rukn
The author explains why the term 'faraid' (plural of fard) is used instead of 'arkan' (pillars). Fard includes both pillars and non-pillars (conditions). Takbir Tahrimah is a condition for validity, not a pillar; the final sitting is obligatory but not an original pillar because it is not performed in every rak'ah.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school and affects the ruling if omitted: omitting a condition invalidates, omitting a rukn also invalidates, but omitting a non-pillar fard requires compensation (sajdah sahw).
4
Analyze the extra proofs for Takbir Tahrimah
The passage lists three additional proofs: the Prophet's consistent practice without omission (indicating obligation), consensus (ijma) from his time to today, and the command in the verse. Note that the imperative 'kabbir' is understood to refer to the opening takbir because no other takbir is obligatory by consensus.
This demonstrates the Hanafi method of combining multiple dalils for a single ruling.
5
Evaluate the significance of the faraid for prayer validity
Recognize that intentionally omitting any of these six invalidates the prayer because they are fard. Unintentional omission of non-pillar faraid (like recitation) requires sajdah sahw. This practical consequence shows the legal weight of the classification.
The mufta bihi position is that all six are obligatory; differences among schools on exact number exist.

Source Text

نماز کے فرائض
فرائض الصلاة ستة: التحريمة لقوله تعالى وَ رَبَّكَ فَكَبِّرْ والمراد به تكبيرة الافتتاح والقيام لقوله تعالى وَ قُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَانِتِينَ والقراءة لقوله تعالى فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ والركوع والسجود لقوله تعالى وَارْكَعُوا وَاسْجُدُوا والقعدة في آخر الصلاة مقدار التشهد لقوله عليه السلام لابن مسعود حين علمه التشهد اذا قلت هذا او فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلاتك علق التمام بالفعل قرأ اولم يقرأ

ترجمہ اور نماز کے فرائض چھ ہیں (۱) تحریمہ کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا اور اپنے رب کی بزرگی بیان کر۔ اور تکبیر سے مراد نماز شروع کرنے کی نیت ہے (۲) قیام اللہ تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے اور کھڑے ہو اللہ تعالیٰ کے واسطے بحالت خشوع ، (۳) قرآت اس لئے کہ اللہ رب عزت نے فرمایا قرآن جس قدر آسان ہو پڑھو (۵۴) رکوع اور سجود کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے اور رکوع کرو اور سجدہ کرو، (۲) آخر نماز میں تشہد کی مقدار قعدہ ہے اس لئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جب عبد اللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی تو فرمایا کہ سب تو نے یہ کہا یا اس کو کر لیا تو تیری نماز پوری ہوگی۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز کا پورا ہو نا فعل پر معلق کیا ہے (خواہ) کچھ پڑھا ہو یا نہ پڑھا ہو۔

 بعض اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد اشرف تشریح یہاں قیاس کا تقاضا یہ تھا کہ امام قدوری فرائض الصلوة مست فرماتے لیکن تین سے نو تک اعداد کے استعمال کا قائم کر۔ یہ ہے کہ معدود اگر مذکر ہو تو عدد مونث ہوگا اور اگر معدود مونث ہے تو عدد مذکر ہوگا۔ اور اس جگہ فرائض (محدود) فریضہ کی جمع ہے او باری فریضہ مونث ہے اس وجہ سے عدد مد کر آنا چاہیے تھا۔ جواب: یہاں فرائض فروض کی تاویل میں کر لیا گیا اور فروض جمع ہے فرض کی اور فرض مذکر ہے لہذ استہ کو مونث لانا قاعدے کے مطابق ہوا۔ صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ بعض نسخوں میں فرائض الصلوة مست ہے پس اس نسخہ کی بنا پر کرنے سے کوئی اشکال واقع نہیں ہوگا۔ خدا رہی یہ بات کہ مصنف نے فرائض الصلوۃ کیوں کہا ارکان الصلاة کیوں نہیں ذکر کیا ؟ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ لفظ فرائض عام ہے ؟ میں ارکان اور غیر ارکان ( شرائط ( سب کو شامل ہے۔ اور یہاں تحریمہ جو د کور ہے وہ رکن صلاۃ نہیں بلک جواز صلاۃ کی شرط ہے اور قعدہ اخیر اگر چہ فرض ہے لیکن رکن اصلی نہیں اور رکن اصلی نہ ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ پہلی رکعت میں مشروع نہیں کیا گیا۔ بہر حال مصنفہ ہے" اگر لفظ فرائض کی جگہ ارکان ذکر کرتے تو یہ تحریمہ وغیرہ کو شامل نہ ہوتا۔ اس لئے ایسا لفظ ذکر کیا گیا جوسب کو عام ہو۔ فرض وہ ہے جس کا کرنا دلیل قطعی سے لازم ہو عام اس سے کہ وہ رکن ہے یا شرط اور رکن وہ ہے جو نماز کی ماہیت میں داخل جزو ہوں۔ ( بحر الرائق ) اور کبھی اس کو بھی فرض کہ دیا جاتا ہے جو نہ رکن ہو اور نہ شرط ہو۔

فائد
نماز کا پہلا فرض نماز کے فرائض میں سے اول تحریمہ ہے اور لغت میں تحریمہ کہتے ہیں جعل الشئ محرما کو یعنی کسی کو گرم کیا بنانا۔ یہاں تحریمہ تکبیر اولیٰ کا نام ہے کیونکہ تکبیر اولی ان تمام چیزوں کو حرام کر دیتی ہے جو اس سے پہلے مباح تھیں ۔ اس کے برخلاف حکم کا دوسری تکبیروں کی یہ شان نہیں ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے کہا کہ تکبیر و تحریمہ کہنا مجازی ہے اس لئے کہ تحریم بذات خود تکبیر نہیں بلکہ اس سے تحریم ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اور اسی قرآیہ کنجی تو طہور ہے اور تحریم اس کی تکبیر ہے اور اس کی تحلیل تسلیم ہے۔ کی طرف اس حدیث کا اشارہ ہے مفتاح الصلوة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم (ابودا دکتر ندی) نماز کی دلیل تکبیر تحریمہ کی فرضیت پر چند دلیلیں ہیں۔ اول تکبیر تحریمہ پر حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا پیشگی فرمانا ہے اور بغیر ترک کے کسی چیز پر آپ کا پیشگی فرمان فاسد وجوب کی علامت ہے دوم اجماع ہے کیونکہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانے سے آج تک تکبیر اولیٰ کے وجوب میں کسی کا اختلاف منقول نہیں ہے۔ تیسری دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَ رَبَّكَ فَكَبر آیت میں اللہ اکبر کہنا مراد ہے کیونکہ مروی ہے انـه الـمـانـزل قال رسول الله الله اکبر فكبرت خديجة وفرحت وايقنت انه الوحی یعنی جب یہ آیت اتری تو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کہا کہ اللہ اکبر پس حضرت خدیجہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے بھی تکبیر کہی اور خوش ہوئیں اور یقین کیا کہ یہودی ہے۔ وبہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ تمام مفسرین کا اس پر اجماع ہے کہ اس سے مراد تکبیر تحریمہ ہے نیز کبر صیغہ امر ہے اور امر کا موجب وجوب ہے اور یہ بات بالا جماع ثابت ہے کہ خارج صلاۃ کوئی تکبیر واجب نہیں ہے پس متعین ہو گیا کہ اس سے تکبیر نماز مراد ہے اور تکبیر تحریمہ کے علاوہ بالا جماع نماز میں کوئی تکبیر واجب نہیں ہے پس متعین ہو گیا کہ اس سے مراد تکبیر تحریمہ ہے۔
دوسرا فرض : قیام ہے یعنی فرض نماز اور وتر اور جو حق بفرض ہوں مثلا نمازندران کو کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنا فرض ہے بشرطیکہ قیام اور سجدد
الله
ایمان
ہے۔
دلیل
Chapter on the Description of Prayer. In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Chapter on the Description of Prayer. Translation: This chapter is about the description of prayer. Explanation: Up to now, the means and preliminaries of prayer were mentioned; now from here we will mention the intended subject, i.e., prayer. According to lexicographers, 'wasf' and 'sifah' are synonymous, both are infinitives like 'wa'd' and 'idah'. According to our scholars among the theologians, 'wasf' is the speech of the describer, and 'sifah' is the meaning that subsists in the described. Thus, 'Zayd is knowledgeable' is a description (wasf) of Zayd, not a quality (sifah); and his knowledge that subsists in him is a quality, not a description. As for what is meant by 'sifah' here, there is disagreement. The author of 'Inayah' said that the apparent meaning is that 'sifah' refers to the many aspects of prayer that arise from its pillars and incidental matters. Some opine that 'sifah' refers to the matters mentioned in this chapter, i.e., obligations, duties, sunan, and recommended acts. In that case, the genitive construction of 'sifah' to 'salah' is of the type 'adding the part to the whole', because each of the mentioned qualities is a part of prayer. Some said that there is an omitted modifier, and the implied phrase is 'Chapter on the Description of the Parts of Prayer'; in that case, 'sifah' means modality, i.e., this chapter is about the modality (obligation, duty, etc.) of the parts of prayer.

The Obligatory Acts of Prayer. The obligatory acts of prayer are six: The Tahrimah (prohibitory declaration), due to His saying, 'And magnify your Lord' [74:3], and what is meant is the opening takbir. Standing, due to His saying, 'And stand before Allah in devotion' [2:238]. Recitation, due to His saying, 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' [73:20]. Bowing and Prostration, due to His saying, 'And bow and prostrate' [22:77]. The sitting at the end of prayer to the extent of the tashahhud, due to his (peace be upon him) saying to Ibn Mas'ud when he taught him the tashahhud: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete.' He (peace be upon him) made completion conditional upon the action, whether he recited or not.

[Page 24] Some... Explanation: Here analogically, Imam Quduri should have said 'sitt' for the six obligatory acts, but he said 'sittah'. The rule for using numbers from three to nine is that if the counted noun is masculine, the number should be feminine, and if the counted noun is feminine, the number should be masculine. Here 'fara'id' (the counted noun) is the plural of 'faridah', and 'faridah' is feminine, so it should have been 'sitt' (feminine). Answer: Here 'fara'id' is interpreted as 'furud', the plural of 'fard', and 'fard' is masculine, so making it 'sittah' (feminine) conforms to the rule. The author of 'Inayah' wrote that in some manuscripts it is 'fara'id al-salat sitt', so based on that manuscript there is no problem. As for why the author said 'fara'id al-salat' and not 'arkan al-salat', the answer is that the word 'fara'id' is general, including both pillars and non-pillars (conditions). Here the Tahrimah, which is mentioned, is not a pillar of prayer but a condition for the validity of prayer, and the final sitting, although obligatory, is not an original pillar. The proof that it is not an original pillar is that the final sitting is not prescribed in the first rak'ah. In any case, if the author had used 'arkan' instead of 'fara'id', it would not include the Tahrimah and others. Therefore, he used a word that is general to all. 'Fard' is that whose performance is necessitated by a definitive proof, regardless of whether it is a pillar or a condition. 'Rukn' is that which enters into the essence of prayer as a part. (Bahr al-Ra'iq) And sometimes that which is neither a pillar nor a condition is also called fard.

Benefit: The first obligatory act of prayer, among the obligations of prayer, is the Tahrimah. In language, 'tahrimah' means making something prohibited. Here 'tahrimah' is the name for the first takbir, because the first takbir makes prohibited all those things that were permissible before it. Other takbirs do not have this characteristic. Allamah Ibn al-Humam said that calling the takbir 'tahrimah' is figurative, because prohibition itself is not the takbir; rather, prohibition is established by it. The hadith 'The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition is the takbir, and its analysis is the taslim' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) alludes to this. Evidence for the obligation of the Takbir Tahrimah: There are several proofs. First, the Prophet (peace be upon him) would commence prayer with it and never omit it, and his consistent practice without omission is a sign of obligation. Second, consensus (ijma'), because from the time of the Prophet until today, no disagreement is reported about the obligation of the first takbir. Third, the saying of Allah, 'And magnify your Lord' [74:3], what is meant is to say 'Allahu Akbar', because it is narrated that when this verse was revealed, the Messenger of Allah said 'Allahu Akbar', and then Khadijah (may Allah be pleased with her) also said the takbir and was happy and became certain that it was revelation. The evidence is that all exegetes agree that what is meant is the Takbir Tahrimah. Also, 'kabbir' is a command verb, and a command necessitates obligation. And it is established by consensus that there is no obligatory takbir outside prayer. Therefore, it is determined that what is meant is the takbir of prayer. And besides the Takbir Tahrimah, by consensus no other takbir in prayer is obligatory. So it is determined that what is meant is the Takbir Tahrimah.

Second obligatory act: Standing. That is, for obligatory prayers and witr, and those that are obligatory, like the prayers of a substitute? It is obligatory to pray standing, provided that standing and prostrating...
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (ruling_with_proof) from the chapter on the description of prayer. The author begins by discussing the meaning of 'sifah' (description) lexically and terminologically, noting differences among scholars. Then he lists the six obligatory acts (fara'id) of prayer: (1) Takbir Tahrimah, (2) Qiyam (standing), (3) Qira'ah (recitation), (4) Ruku' (bowing), (5) Sujud (prostration), and (6) Qa'dah Akhirah (final sitting to the extent of tashahhud). Each is supported by a specific Quranic verse or hadith. For the Takbir Tahrimah, he provides additional evidence including the Prophet's continuous practice, consensus (ijma'), and the command in Surah Al-Muddaththir. The passage also clarifies why the term 'fara'id' is used instead of 'arkan': because 'fara'id' includes both pillars (arkan) and conditions (shurut), and the Takbir Tahrimah is actually a condition for the validity of prayer, not a pillar (rukn). Similarly, the final sitting is obligatory but not an original pillar. A grammatical explanation is given for why 'sittah' (feminine number) is used with 'fara'id'—it is interpreted as 'furud' (masculine plural). The author also notes the figurative use of 'tahrimah' for the takbir, citing a hadith. The Hanafi position is that these six are obligatory (fard) based on definitive evidence, and the Takbir Tahrimah is specifically proven by command, practice, and consensus.

Key Terms
تحریمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that marks the beginning of prayer and renders otherwise permissible actions prohibited during prayer.
فرض (fard): An obligation established by definitive proof (dalil qat'i), whose omission invalidates the act if intentional and requires repetition if unintentional.
رکن (rukn): An integral part of prayer that is part of its essence; omission invalidates prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) considered fard but not a rukn (pillar)?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because it is not prescribed in the first rak'ah, so it is not an original pillar.
C) Because it is proven by hadith not by Quran.
D) Because it is a sunnah, not fard.

Key Takeaway
The six obligatory acts (fara'id) of prayer are established by definitive proofs; the opening takbir is a condition, not a pillar, yet still obligatory.

Understanding 'Farā'iḍ' vs 'Arkān' in Hanafi Prayer Terminology
Terminological analysis of 'farā'iḍ'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi text uses 'farā'iḍ' (obligations) instead of 'arkān' (pillars) when describing the essential components of prayer, and state the legal implication of this broader term.

Core Idea
Farā'iḍ includes both pillars and conditions; the author chose this term to encompass all obligatory elements of prayer.

In Hanafi fiqh, precision of terminology often carries legal depth. This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's matn explains why the author used the word 'farā'iḍ' rather than 'arkān' when enumerating the obligatory parts of prayer. Understanding this choice reveals the school's careful classification of obligations established by definitive evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Linguistic Issue
The text notes that by grammatical analogy, since 'farīḍah' (singular of farā'iḍ) is feminine, the numeral should be feminine. But the author uses 'farā'iḍ' with a masculine numeral? Actually the issue is about the form of the word itself; the commentary clarifies that 'farā'iḍ' is interpreted as 'furūḍ' (masculine plural of farḍ). Focus on the terminological shift.
This grammatical discussion is secondary; the main point is the broader scope of 'farā'iḍ'.
2
Understand Why 'Farā'iḍ' is Preferred
The commentator states that 'farā'iḍ' is general ('āmm) and includes both arkān (pillars) and non-arkān (conditions). By using 'farā'iḍ', the author ensures that all obligatory elements are covered, not just the integral parts.
Contrast with 'arkān' which only refers to the essential pillars.
3
Recognize the Legal Significance
In Hanafi fiqh, the term 'farīḍah' denotes an obligation established by qaṭ'ī (definitive) evidence. By using 'farā'iḍ', the author signals that these obligations are binding with certainty. Conditions like ṭahārah (purity) are included as obligatory prerequisites.
This aligns with the Hanafi hierarchy of rulings: farḍ from qaṭ'ī, wājib from ẓannī.

بعض
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد اشرف تشریح یہاں قیاس کا تقاضا یہ تھا کہ امام قدوری فرائض الصلوة مست فرماتے لیکن تین سے نو تک اعداد کے استعمال کا قائم کر۔ یہ ہے کہ معدود اگر مذکر ہو تو عدد مونث ہوگا اور اگر معدود مونث ہے تو عدد مذکر ہوگا۔ اور اس جگہ فرائض (محدود) فریضہ کی جمع ہے او باری فریضہ مونث ہے اس وجہ سے عدد مد کر آنا چاہیے تھا۔ جواب: یہاں فرائض فروض کی تاویل میں کر لیا گیا اور فروض جمع ہے فرض کی اور فرض مذکر ہے لہذ استہ کو مونث لانا قاعدے کے مطابق ہوا۔ صاحب عنایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ بعض نسخوں میں فرائض الصلوة مست ہے پس اس نسخہ کی بنا پر کرنے سے کوئی اشکال واقع نہیں ہوگا۔ خدا رہی یہ بات کہ مصنف نے فرائض الصلوۃ کیوں کہا ارکان الصلاة کیوں نہیں ذکر کیا ؟ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ لفظ فرائض عام ہے ؟ میں
ارکان اور غیر ارکان ( شرائط ( سب کو شامل ہے۔
Chapter: Description of Prayer. Some: Ashraf al-Bidāyah, Urdu commentary of Hidāyah, volume. Explanation: The requirement of analogy was that Imam Qudūrī says 'farā'iḍ al-ṣalāh', but the usage of numbers from three to nine is established. That is, if the counted noun is masculine, the number is feminine, and if the counted noun is feminine, the number is masculine. Here, 'farā'iḍ' (the counted noun) is the plural of 'farīḍah', and 'farīḍah' is feminine, so the number should have come in the feminine form. Answer: Here, 'farā'iḍ' is interpreted as 'furūḍ', and 'furūḍ' is the plural of 'farḍ', and 'farḍ' is masculine, so bringing the number in the feminine form is according to the rule. The author of 'Ināyah wrote that in some copies it is 'farā'iḍ al-ṣalāh' is correct; based on this copy, there is no problem. As for the issue that why the author said 'farā'iḍ al-ṣalāh' and did not mention 'arkān al-ṣalāh', the answer is that the word 'farā'iḍ' is general; it includes both pillars and non-pillars (conditions).
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a linguistic and terminological analysis of why the author of the matn (likely al-Qudūrī) used the plural feminine form 'farā'iḍ' instead of the masculine form 'furūḍ' when referring to the obligatory elements of prayer. The commentator explains that by analogy, since 'farīḍah' (singular of farā'iḍ) is feminine, the numeral should be feminine; however, the author used the feminine form 'must' (meaning 'established'?), implying a feminine numeral. The response is that 'farā'iḍ' here is interpreted as 'furūḍ' (plural of farḍ), which is masculine, so the feminine form is correct. Then it is asked why the author said 'farā'iḍ' instead of 'arkān'. The answer is that 'farā'iḍ' is a broader term that includes both the arkān (integral parts) and the shurūṭ (conditions), such as the opening takbīr (which is a condition) and the final sitting (which is a farḍ but not a primary rukn). This careful choice of terminology ensures all obligatory elements are covered.

Key Terms
فرائض (farā'iḍ): Plural of farīḍah; here used to mean the obligatory elements of prayer, including both arkān (pillars) and shurūṭ (conditions).
ارکان (arkān): Pillars or integral parts of prayer that constitute its essence; omission invalidates the prayer.
شرائط (sharā'iṭ): Conditions for the validity of prayer, not part of its essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author use the word 'farā'iḍ' instead of 'arkān' for the obligatory elements of prayer?
A) Because 'farā'iḍ' is the plural of 'farḍ' and is feminine, matching the numeral.
B) Because 'farā'iḍ' includes both pillars and conditions, while 'arkān' only includes pillars.
C) Because 'arkān' is not an Arabic word.
D) Because the author made a grammatical error.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi choice of 'farā'iḍ' reflects the school's view that conditions are obligatory (farḍ) and must be included when enumerating essential components of prayer.

First Farḍ: Takbīr Taḥrīmah with Proofs
Establishing takbīr taḥrīmah as obligatory with three proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state three proofs for the obligation of takbīr taḥrīmah and explain how each establishes the ruling as farḍ.

Core Idea
Takbīr taḥrīmah is farḍ, proven by the Prophet's practice, ijmā‘, and the Qur’ānic command 'wa rabbaka fakabbir'.

The first farḍ of prayer is the opening takbīr, known as takbīr taḥrīmah because it renders permissible actions forbidden during prayer. This lesson examines three proofs that establish its obligatory nature, drawing from the Sunnah, consensus, and the Qur’ān. Understanding these proofs strengthens your grasp of the prayer's essential integral.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is takbīr taḥrīmah (the opening takbīr). The ruling is farḍ (obligatory).
Note that taḥrīmah means making things forbidden; only the first takbīr has this effect.
2
Locate the first proof
The Prophet's continuous practice (sunnah ʿamaliyyah) without any omission—persistent practice without leaving it indicates obligation (wujūb).
This is a sign of wujūb because the Prophet never omitted it.
3
Locate the second proof
Ijmā‘ (consensus) of the Ummah from the Prophet's time onward that the first takbīr is obligatory. No disagreement has been reported.
Ijmā‘ is a definitive proof in Ḥanafī uṣūl.
4
Locate the third proof
Qur’ānic command 'wa rabbaka fakabbir' (Sūrat al-Muddaththir 74:3). The imperative 'kabbir' indicates obligation. All exegetes agree it refers to takbīr taḥrīmah because by ijmā‘ no takbīr outside prayer or other takbīrs in prayer are obligatory.
The imperative form (ṣīghat al-amr) in Ḥanafī uṣūl yields wujūb unless there is a qarīna (indicator) to the contrary.
5
Evaluate the authority
These three proofs together make the ruling qaṭʿī (definitive) despite the individual chains being zannī; the convergence of multiple evidences raises the certainty.
The hadith 'miftāḥ al-ṣalāh...' is also cited as an additional support but is not one of the three main proofs.

Source Text
