فائد
نماز کا پہلا فرض نماز کے فرائض میں سے اول تحریمہ ہے اور لغت میں تحریمہ کہتے ہیں جعل الشئ محرما کو یعنی کسی کو گرم کیا بنانا۔ یہاں تحریمہ تکبیر اولیٰ کا نام ہے کیونکہ تکبیر اولی ان تمام چیزوں کو حرام کر دیتی ہے جو اس سے پہلے مباح تھیں ۔ اس کے برخلاف حکم کا دوسری تکبیروں کی یہ شان نہیں ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے کہا کہ تکبیر و تحریمہ کہنا مجازی ہے اس لئے کہ تحریم بذات خود تکبیر نہیں بلکہ اس سے تحریم ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اور اسی قرآیہ کنجی تو طہور ہے اور تحریم اس کی تکبیر ہے اور اس کی تحلیل تسلیم ہے۔ کی طرف اس حدیث کا اشارہ ہے مفتاح الصلوة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم (ابودا دکتر ندی) نماز کی دلیل تکبیر تحریمہ کی فرضیت پر چند دلیلیں ہیں۔ اول تکبیر تحریمہ پر حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا پیشگی فرمانا ہے اور بغیر ترک کے کسی چیز پر آپ کا پیشگی فرمان فاسد وجوب کی علامت ہے دوم اجماع ہے کیونکہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانے سے آج تک تکبیر اولیٰ کے وجوب میں کسی کا اختلاف منقول نہیں ہے۔ تیسری دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول وَ رَبَّكَ فَكَبر آیت میں اللہ اکبر کہنا مراد ہے کیونکہ مروی ہے انـه الـمـانـزل قال رسول الله الله اکبر فكبرت خديجة وفرحت وايقنت انه الوحی یعنی جب یہ آیت اتری تو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کہا کہ اللہ اکبر پس حضرت خدیجہ رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہا نے بھی تکبیر کہی اور خوش ہوئیں اور یقین کیا کہ یہودی ہے۔ وبہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ تمام مفسرین کا اس پر اجماع ہے کہ اس سے مراد تکبیر تحریمہ ہے نیز کبر صیغہ امر ہے اور امر کا موجب وجوب ہے اور یہ بات بالا جماع ثابت ہے کہ خارج صلاۃ کوئی تکبیر واجب نہیں ہے پس متعین ہو گیا کہ اس سے تکبیر نماز مراد ہے اور تکبیر تحریمہ کے علاوہ بالا جماع نماز میں کوئی تکبیر واجب نہیں ہے پس متعین ہو گیا کہ اس سے مراد تکبیر تحریمہ ہے۔
Benefit: The first farḍ of prayer from among the farā'iḍ is taḥrīmah. Lexically, taḥrīmah means making something forbidden. Here taḥrīmah refers to the first takbīr, because the first takbīr makes forbidden all things that were permissible before it. Contrary to this, the other takbīrs do not have this effect. ‘Allāmah Ibn al-Humām said that saying ‘takbīr taḥrīmah’ is metaphorical, because the prohibition (taḥrīm) itself is not the takbīr, rather it becomes established through it. And the same is indicated by the hadith 'The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition (taḥrīmah) is the takbīr, and its analysis (taḥlīl) is the taslīm' (Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi). There are several proofs for the obligation of takbīr taḥrīmah in prayer: First, the persistent practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) of saying it, and his persistent practice on something without omission is a sign of obligation. Second, ijmā‘, because from the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) until today, no disagreement has been reported regarding the obligation of the first takbīr. Third, the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And glorify your Lord' (wa rabbaka fakabbir) – the intended meaning is saying 'Allāhu Akbar', because it is narrated that when this verse was revealed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said 'Allāhu Akbar', and Khadījah (may Allah be pleased with her) also said the takbīr and rejoiced and was certain that it was revelation. The inference is that all exegetes agree that what is meant here is the takbīr taḥrīmah. Also, 'kabbir' is an imperative form, and a command necessitates obligation. And it is established by ijmā‘ that no takbīr is obligatory outside prayer; therefore it is determined that what is meant is the takbīr of prayer. And besides takbīr taḥrīmah, no other takbīr is obligatory in prayer by ijmā‘, so it is determined that what is meant is takbīr taḥrīmah.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a proof-based expansion on the first farḍ of prayer: the opening takbīr (takbīr taḥrīmah). The commentator first defines taḥrīmah as making permissible actions forbidden, and explains that only the first takbīr has this effect, not subsequent ones. Ibn al-Humām clarifies this is metaphorical because the prohibition is not the takbīr itself but its effect. The hadith 'miftāḥ al-ṣalāh al-ṭuhūr...' is quoted as evidence. Then three proofs are presented: (1) The Prophet's continuous practice (sunnah ʿamaliyyah), which indicates obligation (wujūb) because he never omitted it. (2) Ijmāʿ (consensus) of the Ummah from his time onward that the first takbīr is obligatory; no disagreement is reported. (3) The Qur’ānic command 'wa rabbaka fakabbir' (Sūrat al-Muddaththir, 74:3). The commentator argues that the verse commands takbīr, and since no takbīr outside prayer is obligatory, the command must refer to the takbīr of prayer. Moreover, by ijmāʿ, no other takbīr in prayer is obligatory except the opening takbīr, so the verse specifically mandates takbīr taḥrīmah. This chain of reasoning (Qur’ān, Sunnah, Ijmāʿ) establishes the ruling with definitive (qaṭʿī) authority.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (taḥrīmah): The opening takbīr of prayer that makes previously permissible actions (like talking) forbidden during prayer.
اجماع (ijmā‘): Consensus of the Muslim scholars on the obligation of takbīr taḥrīmah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a proof presented in the passage for the obligation of takbīr taḥrīmah?
A) The Prophet's consistent practice without omission.
B) The consensus of scholars from the Prophet's time onward.
C) The Qur'ānic verse 'wa rabbaka fakabbir'.
D) The analogy to the takbīr in Eid prayer.

Key Takeaway
Takbīr taḥrīmah is farḍ, proven by the Prophet’s practice, consensus, and the Qur’ānic imperative.

Obligation of Qiyām (Standing) in Prayer
Proof that qiyām is farḍ for those able

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of qiyām in prayer and derive it from the Quranic command using the Hanafi uṣūl principle that amr indicates wujūb.

Core Idea
The command to stand (qūmū) in prayer is an amr, and a command indicates obligation in Hanafi uṣūl.

In this lesson, we examine the second farḍ of prayer: qiyām (standing). The Ḥanafī school holds that standing is obligatory for all farḍ prayers, including witr, provided the person can both stand and prostrate. The proof is drawn from the Qur’ānic verse 'qūmū lillāhi qānitīn' (2:238). We will unpack the Ḥanafī derivation: the imperative form of the verb indicates wujūb, and since there is consensus that standing is not obligatory outside prayer, the obligation is specifically for prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify which prayers require qiyām (farḍ, witr) and the condition: ability to stand and prostrate.
2
Identify the dalīl
Locate the verse (Q 2:238) and the operative phrase 'qūmū lillāhi qānitīn'.
The verse is cited as proof.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalālah
Apply the Hanafi uṣūl rule: the imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wujūb). Since standing outside prayer is not obligatory by consensus, the obligation must be for standing in prayer.
This is a classic dalīl naqlī argument.
4
Note the exception
If a person can stand but cannot prostrate, it is better to sit and pray with gestures.
This shows the condition is both standing and prostrating ability.
5
Summarize the ruling
Qiyām is farḍ for those able; otherwise, sitting with gestures is recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرا فرض : قیام ہے یعنی فرض نماز اور وتر اور جو حق بفرض ہوں مثلا نمازندران کو کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنا فرض ہے بشرطیکہ قیام اور سجدد کرنے پر قادر ہو ۔ اور اگر قیام کر سکتا ہے مگر سجدہ نہیں کر سکتا تو اس کے لئے بیٹھ کر اشارہ سے پڑھنا بہتر ہے۔ قیام کے فرض ہونے کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول قُومُوا لِللَّهِ قَانِتِین ہے یعنی کھڑے ہو اللہ تعالے کے واسطے بحالت خضوع یا خاموشی قنوت کے معنی اطاعت کرنا ، اور بعض کے نزدیک خشوع اور بعض کے نزدیک سکوت اور خاموشی۔ اور عبداللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما سے روایت ہے کہ قنوت کے معنی نماز میں طول قیام کے ہیں۔ آیت سے استدلال اس طور ہوگا کہ خداوند قدوس نے قیام کا امر فرمایا ہے اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے اور خارج نماز بالا تفاق قیام واجب نہیں پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ قیام نماز میں واجب (فرض) ہے۔
The second farḍ: standing. That is, for farḍ prayers, witr, and such prayers that are obligatory (like nafl? actually 'حق بفرض' unclear: 'such prayers that are farḍ'), it is obligatory to pray standing, provided one is capable of standing and prostrating. If one can stand but cannot prostrate, then it is better for him to pray sitting with gestures. The proof for the obligation of standing is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Stand before Allah in devotion' (qūmū lillāhi qānitīn). That is, stand for Allah in a state of humility or silence. Qunūt means obedience; some say it means humility; some say silence. And it is narrated from ‘Abdullāh ibn ‘Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) that qunūt means prolonged standing in prayer. The inference from the verse is that Allah commanded standing, and a command indicates obligation. And outside prayer, by consensus, standing is not obligatory; therefore it is established that standing in prayer is obligatory (farḍ).
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage states the second farḍ of prayer: qiyām (standing). It applies to all obligatory prayers (farḍ ‘ayn, farḍ kifāyah, and witr) for those who can both stand and prostrate. If a person can stand but cannot prostrate due to illness, the better option is to sit and pray with gestures. The proof is the Qur’ānic verse 'qūmū lillāhi qānitīn' (Sūrat al-Baqarah 2:238). The commentator explains 'qānitīn' with various interpretations: obedience, humility, silence, or prolonged standing, citing a hadith of Ibn ‘Umar. The argument follows the Hanafi uṣūl principle: a command (amr) in the Qur’ān indicates obligation (wujūb). Since there is consensus that standing is not obligatory outside prayer, the command must apply to prayer, thus making qiyām farḍ in prayer.

Key Terms
قیام (qiyām): Standing upright in prayer, obligatory for those capable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who can stand but cannot prostrate?
A) He must pray standing and forgo prostration.
B) He should pray sitting with hand gestures.
C) He is exempt from prayer.
D) He may pray lying down.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of qiyām in prayer is established by the Qur’ānic command (amr) and applies only to those able to both stand and prostrate; otherwise, sitting with gestures is the recommended alternative.

Third Farḍ: Qirā’ah (Recitation) of the Qur’ān in Prayer
Proof that qirā’ah is farḍ in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Qur’ānic proof for the obligation of qirā’ah in prayer and explain the uṣūl inference that the imperative (amr) indicates wujūb, with the consensus that recitation outside prayer is not farḍ.

Core Idea
The imperative in the Qur’ān indicates obligation; combined with consensus on non-obligation outside prayer, it proves qirā’ah is farḍ in prayer.

In this passage, the author establishes the third farḍ of prayer: qirā’ah (recitation of the Qur’ān). The proof is a Qur’ānic verse from Sūrat al-Muzzammil, and the reasoning uses a fundamental uṣūl principle: the imperative form (amr) indicates obligation (wujūb). By noting that recitation outside prayer is not obligatory by consensus (ijmā‘), the obligation is confined to the prayer. This lesson will walk you through the proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage identifies qirā’ah (reciting the Qur’ān) as the third farḍ of prayer. Note that it is classified as farḍ (obligatory), not sunnah or wājib.
The exact amount of recitation required is deferred to the chapter on qirā’ah.
2
Locate the dalīl
The proof is the Qur’ānic verse 'faqra’ū mā tayassara min al-qur’ān' (Sūrat al-Muzzammil 73:20). This is the explicit textual evidence.
The verse is quoted directly in the text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The verse uses an imperative verb 'faqra’ū'. In Hanafi uṣūl, the imperative (amr) primarily indicates obligation (wujūb) unless there is evidence to the contrary.
This principle is foundational for deriving farḍ rulings from commands.
4
Apply the consensus (ijmā‘)
The author notes that recitation outside prayer is not farḍ by consensus. This directs the obligation to prayer specifically, since the command applies generally but is restricted to the prayer context.
Without this jjmā‘, one might think recitation is always obligatory.
5
Conclude the ruling
Thus, recitation in prayer is established as farḍ. The proof combines the Qur’ānic imperative with the consensus that recitation outside prayer is not obligatory.
This conclusion is the foundation for further discussions on the minimum length of recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تیسرا فرض : قرآت ہے دلیل اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول فَاقْرَءُ وُا مَاتَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرانِ ہے۔ وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ قرآت کا حکم بصیغہ امر ہے اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے اور نماز سے باہر بالا جماع قرآت فرض نہیں، پس نماز میں قرآت کا فرض ہونا ثابت ہو گیا رہی یہ بات کہ کتنی مقدار پڑھنا فرض ہے؟ سو اس بارے میں فصل القرأۃ میں مفصل کلام کیا جائے گا۔
The third farḍ: recitation. The proof is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'So recite what is easy from the Qur’ān' (faqra’ū mā tayassara min al-qur’ān). The reason for inference is that the command of recitation is in the imperative form, and an imperative indicates obligation. And outside prayer, by consensus, recitation is not farḍ; therefore it is established that recitation in prayer is farḍ. As for how much recitation is farḍ, that will be discussed in detail in the chapter on recitation (faṣl al-qirā’ah).
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage establishes the third farḍ of prayer: qirā’ah (recitation of the Qur’ān). The proof is the Qur’ānic verse 'faqra’ū mā tayassara min al-qur’ān' (Sūrat al-Muzzammil 73:20). The same uṣūl argument is applied: the imperative 'faqra’ū' commands recitation, indicating wujūb. Since recitation outside prayer is not obligatory by consensus, the obligation must be specific to prayer. The commentator notes that the exact amount of recitation (i.e., how many verses or what length) is a separate issue to be addressed later in the chapter on recitation (faṣl al-qirā’ah). This leaves room for detailed discussion but affirms the basic obligation.

Key Terms
قرآت (qirā’ah): Recitation of the Qur’ān during prayer, which is farḍ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'Iqra’ bi-smi rabbika'
B) 'Faqra’ū mā tayassara min al-qur’ān'
C) 'Qūmū lillāhi qānitīn'
D) 'Wa rabbaka fakabbir'

Key Takeaway
The imperative in the Qur’ān, combined with consensus on non-obligation outside prayer, establishes recitation as a farḍ of prayer.

The Obligation of Rukū‘ and Sujūd
Ruling with proof for rukū‘ and sujūd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of rukū‘ and sujūd, identify their proof from the Qur’an, and explain the historical context that necessitated the command.

Core Idea
Rukū‘ and sujūd are farḍ, proven by the imperative 'warka‘ū wasjudū' in the Qur’an.

In this lesson, we examine the fourth and fifth obligatory acts (farā’iḍ) of prayer: bowing (rukū‘) and prostration (sujūd). The author presents the primary proof from the Qur’an and a historical note about early practices. Understanding this ruling is essential for correct prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the farḍ acts
Read the opening sentence: the fourth farḍ is rukū‘ and the fifth is sujūd. Note that sujūd here refers to the prostration in general, but the passage will later discuss the two prostrations.
Sujūd is mentioned as a single farḍ, but each rak‘ah actually contains two prostrations.
2
Locate the dalīl
The proof is the Qur’anic verse 'warka‘ū wasjudū' (Sūrat al-Ḥajj 22:77). The author cites this as the basis for obligation.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalālah
The verse uses the imperative mood (amr). In Ḥanafī uṣūl, the imperative indicates obligation (wujūb) unless there is a qarīnah (context) to the contrary. Here, no such qarīnah exists.
This is the same argument used for other prayer obligations.
4
Consider the historical context
The passage mentions that in early Islam, some people performed only prostration, others only bowing. Allah commanded both together in the verse.
This reinforces that both actions are essential components of prayer.
5
Recognize the scattered nature of prayer pillars in the Qur’an
The author notes that the pillars of prayer are prescribed in different verses: rukū‘ and sujūd in one, qirā’ah in another, qiyām in another, etc. This shows the comprehensive nature of guidance.
This is a benefit (fā’idah) for understanding the Qur’an's structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوتھا فرض رکوع اور پانچواں بجود ہے دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول واركعوا واسجدوا ہے یعنی رکوع کرو اور سجدہ کرو۔ وجہ استدلال و ہی ہے جو سابق میں گذر چکی کہ رکوع اور سجود کا حکم بصیغہ امر ہے اور امر کا موجب وجوب ہے بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ اسلام کے شروع زمانے میں کچھ لوگ سجدہ کرتے تھے مگر رکوع نہیں کرتے تھے اور کچھ رکوع کرتے تھے مگر سجدہ نہیں کرتے تھے پس ان کو حکم کیا گیا کہ رکوع اور سجدہ کے ساتھ نماز پڑھو۔ فائدہ نماز کے ارکان کتاب اللہ میں متفرق کر کے مشروع کئے گئے ہیں چنانچہ کسی آیت میں رکوع اور سجود کا بیان ہے اور کسی میں قرآت کا اور کسی میں قیام کا وغیرہ۔ صاحب شرح نقایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ دوسر اسجدہ واجب یعنی فرض عملی ہے کیونکہ اس کا ثبوت دلیل قطعی سے نہیں ہوا۔ اور بعض فقہاء کا قول ہے کہ دوسرے جدہ کی فرضیت بالا جماع ثابت ہے حتی کہ اگر ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کو ترک کر دیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ پھر فرمایا کہ ہر رکعت میں تکرار سجود نہ کہ تکرار رکوع امر تعبدی ہے یعنی خلاف قیاس ثابت ہے۔ اور بعض نے کہا کہ پہلا سجدہ (آقا) کے حکم کی تعمیل کے لئے ہے اور دوسرا ابلیس کو رسوا اور ذلیل کرنے کے لئے ہے کیونکہ اس نے اللہ کے حکم کے باوجود از راہ تکبر سجدہ نہیں کیا تھا۔ اور بعض کا قول یہ ہے کہ پہلا سجدہ للامر اور دوسرا لشکر ہے۔ بعض نے کہا کہ پہلا سجدہ ایمان کی وجہ سے ہے اور دوسرا بقائے ایمان کی وجہ سے۔ اور بعض نے کہا کہ پہلے سجدے سے انسان کی ابتداء پیدائش کی طرف اشارہ ہے اور دوسرے سے اس کی حالت بقاء کی طرف اشارہ ہے جیسا کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول مِنْهَا خَلَقْنَكُمْ وَفِيهَا نُعِيدُ كُمْ وَمِنْهَا نُخْرِجُكُمْ تَارَةً أخری میں اسی طرف اشارہ کیا گیا ہے۔
The fourth farḍ: rukū‘; the fifth: sujūd. The proof is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And bow and prostrate' (warka‘ū wasjudū). The reason for inference is the same as what has passed before: the command for rukū‘ and sujūd is in the imperative form, and an imperative necessitates obligation. Some say that in the early days of Islam, some people used to prostrate but not bow, and some used to bow but not prostrate; so they were commanded to pray with both rukū‘ and sujūd. Benefit: The pillars of prayer are prescribed in the Book of Allah in different places; thus in one verse rukū‘ and sujūd are mentioned, in another qirā’ah, in another qiyām, etc. The author of Sharḥ al-Niqāyah wrote that apparently the second sajdah is wājib (i.e., practical farḍ) because its establishment is not with a definitive proof. And some jurists say that the obligation of the second sajdah is established by ijmā‘ to the extent that if one omits either of the two, the prayer becomes invalid. Then he said that the repetition of sajdah (but not repetition of rukū‘) in each rak‘ah is a ta‘abbudī (devotional) matter, i.e., established contrary to analogy. And some said that the first sajdah is for fulfilling the command (of Allah), and the second is to disgrace and humiliate Iblīs, because he did not prostrate out of arrogance despite the command of Allah. And some said that the first sajdah is 'lil-amr' (for the command) and the second is 'lashkar' (for the army/soldiers?). Some said the first sajdah is due to faith (īmān) and the second due to remaining in faith. Some said the first sajdah indicates the beginning of creation, and the second indicates the state of survival, as indicated by the saying of Allah: 'From it We created you, and into it We will return you, and from it We will bring you out another time.'
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage covers the fourth and fifth farā’iḍ: rukū‘ (bowing) and sujūd (prostration). The proof is the Qur’ānic imperative 'warka‘ū wasjudū' from Sūrat al-Ḥajj 22:77. The same uṣūl argument applies: the imperative indicates wujūb. A historical note explains that in early Islam, some prayed without rukū‘ and some without sujūd, so the verse commanded both. Then there is a discussion about the two sajdahs in each rak‘ah. According to the author of Sharḥ al-Niqāyah, the second sajdah is considered wājib (practical farḍ) because its proof is not definitive (qaṭ‘ī). However, other jurists assert that its obligation is established by ijmā‘, so omitting either sajdah invalidates the prayer. The commentator then presents various wisdoms (ḥikam) for the repetition of sujūd (but not rukū‘) in each rak‘ah. These include: following the command, humiliating Iblīs, symbolizing faith and its continuation, and indicating the cycle of creation and return to Allah. This is a devotional command (ta‘abbudī) that cannot be measured by analogy. The passage highlights both the legal ruling (obligation of the two sajdahs) and the spiritual wisdoms behind them.

Key Terms
رکوع (rukū‘): Bowing in prayer; an obligatory act.
سجود (sujūd): Prostration; two prostrations per rak‘ah are obligatory.
أمر (amr): Imperative mood in Arabic grammar; in uṣūl al-fiqh, it indicates obligation unless there is a qarīnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof for the obligation of rukū‘ and sujūd according to this passage?
A) The practice of the Companions.
B) The Qur’anic verse 'warka‘ū wasjudū'.
C) The ḥadīth 'Pray as you see me pray'.
D) The ijmā‘ of the Ummah.

Key Takeaway
Rukū‘ and sujūd are farḍ pillars of prayer, proven by the Qur’anic imperative, and omitting either invalidates the prayer.

The Second Sajdah: Obligation and Wisdom
Intra-Hanafi dispute and wisdoms for two sajdahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the second sajdah, state the relied-upon position, and list the wisdoms behind the two prostrations.

Core Idea
The second sajdah is farḍ by ijmā‘, and its repetition is a devotional command with deep spiritual wisdom.

This lesson delves into the second prostration in each rak‘ah. While all agree that two prostrations are required, there is a subtle Ḥanafī internal discussion about the legal status of the second one. The author also presents several wisdoms for why Allah prescribed two sajdahs and not two rukū‘s.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ikhtilāf on the second sajdah
The author of Sharḥ al-Niqāyah said the second sajdah is wājib (practical farḍ) because its proof is not qaṭ‘ī. Other jurists say it is farḍ by ijmā‘.
Wājib in Ḥanafī terminology means obligatory with a ẓannī proof; farḍ requires a qaṭ‘ī proof. This distinction impacts compensation if omitted.
2
Understand the consequence of omission
According to the farḍ view, omitting either sajdah invalidates the prayer entirely. According to the wājib view, the second sajdah omission would require compensation (sajdah al-sahw or repetition) but not necessarily invalidate? Actually, in Ḥanafī fiqh, omitting a wājib does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajdah al-sahw. The passage says if either is omitted, prayer becomes invalid – this supports the farḍ position.
The text states: 'if one omits either, the prayer becomes invalid.' This is the muftā bihī view.
3
Recognize the ta‘abbudī nature
The repetition of sajdah (but not of rukū‘) is ta‘abbudī—established contrary to analogy (khilāf al-qiyās). It is a pure act of worship whose reason is not deduced by human reason.
This means we accept it as commanded without seeking a rational cause.
4
Explore the wisdoms (ḥikam)
The passage lists several explanations: first sajdah for fulfilling the command, second to humiliate Iblīs; first for faith, second for perseverance; first indicates beginning of creation, second indicates return to Allah.
These are not the legal cause but spiritual insights.

اجماع (ijmā‘): Consensus of the mujtahidūn of the Ummah after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

The Final Sitting: Farḍ Ruling and Its Evidence
Proof that the final sitting is farḍ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the final sitting is farḍ, identify its minimum duration, and explain the hadith evidence used.

Core Idea
The final sitting for tashahhud is farḍ; its minimum is the time to recite tashahhud up to 'wa ʿabduhū wa rasūluhū'.

In this lesson, we examine the sixth farḍ of prayer: the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah). The Hanafi school holds it to be farḍ, meaning its omission invalidates the prayer. We will look at the precise definition, the minimum requirement, and the hadith proof cited by the classical authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage clearly states that the sixth farḍ is the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud. Note that the ruling is farḍ, not wājib or sunnah.
The minimum is sitting long enough to recite from 'al-taḥiyyāt' to 'wa ʿabduhū wa rasūluhū'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a ḥadīth narrated by Imam Aḥmad, Abū Dāwūd, and al-Ṭaḥāwī from Ibn Mas‘ūd. The text cuts off but the full narration describes the Prophet teaching the tashahhud while sitting.
The ḥadīth is aḥad (single-chain), so its thubūt is ẓannī.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The Prophet's act of teaching the tashahhud in a sitting position and emphasizing its recitation demonstrates that the sitting itself is an obligatory component.
The Hanafīs infer farḍiyyah from the consistent practice and the command implicit in the teaching.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilāf
Other schools classify the final sitting differently: Shāfiʿīs as a rukn, Mālikīs as sunnah, Ḥanbalīs as wājib. The Hanafīs consider it farḍ, which carries the same practical consequence as a rukn – omission invalidates.
The difference stems from varying evaluations of the ḥadīth and principles of uṣūl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چھٹا فرض بقدر تشہد قعدہ اخیرہ ہے یعنی اتنی مقدار بیٹھنا فرض ہے جس میں التحیات سے عبدہ ورسولہ تک پڑھنا ممکن ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام احمد امام ابو داؤد اور امام طحاوی نے حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ سے روایت کی ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اخذہ بیدہ
The sixth farḍ: the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud. That is, it is farḍ to sit for a duration in which one can recite from 'al-taḥiyyāt' to 'ʿabduhū wa rasūluhū'. The proof is that Imam Aḥmad, Imam Abū Dāwūd, and Imam al-Ṭaḥāwī narrated from ‘Abdullāh ibn Mas‘ūd (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Prophet (peace be upon him) took him by the hand...
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage identifies the sixth farḍ of prayer: the final sitting (qa‘dah akhīrah). The minimum required is sitting long enough to recite the tashahhud from 'al-taḥiyyātu lillāhi...' to '...wa ʿabduhū wa rasūluhū'. The proof is a ḥadīth narrated through multiple chains (Aḥmad, Abū Dāwūd, al-Ṭaḥāwī) from Ibn Mas‘ūd, but the text cuts off before the full narration. The ḥadīth likely describes how the Prophet taught the tashahhud and emphasized its recitation in the final sitting. This establishes the obligation of the final sitting, as opposed to earlier sittings (jalsah bayna al-sajdatayn, etc.) which are sunnah or wājib. The Hanafi school considers the final sitting to be farḍ, while other schools may consider it rukn or sunnah. The incomplete text is supplemented in the original book (Ashraf al-Hidayah) with the full narration.

Key Terms
قعدہ اخیرہ (qa‘dah akhīrah): The final sitting in prayer in which the tashahhud is recited; it is farḍ.
تشہد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in the sitting, beginning with 'al-taḥiyyātu lillāhi'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Reciting from 'al-taḥiyyāt' to 'ʿabduhū wa rasūluhū'
C) Reciting any verse from the Qur’an
D) Saying 'Allāhu Akbar' once

Key Takeaway
The final sitting (qa‘dah akhīrah) is farḍ; its minimum is sitting for the duration of reciting the tashahhud, and omitting it invalidates the prayer.

Proof for Qiyam and Qira'ah as Fard Acts
Proof for qiyam and qira'ah using Quranic amr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic proofs for the obligation of standing (qiyam) and recitation (qira'ah) in prayer and explain how the imperative (amr) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The imperative form in the Quran proves that standing and recitation are fard in prayer.

In this lesson, we examine the textual proofs from the Quran for two of the fard acts of prayer: standing (qiyam) and recitation (qira'ah). The author of al-Hidayah uses the principle that a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub). Since these acts are not obligatory by consensus outside of prayer, their obligation within prayer is established solely by the divine command.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fard act being proved
First, we look at standing (qiyam). The author states that the proof is the verse 'Qumu lillahi qanitin' (al-Baqarah 2:238).
2
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
The imperative (amr) in the verse indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub. The author notes that outside prayer, standing is not obligatory by consensus, so the obligation is specific to prayer.
This is the key reasoning: amr + absence of external qarinah = wujub.
3
Repeat for recitation (qira'ah)
The same reasoning applies to the verse 'Faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' (al-Muzzammil 73:20). The imperative form indicates obligation, and since recitation outside prayer is not obligatory, it becomes fard within prayer.
The exact amount of recitation will be detailed later.

Source Text

باب صفة الصلوة
کرنے پر قادر ہو ۔ اور اگر قیام کر سکتا ہے مگر سجدہ نہیں کر سکتا تو اس کے لئے بیٹھ کر اشارہ سے پڑھنا بہتر ہے۔ قیام کے فرض ہونے کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول قُومُوا لِللَّهِ قَانِتِین ہے یعنی کھڑے ہو اللہ تعالے کے واسطے بحالت خضوع یا خاموشی قنوت کے معنی اطاعت کرنا ، اور بعض کے نزدیک خشوع اور بعض کے نزدیک سکوت اور خاموشی۔ اور عبداللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما سے روایت ہے کہ قنوت کے معنی نماز میں طول قیام کے ہیں۔ آیت سے استدلال اس طور ہوگا کہ خداوند قدوس نے قیام کا امر فرمایا ہے اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے اور خارج نماز بالا تفاق قیام واجب نہیں پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ قیام نماز میں واجب (فرض) ہے۔ تیسرا فرض : قرآت ہے دلیل اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول فَاقْرَءُ وُا مَاتَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرانِ ہے۔ وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ قرآت کا حکم بصیغہ امر ہے اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے اور نماز سے باہر بالا جماع قرآت فرض نہیں، پس نماز میں قرآت کا فرض ہونا ثابت ہو گیا رہی یہ بات
کہ کتنی مقدار پڑھنا فرض ہے؟ سو اس بارے میں فصل القرأۃ میں مفصل کلام کیا جائے گا۔
چوتھا فرض رکوع اور پانچواں بجود ہے دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول واركعوا واسجدوا ہے یعنی رکوع کرو اور سجدہ کرو۔ وجہ استدلال و ہی ہے جو سابق میں گذر چکی کہ رکوع اور سجود کا حکم بصیغہ امر ہے اور امر کا موجب وجوب ہے بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ اسلام کے شروع زمانے میں کچھ لوگ سجدہ کرتے تھے مگر رکوع نہیں کرتے تھے اور کچھ رکوع کرتے تھے مگر سجدہ نہیں کرتے تھے پس ان کو حکم کیا گیا کہ رکوع اور سجدہ کے ساتھ نماز پڑھو۔ فائدہ نماز کے ارکان کتاب اللہ میں متفرق کر کے مشروع کئے گئے ہیں چنانچہ کسی آیت میں رکوع اور سجود کا بیان ہے اور کسی میں قرآت کا اور کسی میں قیام کا وغیرہ۔ صاحب شرح نقایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ دوسر اسجدہ واجب یعنی فرض عملی ہے کیونکہ اس کا ثبوت دلیل قطعی سے نہیں ہوا۔ اور بعض فقہاء کا قول ہے کہ دوسرے جدہ کی فرضیت بالا جماع ثابت ہے حتی کہ اگر ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کو ترک کر دیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ پھر فرمایا کہ ہر رکعت میں تکرار سجود نہ کہ تکرار رکوع امر تعبدی ہے یعنی خلاف قیاس ثابت ہے۔ اور بعض نے کہا کہ پہلا سجدہ (آقا) کے حکم کی تعمیل کے لئے ہے اور دوسرا ابلیس کو رسوا اور ذلیل کرنے کے لئے ہے کیونکہ اس نے اللہ کے حکم کے باوجود از راہ تکبر سجدہ نہیں کیا تھا۔ اور بعض کا قول یہ ہے کہ پہلا سجدہ للامر اور دوسرا لشکر ہے۔ بعض نے کہا کہ پہلا سجدہ ایمان کی وجہ سے ہے اور دوسرا بقائے
ایمان کی وجہ سے۔
اور بعض نے کہا کہ پہلے سجدے سے انسان کی ابتداء پیدائش کی طرف اشارہ ہے اور دوسرے سے اس کی حالت بقاء کی طرف اشارہ ہے جیسا کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول مِنْهَا خَلَقْنَكُمْ وَفِيهَا نُعِيدُ كُمْ وَمِنْهَا نُخْرِجُكُمْ تَارَةً أخری میں اسی طرف اشارہ کیا گیا ہے۔ چھٹا فرض بقدر تشہد قعدہ اخیرہ ہے یعنی اتنی مقدار بیٹھنا فرض ہے جس میں التحیات سے عبدہ ورسولہ تک پڑھنا ممکن ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام احمد امام ابو داؤد اور امام طحاوی نے حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ سے روایت کی ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اخذہ بیدہ
وعلم التشهد بچر آخر حدیث میں ہے اذا قلت هذا او قضيت هذا فقد قضيت صلوتک ان شئت ان تقوم فقم وان تقعد فاقعد، صاحب ہدایہ اسی کے ہم معنی یہ الفاظ نقل کرتے ہیں اذا قلت هذا او فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلو تک تین سے کا پوری کر لے اگر کھڑا ہونا چاہئے تو کھڑا ہو جا اور اگر بیٹھنا چاہے تو بیٹھے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا ہاتھ پکڑ کر ان کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی اور آخر میں فرمایا کہ جب تو نے یہ کہ لیا یا یہ کرلیا تو اپنی نماز
مراد لیے
اس حدیث سے استدلال اس طور پر ہوگا کہ اللہ کے پیارے نبی جانے نماز کے پورا ہونے کو قعود مع قرأت التشهد اور قعود بدون آے
قرأت التشهد پر معلق فرمایا کیونکہ اذا قلت ھذا کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اگر تونے قصور میں تشہد پڑھا۔ اس لئے کہ تشہد کا پڑھنا بغیر قعود کے معتبر نہیں ہے اور او قضيت هذا يا او فعلت هذا کے معنی ہیں کہ یا تو نے نفس قعو کیا یعنی بیٹھا پایا گیا مگر شہید کا پڑھنا نہیں پایا گیا تو تیری تحت نماز پوری ہوگئی۔ حاصل یہ کہ نماز کا پورا ہونا قعود پر موقوف ہے خواہ کچھ پڑھا ہو یا نہ پڑھا ہو۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد پڑھنے کی مقدار بیٹھنا فرض
ہے۔
نیز عبد اللہ بن عمرو بن العاص رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے روایت کرتے ہیں انه قال اذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الاخيرة اولى جائے پھر اس نے حدث کیا تو اس کی نماز پوری ہو گئی۔ قعد قدر التشهدئم احدث فقد تمت صلوته حضور ا نے فرمایا جب وہ آخری سجدے سے اپنا سر اٹھا لے اور تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھ کر ہے۔ (حاشیہ شرح نقایہ از شیخ الادب ) اس حدیث میں بھی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز پورا ہونے کو بقدر تشہد بیٹھنے پرمعلق کیا ہے لہذا اس سے بھی ثابت ہوا کہ بقدر تشہد بیٹھنا فرض ہے۔
Chapter on the description of prayer. He is able to do it. And if he can stand but cannot prostrate, then it is better for him to sit and pray by gesture. The proof for the obligation of standing is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Stand for Allah with devotion' meaning stand for Allah in a state of humility or silence. Qunut means obedience, and according to some it means humility, and according to some it means silence. And it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Umar that qunut means lengthening the standing in prayer. The deduction from the verse is that Allah the Holy commanded standing, and command comes for obligation, and outside of prayer standing is not obligatory by consensus, so it is established that standing in prayer is obligatory (fard). The third fard: recitation. The proof is Allah's saying: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran.' The reasoning is that the command for recitation is in the imperative form and command comes for obligation, and outside of prayer recitation is not obligatory by consensus, so recitation in prayer becomes established as fard. As for how much recitation is fard, detailed discussion will come in the chapter on recitation. The fourth fard is bowing and the fifth is prostration. The proof is Allah's saying: 'And bow and prostrate' meaning perform bowing and prostration. The reasoning is the same as before: the command for bowing and prostration is in the imperative form, and the imperative necessitates obligation. Some people say that in the early time of Islam, some people would prostrate but not bow, and some would bow but not prostrate, so they were commanded to pray with both bowing and prostration. Benefit: The pillars of prayer were legislated separately in the Book of Allah; in one verse the mention of bowing and prostration, in another recitation, in another standing, etc. The author of Sharh al-Niqayah wrote that apparently the second prostration is wajib, i.e., practically fard, because its proof is not from a decisive evidence. And some jurists say that the obligation of the second prostration is established by consensus, such that if either of them is omitted, the prayer becomes invalid. Then he said that repeating prostration in each rak'ah and not repeating bowing is a ta'abbudi matter, i.e., established contrary to analogy. And some said that the first prostration is to fulfill the command of (Allah) and the second is to disgrace and humiliate Iblis because he refused to prostrate out of pride despite Allah's command. And some said the first prostration is for the command and the second is for thankfulness. Some said the first prostration is due to faith and the second due to preservation of faith. And some said that the first prostration indicates the beginning of man's creation and the second indicates his state of preservation, as is indicated in Allah's saying: 'From it We created you, and into it We shall return you, and from it We shall bring you out once again.' The sixth fard is the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud, meaning it is fard to sit for an amount in which recitation from 'al-Tahiyyat' to 'Abduhu wa Rasuluhu' is possible. The proof is that Imam Ahmad, Imam Abu Dawud, and Imam al-Tahawi narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet took his hand and taught him the tashahhud. At the end of the hadith it says: 'When you say this or you do this, then your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, stand; and if you wish to sit, sit.' The author of al-Hidayah transmits similar words: 'When you say this or you do this, then your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, then stand; and if you wish to sit, then sit.' The Prophet held Ibn Mas'ud's hand and taught him tashahhud, and at the end said: 'When you have said this or done this, then you have completed your prayer.' The deduction from this hadith is that the Prophet made the completion of prayer conditional upon sitting with recitation of tashahhud and upon sitting without recitation of tashahhud, because 'when you say this' means if you recited tashahhud in the sitting, for recitation of tashahhud is not valid without sitting, and 'or you do this' means if you performed the sitting itself, i.e., you were found sitting even if you did not recite tashahhud, then your prayer is complete. The conclusion is that the completion of prayer is dependent on sitting, whether one recited something or not. So it is learned that sitting to the extent of reciting tashahhud is fard. Also, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As narrates from the Prophet that he said: 'When he raises his head from the last prostration, then he sits to the extent of tashahhud, then he commits hadath, his prayer is complete.' In this hadith, the Prophet also made the completion of prayer conditional upon sitting to the extent of tashahhud, so it is also established that sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the Urdu commentary Ashraf al-Hidayah, explaining the third through sixth fard acts of prayer. The author begins by noting that if one can stand but cannot prostrate, sitting and gesturing is better—this is a dispensation for those with an excuse. The main discussion then turns to establishing each fard through textual proof. For standing (qiyam), the verse 'Qumu lillahi qanitin' is cited; the principle is that an imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wujub), and since standing outside prayer is not obligatory by consensus, its obligation in prayer is proven. The definition of 'qunut' is discussed, with preferences for obedience, humility, or long standing. For recitation (qira'ah), the verse 'Faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' is used similarly. The author notes that the exact amount required will be detailed later. For bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud), the verse 'Warka'u wa asjudu' is cited, and a historical context is given: some early Muslims did only one of the two, so both were commanded together. The two prostrations per rak'ah are then discussed: though contrary to analogy (qiyas), this is a ta'abbudi (devotional) ruling. There is an ikhtilaf on whether the second sujud is fard or wajib; some say its proof is not qat'i (decisive), while others claim ijma' for its fardiyyah. Various wisdoms are offered: the second sujud humiliates Iblis, is for thankfulness, preserves faith, and alludes to the stages of creation. The sixth fard is the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) to the extent of tashahhud. The proof is from a hadith where the Prophet taught tashahhud and said completion of prayer is conditional on either reciting it or sitting (i.e., the sitting itself). The commentary clarifies that even without recitation, if one sits, the prayer is valid; but to meet the fard, one must sit long enough to recite tashahhud. A second hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr reinforces that sitting after the last prostration to the extent of tashahhud completes the prayer. Thus, the fard acts of prayer are firmly established by Quran and Sunnah, with the second sujud being a matter of some debate but generally accepted as fard.

Key Terms
قیام (qiyam): Standing upright during the prayer, the first fard act.
قرآت (qira'ah): Recitation of Quranic verses during prayer, specifically after al-Fatiha.
امر (amr): The imperative grammatical form, which according to Hanafi usul indicates obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual proof used in this passage to establish that recitation (qira'ah) is a fard act of prayer?
A) The hadith 'Pray as you have seen me pray'
B) The verse 'So recite what is easy from the Quran'
C) The consensus of the Companions
D) Logical reasoning that prayer requires speech

Key Takeaway
The imperative in the Quran is the primary proof for the fard status of qiyam and qira'ah in prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Proof for Ruku' and Sujud, and the Status of the Second Sujud
Proof for ruku' and sujud with ikhtilaf on second sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Quranic proof for ruku' and sujud, and distinguish between the majority view that both sujuds are fard and the minority view that the second is wajib.

Core Idea
Both ruku' and sujud are fard by the imperative, but the second sujud is a point of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

This lesson covers the proof for bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud) from the verse 'Warka'u wa asjudu' (al-Hajj 22:77). The author then discusses the special case of the two prostrations per rak'ah. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about whether the second sujud is fard or wajib. We will examine both positions and the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key verse
The verse 'Warka'u wa asjudu' (al-Hajj 22:77) is cited as proof for both ruku' and sujud.
2
Apply the amr principle
The imperative indicates obligation for both acts. The author mentions a historical context: some early Muslims did only one, so both were commanded together.
3
Analyze the second sujud ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., from Sharh al-Niqayah) say the second sujud is wajib because its proof is not qat'i (decisive). Others claim ijma' for its fardiyyah. The author implies the latter view is stronger.
The practical consequence: omitting the second sujud invalidates the prayer according to the majority.
4
Note the wisdoms for two sujuds
The passage lists several wisdoms: ta'abbudi, humiliation of Iblis, thankfulness, preservation of faith, and allusion to creation and return.

کرنے پر قادر ہو ۔ اور اگر قیام کر سکتا ہے مگر سجدہ نہیں کر سکتا تو اس کے لئے بیٹھ کر اشارہ سے پڑھنا بہتر ہے۔ قیام کے فرض ہونے کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول قُومُوا لِللَّهِ قَانِتِین ہے یعنی کھڑے ہو اللہ تعالے کے واسطے بحالت خضوع یا خاموشی قنوت کے معنی اطاعت کرنا ، اور بعض کے نزدیک خشوع اور بعض کے نزدیک سکوت اور خاموشی۔ اور عبداللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما سے روایت ہے کہ قنوت کے معنی نماز میں طول قیام کے ہیں۔ آیت سے استدلال اس طور ہوگا کہ خداوند قدوس نے قیام کا امر فرمایا ہے اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے اور خارج نماز بالا تفاق قیام واجب نہیں پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ قیام نماز میں واجب (فرض) ہے۔ تیسرا فرض : قرآت ہے دلیل اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول فَاقْرَءُ وُا مَاتَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرانِ ہے۔ وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ قرآت کا حکم بصیغہ امر ہے اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے اور نماز سے باہر بالا جماع قرآت فرض نہیں، پس نماز میں قرآت کا فرض ہونا ثابت ہو گیا رہی یہ بات
کہ کتنی مقدار پڑھنا فرض ہے؟ سو اس بارے میں فصل القرأۃ میں مفصل کلام کیا جائے گا۔
چوتھا فرض رکوع اور پانچواں بجود ہے دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول واركعوا واسجدوا ہے یعنی رکوع کرو اور سجدہ کرو۔ وجہ استدلال و ہی ہے جو سابق میں گذر چکی کہ رکوع اور سجود کا حکم بصیغہ امر ہے اور امر کا موجب وجوب ہے بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ اسلام کے شروع زمانے میں کچھ لوگ سجدہ کرتے تھے مگر رکوع نہیں کرتے تھے اور کچھ رکوع کرتے تھے مگر سجدہ نہیں کرتے تھے پس ان کو حکم کیا گیا کہ رکوع اور سجدہ کے ساتھ نماز پڑھو۔ فائدہ نماز کے ارکان کتاب اللہ میں متفرق کر کے مشروع کئے گئے ہیں چنانچہ کسی آیت میں رکوع اور سجود کا بیان ہے اور کسی میں قرآت کا اور کسی میں قیام کا وغیرہ۔ صاحب شرح نقایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ دوسر اسجدہ واجب یعنی فرض عملی ہے کیونکہ اس کا ثبوت دلیل قطعی سے نہیں ہوا۔ اور بعض فقہاء کا قول ہے کہ دوسرے جدہ کی فرضیت بالا جماع ثابت ہے حتی کہ اگر ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کو ترک کر دیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ پھر فرمایا کہ ہر رکعت میں تکرار سجود نہ کہ تکرار رکوع امر تعبدی ہے یعنی خلاف قیاس ثابت ہے۔ اور بعض نے کہا کہ پہلا سجدہ (آقا) کے حکم کی تعمیل کے لئے ہے اور دوسرا ابلیس کو رسوا اور ذلیل کرنے کے لئے ہے کیونکہ اس نے اللہ کے حکم کے باوجود از راہ تکبر سجدہ نہیں کیا تھا۔ اور بعض کا قول یہ ہے کہ پہلا سجدہ للامر اور دوسرا لشکر ہے۔ بعض نے کہا کہ پہلا سجدہ ایمان کی وجہ سے ہے اور دوسرا بقائے
ایمان کی وجہ سے۔
اور بعض نے کہا کہ پہلے سجدے سے انسان کی ابتداء پیدائش کی طرف اشارہ ہے اور دوسرے سے اس کی حالت بقاء کی طرف اشارہ ہے جیسا کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول مِنْهَا خَلَقْنَكُمْ وَفِيهَا نُعِيدُ كُمْ وَمِنْهَا نُخْرِجُكُمْ تَارَةً أخری میں اسی طرف اشارہ کیا گیا ہے۔ چھٹا فرض بقدر تشہد قعدہ اخیرہ ہے یعنی اتنی مقدار بیٹھنا فرض ہے جس میں التحیات سے عبدہ ورسولہ تک پڑھنا ممکن ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام احمد امام ابو داؤد اور امام طحاوی نے حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ سے روایت کی ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اخذہ بیدہ
وعلم التشهد بچر آخر حدیث میں ہے اذا قلت هذا او قضيت هذا فقد قضيت صلوتک ان شئت ان تقوم فقم وان تقعد فاقعد، صاحب ہدایہ اسی کے ہم معنی یہ الفاظ نقل کرتے ہیں اذا قلت هذا او فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلو تک تین سے کا پوری کر لے اگر کھڑا ہونا چاہئے تو کھڑا ہو جا اور اگر بیٹھنا چاہے تو بیٹھے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا ہاتھ پکڑ کر ان کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی اور آخر میں فرمایا کہ جب تو نے یہ کہ لیا یا یہ کرلیا تو اپنی نماز
مراد لیے
اس حدیث سے استدلال اس طور پر ہوگا کہ اللہ کے پیارے نبی جانے نماز کے پورا ہونے کو قعود مع قرأت التشهد اور قعود بدون آے
قرأت التشهد پر معلق فرمایا کیونکہ اذا قلت ھذا کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اگر تونے قصور میں تشہد پڑھا۔ اس لئے کہ تشہد کا پڑھنا بغیر قعود کے معتبر نہیں ہے اور او قضيت هذا يا او فعلت هذا کے معنی ہیں کہ یا تو نے نفس قعو کیا یعنی بیٹھا پایا گیا مگر شہید کا پڑھنا نہیں پایا گیا تو تیری تحت نماز پوری ہوگئی۔ حاصل یہ کہ نماز کا پورا ہونا قعود پر موقوف ہے خواہ کچھ پڑھا ہو یا نہ پڑھا ہو۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد پڑھنے کی مقدار بیٹھنا فرض
ہے۔
نیز عبد اللہ بن عمرو بن العاص رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے روایت کرتے ہیں انه قال اذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الاخيرة اولى جائے پھر اس نے حدث کیا تو اس کی نماز پوری ہو گئی۔ قعد قدر التشهدئم احدث فقد تمت صلوته حضور ا نے فرمایا جب وہ آخری سجدے سے اپنا سر اٹھا لے اور تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھ کر ہے۔ (حاشیہ شرح نقایہ از شیخ الادب ) اس حدیث میں بھی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز پورا ہونے کو بقدر تشہد بیٹھنے پرمعلق کیا ہے لہذا اس سے بھی ثابت ہوا کہ بقدر تشہد بیٹھنا فرض ہے۔
Chapter on the description of prayer. He is able to do it. And if he can stand but cannot prostrate, then it is better for him to sit and pray by gesture. The proof for the obligation of standing is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Stand for Allah with devotion' meaning stand for Allah in a state of humility or silence. Qunut means obedience, and according to some it means humility, and according to some it means silence. And it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Umar that qunut means lengthening the standing in prayer. The deduction from the verse is that Allah the Holy commanded standing, and command comes for obligation, and outside of prayer standing is not obligatory by consensus, so it is established that standing in prayer is obligatory (fard). The third fard: recitation. The proof is Allah's saying: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran.' The reasoning is that the command for recitation is in the imperative form and command comes for obligation, and outside of prayer recitation is not obligatory by consensus, so recitation in prayer becomes established as fard. As for how much recitation is fard, detailed discussion will come in the chapter on recitation. The fourth fard is bowing and the fifth is prostration. The proof is Allah's saying: 'And bow and prostrate' meaning perform bowing and prostration. The reasoning is the same as before: the command for bowing and prostration is in the imperative form, and the imperative necessitates obligation. Some people say that in the early time of Islam, some people would prostrate but not bow, and some would bow but not prostrate, so they were commanded to pray with both bowing and prostration. Benefit: The pillars of prayer were legislated separately in the Book of Allah; in one verse the mention of bowing and prostration, in another recitation, in another standing, etc. The author of Sharh al-Niqayah wrote that apparently the second prostration is wajib, i.e., practically fard, because its proof is not from a decisive evidence. And some jurists say that the obligation of the second prostration is established by consensus, such that if either of them is omitted, the prayer becomes invalid. Then he said that repeating prostration in each rak'ah and not repeating bowing is a ta'abbudi matter, i.e., established contrary to analogy. And some said that the first prostration is to fulfill the command of (Allah) and the second is to disgrace and humiliate Iblis because he refused to prostrate out of pride despite Allah's command. And some said the first prostration is for the command and the second is for thankfulness. Some said the first prostration is due to faith and the second due to preservation of faith. And some said that the first prostration indicates the beginning of man's creation and the second indicates his state of preservation, as is indicated in Allah's saying: 'From it We created you, and into it We shall return you, and from it We shall bring you out once again.' The sixth fard is the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud, meaning it is fard to sit for an amount in which recitation from 'al-Tahiyyat' to 'Abduhu wa Rasuluhu' is possible. The proof is that Imam Ahmad, Imam Abu Dawud, and Imam al-Tahawi narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet took his hand and taught him the tashahhud. At the end of the hadith it says: 'When you say this or you do this, then your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, stand; and if you wish to sit, sit.' The author of al-Hidayah transmits similar words: 'When you say this or you do this, then your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, then stand; and if you wish to sit, then sit.' The Prophet held Ibn Mas'ud's hand and taught him tashahhud, and at the end said: 'When you have said this or done this, then you have completed your prayer.' The deduction from this hadith is that the Prophet made the completion of prayer conditional upon sitting with recitation of tashahhud and upon sitting without recitation of tashahhud, because 'when you say this' means if you recited tashahhud in the sitting, for recitation of tashahhud is not valid without sitting, and 'or you do this' means if you performed the sitting itself, i.e., you were found sitting even if you did not recite tashahhud, then your prayer is complete. The conclusion is that the completion of prayer is dependent on sitting, whether one recited something or not. So it is learned that sitting to the extent of reciting tashahhud is fard. Also, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As narrates from the Prophet that he said: 'When he raises his head from the last prostration, then he sits to the extent of tashahhud, then he commits hadath, his prayer is complete.' In this hadith, the Prophet also made the completion of prayer conditional upon sitting to the extent of tashahhud, so it is also established that sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the Urdu commentary Ashraf al-Hidayah, explaining the third through sixth fard acts of prayer. The author begins by noting that if one can stand but cannot prostrate, sitting and gesturing is better—this is a dispensation for those with an excuse. The main discussion then turns to establishing each fard through textual proof. For standing (qiyam), the verse 'Qumu lillahi qanitin' is cited; the principle is that an imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wujub), and since standing outside prayer is not obligatory by consensus, its obligation in prayer is proven. The definition of 'qunut' is discussed, with preferences for obedience, humility, or long standing. For recitation (qira'ah), the verse 'Faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' is used similarly. The author notes that the exact amount required will be detailed later. For bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud), the verse 'Warka'u wa asjudu' is cited, and a historical context is given: some early Muslims did only one of the two, so both were commanded together. The two prostrations per rak'ah are then discussed: though contrary to analogy (qiyas), this is a ta'abbudi (devotional) ruling. There is an ikhtilaf on whether the second sujud is fard or wajib; some say its proof is not qat'i (decisive), while others claim ijma' for its fardiyyah. Various wisdoms are offered: the second sujud humiliates Iblis, is for thankfulness, preserves faith, and alludes to the stages of creation. The sixth fard is the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) to the extent of tashahhud. The proof is from a hadith where the Prophet taught tashahhud and said completion of prayer is conditional on either reciting it or sitting (i.e., the sitting itself). The commentary clarifies that even without recitation, if one sits, the prayer is valid; but to meet the fard, one must sit long enough to recite tashahhud. A second hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr reinforces that sitting after the last prostration to the extent of tashahhud completes the prayer. Thus, the fard acts of prayer are firmly established by Quran and Sunnah, with the second sujud being a matter of some debate but generally accepted as fard.

Key Terms
رکوع (ruku'): Bowing from the waist, a fard act of prayer.
سجود (sujud): Prostration, two per rak'ah, a fard act.
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of scholars; here used by some to prove fardiyyah of second sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main point of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding sujud?
A) Whether ruku' is fard or sunnah
B) Whether the first sujud is fard or wajib
C) Whether the second sujud is fard or wajib
D) Whether sujud requires touching the ground

Key Takeaway
The second sujud per rak'ah is a point of ikhtilaf, but the majority Hanafi view treats it as fard.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Proof for the Final Sitting (Qa'dah Akhirah) as Fard
Proof for qa'dah akhirah using hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith evidence for the obligation of the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud and explain how the hadith makes the completion of prayer conditional on sitting.

Core Idea
The final sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard because the Prophet made prayer complete only upon sitting.

The sixth fard act of prayer is the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) for at least the duration of reciting the tashahhud. The proof comes from prophetic hadiths, one from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and another from Abdullah ibn Amr. These hadiths state that if one sits to that extent, the prayer is complete even if one doesn't recite tashahhud. This establishes the obligation of the sitting itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first hadith (Ibn Mas'ud)
The Prophet taught tashahhud and said: 'When you say this or you do this, your prayer is complete.' 'Say this' refers to reciting tashahhud while sitting; 'do this' refers to the sitting itself.
The hadith is transmitted by Imam Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tahawi.
2
Understand the inference
The Prophet made completion of prayer conditional on either reciting tashahhud while sitting or simply sitting without recitation. This shows sitting is the essential element.
3
Identify the second hadith (Ibn 'Amr)
The Prophet said: 'When he raises his head from the last prostration, then sits to the extent of tashahhud, then performs hadath, his prayer is complete.'
4
Apply the principle
Both hadiths make the completion of prayer conditional on sitting to the extent of tashahhud. This indicates sitting is fard.
The amount is the time to recite from 'al-Tahiyyat' to 'Abduhu wa Rasuluhu'.

کرنے پر قادر ہو ۔ اور اگر قیام کر سکتا ہے مگر سجدہ نہیں کر سکتا تو اس کے لئے بیٹھ کر اشارہ سے پڑھنا بہتر ہے۔ قیام کے فرض ہونے کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول قُومُوا لِللَّهِ قَانِتِین ہے یعنی کھڑے ہو اللہ تعالے کے واسطے بحالت خضوع یا خاموشی قنوت کے معنی اطاعت کرنا ، اور بعض کے نزدیک خشوع اور بعض کے نزدیک سکوت اور خاموشی۔ اور عبداللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہما سے روایت ہے کہ قنوت کے معنی نماز میں طول قیام کے ہیں۔ آیت سے استدلال اس طور ہوگا کہ خداوند قدوس نے قیام کا امر فرمایا ہے اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے اور خارج نماز بالا تفاق قیام واجب نہیں پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ قیام نماز میں واجب (فرض) ہے۔ تیسرا فرض : قرآت ہے دلیل اللہ تعالیٰ کا قول فَاقْرَءُ وُا مَاتَيَسَّرَ مِنَ الْقُرانِ ہے۔ وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ قرآت کا حکم بصیغہ امر ہے اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے اور نماز سے باہر بالا جماع قرآت فرض نہیں، پس نماز میں قرآت کا فرض ہونا ثابت ہو گیا رہی یہ بات
کہ کتنی مقدار پڑھنا فرض ہے؟ سو اس بارے میں فصل القرأۃ میں مفصل کلام کیا جائے گا۔
چوتھا فرض رکوع اور پانچواں بجود ہے دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول واركعوا واسجدوا ہے یعنی رکوع کرو اور سجدہ کرو۔ وجہ استدلال و ہی ہے جو سابق میں گذر چکی کہ رکوع اور سجود کا حکم بصیغہ امر ہے اور امر کا موجب وجوب ہے بعض حضرات کا کہنا ہے کہ اسلام کے شروع زمانے میں کچھ لوگ سجدہ کرتے تھے مگر رکوع نہیں کرتے تھے اور کچھ رکوع کرتے تھے مگر سجدہ نہیں کرتے تھے پس ان کو حکم کیا گیا کہ رکوع اور سجدہ کے ساتھ نماز پڑھو۔ فائدہ نماز کے ارکان کتاب اللہ میں متفرق کر کے مشروع کئے گئے ہیں چنانچہ کسی آیت میں رکوع اور سجود کا بیان ہے اور کسی میں قرآت کا اور کسی میں قیام کا وغیرہ۔ صاحب شرح نقایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ دوسر اسجدہ واجب یعنی فرض عملی ہے کیونکہ اس کا ثبوت دلیل قطعی سے نہیں ہوا۔ اور بعض فقہاء کا قول ہے کہ دوسرے جدہ کی فرضیت بالا جماع ثابت ہے حتی کہ اگر ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کو ترک کر دیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ پھر فرمایا کہ ہر رکعت میں تکرار سجود نہ کہ تکرار رکوع امر تعبدی ہے یعنی خلاف قیاس ثابت ہے۔ اور بعض نے کہا کہ پہلا سجدہ (آقا) کے حکم کی تعمیل کے لئے ہے اور دوسرا ابلیس کو رسوا اور ذلیل کرنے کے لئے ہے کیونکہ اس نے اللہ کے حکم کے باوجود از راہ تکبر سجدہ نہیں کیا تھا۔ اور بعض کا قول یہ ہے کہ پہلا سجدہ للامر اور دوسرا لشکر ہے۔ بعض نے کہا کہ پہلا سجدہ ایمان کی وجہ سے ہے اور دوسرا بقائے
ایمان کی وجہ سے۔
اور بعض نے کہا کہ پہلے سجدے سے انسان کی ابتداء پیدائش کی طرف اشارہ ہے اور دوسرے سے اس کی حالت بقاء کی طرف اشارہ ہے جیسا کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول مِنْهَا خَلَقْنَكُمْ وَفِيهَا نُعِيدُ كُمْ وَمِنْهَا نُخْرِجُكُمْ تَارَةً أخری میں اسی طرف اشارہ کیا گیا ہے۔ چھٹا فرض بقدر تشہد قعدہ اخیرہ ہے یعنی اتنی مقدار بیٹھنا فرض ہے جس میں التحیات سے عبدہ ورسولہ تک پڑھنا ممکن ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ امام احمد امام ابو داؤد اور امام طحاوی نے حضرت عبد اللہ بن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ سے روایت کی ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اخذہ بیدہ
وعلم التشهد بچر آخر حدیث میں ہے اذا قلت هذا او قضيت هذا فقد قضيت صلوتک ان شئت ان تقوم فقم وان تقعد فاقعد، صاحب ہدایہ اسی کے ہم معنی یہ الفاظ نقل کرتے ہیں اذا قلت هذا او فعلت هذا فقد تمت صلو تک تین سے کا پوری کر لے اگر کھڑا ہونا چاہئے تو کھڑا ہو جا اور اگر بیٹھنا چاہے تو بیٹھے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ابن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ کا ہاتھ پکڑ کر ان کو تشہد کی تعلیم دی اور آخر میں فرمایا کہ جب تو نے یہ کہ لیا یا یہ کرلیا تو اپنی نماز
مراد لیے
اس حدیث سے استدلال اس طور پر ہوگا کہ اللہ کے پیارے نبی جانے نماز کے پورا ہونے کو قعود مع قرأت التشهد اور قعود بدون آے
قرأت التشهد پر معلق فرمایا کیونکہ اذا قلت ھذا کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اگر تونے قصور میں تشہد پڑھا۔ اس لئے کہ تشہد کا پڑھنا بغیر قعود کے معتبر نہیں ہے اور او قضيت هذا يا او فعلت هذا کے معنی ہیں کہ یا تو نے نفس قعو کیا یعنی بیٹھا پایا گیا مگر شہید کا پڑھنا نہیں پایا گیا تو تیری تحت نماز پوری ہوگئی۔ حاصل یہ کہ نماز کا پورا ہونا قعود پر موقوف ہے خواہ کچھ پڑھا ہو یا نہ پڑھا ہو۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ تشہد پڑھنے کی مقدار بیٹھنا فرض
ہے۔
نیز عبد اللہ بن عمرو بن العاص رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے روایت کرتے ہیں انه قال اذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الاخيرة اولى جائے پھر اس نے حدث کیا تو اس کی نماز پوری ہو گئی۔ قعد قدر التشهدئم احدث فقد تمت صلوته حضور ا نے فرمایا جب وہ آخری سجدے سے اپنا سر اٹھا لے اور تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھ کر ہے۔ (حاشیہ شرح نقایہ از شیخ الادب ) اس حدیث میں بھی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نماز پورا ہونے کو بقدر تشہد بیٹھنے پرمعلق کیا ہے لہذا اس سے بھی ثابت ہوا کہ بقدر تشہد بیٹھنا فرض ہے۔
Chapter on the description of prayer. He is able to do it. And if he can stand but cannot prostrate, then it is better for him to sit and pray by gesture. The proof for the obligation of standing is the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Stand for Allah with devotion' meaning stand for Allah in a state of humility or silence. Qunut means obedience, and according to some it means humility, and according to some it means silence. And it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Umar that qunut means lengthening the standing in prayer. The deduction from the verse is that Allah the Holy commanded standing, and command comes for obligation, and outside of prayer standing is not obligatory by consensus, so it is established that standing in prayer is obligatory (fard). The third fard: recitation. The proof is Allah's saying: 'So recite what is easy from the Quran.' The reasoning is that the command for recitation is in the imperative form and command comes for obligation, and outside of prayer recitation is not obligatory by consensus, so recitation in prayer becomes established as fard. As for how much recitation is fard, detailed discussion will come in the chapter on recitation. The fourth fard is bowing and the fifth is prostration. The proof is Allah's saying: 'And bow and prostrate' meaning perform bowing and prostration. The reasoning is the same as before: the command for bowing and prostration is in the imperative form, and the imperative necessitates obligation. Some people say that in the early time of Islam, some people would prostrate but not bow, and some would bow but not prostrate, so they were commanded to pray with both bowing and prostration. Benefit: The pillars of prayer were legislated separately in the Book of Allah; in one verse the mention of bowing and prostration, in another recitation, in another standing, etc. The author of Sharh al-Niqayah wrote that apparently the second prostration is wajib, i.e., practically fard, because its proof is not from a decisive evidence. And some jurists say that the obligation of the second prostration is established by consensus, such that if either of them is omitted, the prayer becomes invalid. Then he said that repeating prostration in each rak'ah and not repeating bowing is a ta'abbudi matter, i.e., established contrary to analogy. And some said that the first prostration is to fulfill the command of (Allah) and the second is to disgrace and humiliate Iblis because he refused to prostrate out of pride despite Allah's command. And some said the first prostration is for the command and the second is for thankfulness. Some said the first prostration is due to faith and the second due to preservation of faith. And some said that the first prostration indicates the beginning of man's creation and the second indicates his state of preservation, as is indicated in Allah's saying: 'From it We created you, and into it We shall return you, and from it We shall bring you out once again.' The sixth fard is the final sitting to the extent of tashahhud, meaning it is fard to sit for an amount in which recitation from 'al-Tahiyyat' to 'Abduhu wa Rasuluhu' is possible. The proof is that Imam Ahmad, Imam Abu Dawud, and Imam al-Tahawi narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet took his hand and taught him the tashahhud. At the end of the hadith it says: 'When you say this or you do this, then your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, stand; and if you wish to sit, sit.' The author of al-Hidayah transmits similar words: 'When you say this or you do this, then your prayer is complete. If you wish to stand, then stand; and if you wish to sit, then sit.' The Prophet held Ibn Mas'ud's hand and taught him tashahhud, and at the end said: 'When you have said this or done this, then you have completed your prayer.' The deduction from this hadith is that the Prophet made the completion of prayer conditional upon sitting with recitation of tashahhud and upon sitting without recitation of tashahhud, because 'when you say this' means if you recited tashahhud in the sitting, for recitation of tashahhud is not valid without sitting, and 'or you do this' means if you performed the sitting itself, i.e., you were found sitting even if you did not recite tashahhud, then your prayer is complete. The conclusion is that the completion of prayer is dependent on sitting, whether one recited something or not. So it is learned that sitting to the extent of reciting tashahhud is fard. Also, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As narrates from the Prophet that he said: 'When he raises his head from the last prostration, then he sits to the extent of tashahhud, then he commits hadath, his prayer is complete.' In this hadith, the Prophet also made the completion of prayer conditional upon sitting to the extent of tashahhud, so it is also established that sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the Urdu commentary Ashraf al-Hidayah, explaining the third through sixth fard acts of prayer. The author begins by noting that if one can stand but cannot prostrate, sitting and gesturing is better—this is a dispensation for those with an excuse. The main discussion then turns to establishing each fard through textual proof. For standing (qiyam), the verse 'Qumu lillahi qanitin' is cited; the principle is that an imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wujub), and since standing outside prayer is not obligatory by consensus, its obligation in prayer is proven. The definition of 'qunut' is discussed, with preferences for obedience, humility, or long standing. For recitation (qira'ah), the verse 'Faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' is used similarly. The author notes that the exact amount required will be detailed later. For bowing (ruku') and prostration (sujud), the verse 'Warka'u wa asjudu' is cited, and a historical context is given: some early Muslims did only one of the two, so both were commanded together. The two prostrations per rak'ah are then discussed: though contrary to analogy (qiyas), this is a ta'abbudi (devotional) ruling. There is an ikhtilaf on whether the second sujud is fard or wajib; some say its proof is not qat'i (decisive), while others claim ijma' for its fardiyyah. Various wisdoms are offered: the second sujud humiliates Iblis, is for thankfulness, preserves faith, and alludes to the stages of creation. The sixth fard is the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) to the extent of tashahhud. The proof is from a hadith where the Prophet taught tashahhud and said completion of prayer is conditional on either reciting it or sitting (i.e., the sitting itself). The commentary clarifies that even without recitation, if one sits, the prayer is valid; but to meet the fard, one must sit long enough to recite tashahhud. A second hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr reinforces that sitting after the last prostration to the extent of tashahhud completes the prayer. Thus, the fard acts of prayer are firmly established by Quran and Sunnah, with the second sujud being a matter of some debate but generally accepted as fard.

Key Terms
قعدہ اخیرہ (qa'dah akhirah): The final sitting after the last prostration, to the extent of reciting tashahhud.
تشہد (tashahhud): A supplication recited in the sitting, beginning with 'al-Tahiyyat' and ending with 'Abduhu wa Rasuluhu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key inference from the hadith 'When you say this or you do this, your prayer is complete'?
A) Recitation of tashahhud is fard, sitting is sunnah
B) Sitting alone (without recitation) is sufficient to complete prayer
C) Both recitation and sitting are fard
D) The prayer is incomplete without salaam

Key Takeaway
The final sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard, established by hadith making prayer complete upon sitting.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Wajibat of Prayer: Correcting al-Quduri's Terminology
Correction of a terminological inaccuracy by al-Hidayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi wajibat of prayer, distinguish them from sunnah, and state the ruling and compensation for their omission.

Core Idea
Not everything called 'sunnah' is optional—many prayer acts are wajib, their omission requiring prostration of forgetfulness.

In his matn, al-Quduri classified all prayer acts beyond the fard as 'sunnah'. However, al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah corrects this: several of those acts are actually wajib (obligatory). The distinction is crucial because omitting a sunnah requires no compensation, whereas omitting a wajib—whether forgetfully or intentionally—demands a specific remedy. This lesson unpacks that correction, lists the wajibat, and explains the proof and consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terminological correction
Recognize that al-Quduri's blanket term 'sunnah' is too broad. Al-Hidayah specifies that a subset of acts are wajib.
The term 'sunnah' is used loosely in the book because the obligation of these acts is established by the Sunnah itself.
2
List the acts the Hanafi school classifies as wajib
From the passage: reciting al-Fatiha, adding a surah, maintaining order in repeated acts, first sitting (qa'dah ula), reciting tashahhud in the final sitting, qunut in witr, takbirs of Eid, and raising/lowering the voice as required.
These are not exhaustive; additional wajibat exist in prayer but this list is from the text.
3
Understand the proof (dalil) for wajib status
These acts are proven by ahad hadith (the Sunnah as a source of proof, not mutawatir). In Hanafi usul, dalil zanni al-thubut yields hukm wajib, not fard.
For example, the hadith 'La salata liman lam yaqra' bi-Fatihah' is ahad, making reciting al-Fatiha wajib.
4
Analyze the consequence of omission
Forgetful omission requires sajdat al-sahw (two extra prostrations). Intentional omission invalidates the prayer entirely.
This is because wajib, though less than fard, is still obligatory.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school considers reciting al-Fatiha as fard (rukn). The Hanafi view is wajib, meaning it can be compensated if forgotten.
This difference stems from varying assessments of the proof's strength.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وما سوى ذلك فهو سنة، اطلق اسم السنة وفيها واجبات كقراءة الفاتحة وضم السورة معها ومراعات الترتيب فيما شرع مكررا من الافعال والعقدة الأولى وقراءة التشهد في الاخيرة والقنوت في الوتر وتكبيرات العيدين والجهر فيما جهر والمخافتة فيما تخافت فيه ولهذا يجب عليه سجدتا السهو بتركها هذا هو الصحيح وتسميتها سنة في الكتاب لما انه ثبت وجوبها بالسنة
ترجمہ فرمایا کہ اور جو افعال ان کے علاوہ ہیں ، وہ سنت ہیں قدوری نے سنت کا اطلاق کیا حالانکہ ان افعال میں واجبات بھی ہیں جیسے سورۂ فاتحہ پڑھنا اور اس کے ساتھ کسی سورت کا ملانا۔ اور ان افعال میں ترتیب کی رعایت رکھنا جو کر ر مشروع ہوئے ہیں اور پہلا قعدہ اور قعدہ اخیرہ میں تشہد پڑھنا اور وتر میں قنوت پڑھنا اور عیدین کی تکبیر میں اور جن میں جبر واجب ہے ان میں ہر کرنا اور جن میں اختفاء واجب ہے ان میں اختفاء کرنا اور اسی واسطے مصلی پر ان میں سے ہر ایک کے ترک سے سہو کے دو سجدے واجب ہوتے ہیں یہی بیج ہے اور کتاب میں ان کا سنت نام رکھنا اس لئے ہے کہ ان کا وجوب سنت سے ثابت ہے۔ تشریح شیخ قدوری نے کہا کہ مذکورہ چیزوں یعنی فرائض کے علاوہ سب سنت ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ قدوری نے لفظ سنت استعمال کیا ہے حالانکہ ان افعال میں واجبات بھی ہیں لہذا یہاں لفظ سنت کا اطلاق صحیح نہیں ہوگا۔
He said: 'And whatever is besides that is sunnah.' He used the term sunnah, but among these acts are wajibat, such as reciting al-Fatiha and adding a surah with it, maintaining order in what is legislated repeatedly from the actions, the first sitting, reciting tashahhud in the final sitting, reciting qunut in witr, the takbirs of the two Eids, raising the voice where it is to be raised, and lowering it where it is to be lowered. For this reason, prostrations of forgetfulness are obligatory upon the one praying due to omitting any of these. This is the correct view. They are called sunnah in the book because their obligation is established by the Sunnah. Translation: He said that the acts besides these are sunnah. al-Quduri applied the term sunnah, although among these acts there are wajibat, such as reciting Surah al-Fatiha and adding a surah with it, maintaining order in the acts that are legislated repeatedly, the first sitting, reciting tashahhud in the final sitting, reciting qunut in witr, the takbirs of the two Eids, raising the voice where it is wajib, and lowering the voice where it is wajib. For this reason, upon omitting any of these, two prostrations of forgetfulness become obligatory for the one praying. This is the correct (view). And their being called sunnah in the book is because their obligation is established by the Sunnah. Explanation: Sheikh al-Quduri said that everything mentioned besides the fara'id is sunnah. The author of al-Hidayah said that al-Quduri used the word 'sunnah' although among these acts there are wajibat, therefore the use of the term sunnah here is not correct.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from the commentary on al-Hidayah, addressing a terminological issue. Al-Quduri, in his matn, stated that all acts of prayer besides the fard are 'sunnah.' The author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) corrects this: many of those acts are actually wajib (obligatory), not mere sunnah. The distinction is crucial: omitting a sunnah does not require compensation, but omitting a wajib necessitates sajdat al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The passage lists examples of these wajibat: reciting Surah al-Fatiha, adding another surah after it, maintaining order in repeated acts (like bowing and prostration), the first sitting (qa'dah ula), reciting tashahhud in the final sitting, qunut in witr, takbirs of Eid prayer, and reciting aloud or quietly where required. Each of these is obligatory (wajib) because their proof comes from the Sunnah (ahad hadith), not from the Quran or mutawatir. If one omits any of them intentionally, sajdat al-sahw is not sufficient; the prayer becomes invalid. But if omitted forgetfully, sajdat al-sahw repairs it. The author clarifies that calling them 'sunnah' is a misnomer in this context; it was only done because the source of their obligation is the Sunnah (the practice of the Prophet). This highlights the Hanafi hierarchy: fard from qat'i dalil, wajib from zanni dalil (like ahad hadith), and sunnah from the Prophet's consistent practice without obligation.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act in prayer whose proof comes from a zanni source (ahad hadith); omission requires sajdat al-sahw if done forgetfully, but intentional omission invalidates the prayer.
سنت (sunnah): In this passage, a term used by al-Quduri for all non-fard acts, but corrected by al-Hidayah to refer only to those that are not wajib. The author notes the term is used loosely because the proof is from the Sunnah.
سجدہ سہو (sajdat al-sahw): Two extra prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for the unintentional omission of a wajib act.
فاتحہ (al-Fatiha): The opening chapter of the Quran, whose recitation in prayer is wajib per Hanafi (not fard as in Shafi'i).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the consequence of forgetfully omitting a wajib act like reciting al-Fatiha in prayer?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated
B) Two prostrations of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) are required to rectify it
C) No compensation is needed; the prayer remains valid
D) The prayer is valid but one must give charity

Key Takeaway
Acts of prayer proven by ahad hadith are wajib, not optional sunnah, and their forgetful omission is remedied by sajdat al-sahw.

Sitting for Tashahhud is Fard: Proof from Hadith
Proves fardiyyah of sitting for qadr al-tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that sitting for the amount of tashahhud in the last rak'ah is fard and derive this ruling from the two hadith presented in Al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
Sitting for tashahhud is fard, not just wajib — omission invalidates the prayer.

This lesson examines two authenticated hadith that the Hanafi school uses to establish that the last sitting (qu'ud) in prayer is a fundamental pillar (fard/rukn). The first from Ibn Mas'ud and the second from Abdullah ibn Amr clearly link the completion of prayer to the act of sitting, whether or not one recites the tashahhud. Understanding this distinction is critical because it determines whether a missed sitting can be compensated by prostrations of forgetfulness or requires a full repetition of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what legal category it falls under.
The act is sitting (qu'ud) in the last rak'ah for the duration of tashahhud. The ruling: fard (rukn).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited by the author. Here, two hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and Abdullah ibn Amr.
Both hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but their meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith text proves the ruling. The phrase 'when you say this or you have done this' indicates that prayer completion depends on sitting.
The alternate wording 'or you have done this' covers sitting even without recitation, proving the obligation is sitting itself.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify which school disagrees and on what basis.
Shafi'is consider it wajib (not fard) and allow compensation with sajdat al-sahw.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Confirm the relied-upon position for fatwa and why it prevails.
The mufta bihi is that sitting for tashahhud is fard, based on the explicit linking of prayer completion to sitting in both hadith.
