And the teaching of tashahhud is at the end of the hadith: 'When you say this or you have done this, you have completed your prayer. If you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit.' The author of Hidayah quotes similar words: 'When you say this or do this, your prayer is complete.' ... The Prophet (s) held the hand of Ibn Mas'ud (r) and taught him tashahhud, and at the end said: 'When you have said this or done this, your prayer is complete.' The inference from this hadith is that the Prophet linked the completion of prayer to sitting with recitation of tashahhud and to sitting without recitation of tashahhud, because 'when you say this' means if you recited tashahhud while sitting (since recitation of tashahhud is not valid without sitting), and 'or you have done this' means if you performed the act of sitting (i.e., you were found sitting) even without reciting tashahhud, then your prayer is complete. The conclusion is that the completion of prayer depends on sitting, whether one recited something or not. Thus it is established that sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard. Also, Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As (r) narrates from the Prophet (s) that he said: 'When he raises his head from the last prostration and then he passes wind, his prayer is complete; if he sits to the extent of tashahhud and then passes wind, his prayer is complete.' The Prophet linked completion of prayer to sitting to the extent of tashahhud. Hence it is also established that sitting to the extent of tashahhud is fard.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing that sitting (jalsah) for the duration of tashahhud in the last rak'ah of prayer is fard (obligatory). The author presents two hadith proofs. The first is the well-known hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet (s) taught him tashahhud and said that completing the prayer is contingent upon either saying the tashahhud or performing the sitting itself. The commentator explains that the phrase 'when you say this' implies reciting tashahhud while sitting (since recitation without sitting is invalid), and 'or you have done this' means the act of sitting even without recitation. Thus both options indicate that the prayer is complete only after sitting, proving that sitting is fard. The second hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr clarifies that even if something nullifies wudu (like passing wind) after sitting for the duration of tashahhud, the prayer is still complete. This further supports that the obligation is the sitting itself, not the recitation. This ruling is relied upon in the Hanafi madhhab and is from the Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad). Note that the first qa'dah in the second rak'ah is wajib, not fard, and its omission requires sajdat al-sahw, whereas this last sitting is fard and its omission invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms
قعود (qu'ud): Sitting posture in prayer, specifically the sitting after the last prostration (jalsah) in the final rak'ah.
تشہد (tashahhud): The specific supplication recited while sitting in prayer, commencing with 'At-tahiyyat lillah...'
فرض (fard): An integral (rukn) of prayer whose omission invalidates the prayer and requires repetition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the consequence of omitting the last sitting (qu'ud) in prayer?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is still valid if sajdat al-sahw is performed.
C) The prayer becomes makruh but remains valid.
D) The prayer is valid, but the person must repeat just the sitting.

Key Takeaway
Sitting for the duration of tashahhud in the last rak'ah is a fard pillar of prayer; its omission invalidates the prayer regardless of recitation.

Wajibat of Prayer: Terminology and List
Explains why Quduri called them sunan and lists the wajibat with definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the wajibat of prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain why the term 'sunnah' can be applied to them without contradiction.

Core Idea
What Quduri called 'sunnah' includes wajibat – actions whose omission requires sajdat al-sahw.

In this passage, al-Marghinani (Sahib al-Hidayah) clarifies a potential terminological confusion in Quduri's matn. Quduri stated that all acts other than the explicit fara'id are 'sunnah', but this includes several wajibat. The commentator resolves this by explaining that 'sunnah' here means 'established by the sunnah', so both sunnan and wajibat are included literally. Understanding this distinction is key to mastering the Hanafi hierarchy of obligations in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base claim
Quduri states that everything besides the fara'id is 'sunnah'. Recognize that this is a general categorization.
The base text is Quduri's matn.
2
Spot the problem
Sahib al-Hidayah objects that among those 'sunnah' acts, some are actually wajib (obligatory). List them from the text.
Wajib acts require sajdat al-sahw if omitted forgetfully.
3
List the wajibat
From the passage: reciting Fatiha, adding a sura, maintaining order in repeated actions, first sitting, tashahhud in last sitting, qunut in witr, takbirat of Eid, jahr in loud prayers, ikhfa in quiet prayers.
These are not exhaustive but are the ones mentioned.
4
Understand the resolution
The term 'sunnah' in the matn means 'established by the sunnah', so it literally includes both sunnan and wajibat, avoiding metaphorical interpretation.
This resolves the objection of combining literal and metaphorical.
5
Grasp the Hanafi hierarchy
Distinguish fard (qat'i, invalidates prayer if omitted), wajib (zanni, requires sajdat al-sahw if forgotten), sunnah (consistent practice, no compensation), and adab (occasional practice).
This hierarchy is unique to Hanafi fiqh.

He said: 'And whatever is besides that is sunnah.' He used the term sunnah, although among these actions there are wajibat, such as reciting Surah al-Fatihah, adding a surah with it, maintaining order in actions that are repeated, the first sitting, reciting tashahhud in the last sitting, qunut in witr, takbirat of the two Eids, raising the voice where it is required, and lowering the voice where it is required. For this reason, if one omits any of these, two prostrations of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) become obligatory. This is the correct view. Their being called sunnah in the book is because their obligation is established by the sunnah. Translation: He said: 'and whatever is besides that, they are sunnah'. Quduri used the term sunnah, although these actions include wajibat, such as reciting Fatiha, adding a surah, maintaining order in repeated actions, the first sitting, reciting tashahhud in the last sitting, reciting qunut in witr, takbirat of the two Eids, raising the voice where required, and lowering the voice where required. For this reason, if a worshipper omits any of these, two prostrations of forgetfulness become obligatory; that is the correct view. Their being named sunnah in the book is because their obligation is established by the sunnah. Explanation: Shaykh Quduri said that the mentioned things other than the fara'id are all sunnah. Sahib al-Hidayah said that Quduri used the term sunnah, although these actions include wajibat, so using the term sunnah here is not correct. ... [garbled section] ... Sahib al-Hidayah responded at the end of this passage saying that 'sunnah' here means what is established by the sunnah, and since the wajib is also established by the sunnah, the term sunnah is applied to the wajibat. But this answer of Sahib al-Hidayah is not correct, because in this case combining the literal and metaphorical meanings becomes necessary: taking sunnah to mean sunan (plural of sunnah) is a literal usage, and taking it to mean wajibat is a metaphorical usage; since both are intended here, combining literal and metaphorical would be necessary. The answer: Quduri's statement 'it is sunnah' means 'established by the sunnah'; and the wajibat and sunnan mentioned in this chapter are included under this word in a literal sense, so the problem of combining literal and metaphorical does not arise. Sahib al-Hidayah, enumerating the wajibat, said: For example, reciting Surah al-Fatihah is wajib, and adding a surah with it is wajib. Maintaining order in actions that are repeated in a rak'ah is also wajib. So if someone forgetfully leaves out the second prostration of the first rak'ah and stands up and completes the prayer, then remembers, he should perform the missed prostration and also perform sajdat al-sahw due to breach of order. This recollection may be before salam or after salam, provided that no invalidator of prayer has occurred. Also, the first sitting, reciting tashahhud in the last sitting, reciting the qunut supplication in witr, the takbirat of the two Eids, raising the voice in loud prayers, and lowering the voice in silent prayers are all wajib. This is why if any of these is omitted, sajdat al-sahw becomes obligatory. Benefit: Here 'wajib' means that without it the prayer is still valid, but its omission due to forgetfulness requires sajdat al-sahw. And 'sunnah' means that which the Prophet (s) performed with regularity and never left without excuse, such as the ta'awwudh, takbirat, ruku', and sujud. Prayer has some 'adab'; and 'adab' in prayer is that which the Prophet (s) performed occasionally and did not regularly maintain, such as increasing the tasbihat beyond three in ruku' and sujud, and reciting more than the customary amount of recitation.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a terminological discussion and enumeration of the wajibat of prayer. The base text (Quduri) stated that all acts other than the clearly mentioned fara'id are sunnah. Sahib al-Hidayah objects that this is imprecise because many of those acts are actually wajib (obligatory but with a lesser degree than fard). He lists them: reciting Fatiha, adding a sura, maintaining order in repeated actions (e.g., if one forgets a sajdah and remembers later, he must do it and also perform sajdat al-sahw for the disrupted order), the first sitting, tashahhud in the last sitting, qunut in witr, takbirat of Eid, jahr (loud) in loud prayers, and ikhfa (quiet) in quiet prayers. The resolution provided is that the term 'sunnah' in the matn means 'established by the sunnah', so it includes both sunnan and wajibat in a literal sense, avoiding the need for metaphorical interpretation. The passage then defines the technical terms: 'wajib' here refers to an act whose omission requires sajdat al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer; 'sunnah' refers to acts that the Prophet consistently performed; and 'adab' refers to occasional acts. This is a foundational lesson for understanding the Hanafi hierarchy of obligations in prayer.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act whose omission due to forgetfulness requires sajdat al-sahw; intentional omission is sinful but the prayer is valid.
سنت (sunnah): An act that the Prophet (s) consistently performed and never left without excuse; its omission is not sinful but disliked.
ادب (adab): A recommended act that the Prophet (s) performed occasionally but did not maintain regularly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a wajib according to the Hanafi school as listed in this passage?
A) Raising the hands before takbir
B) Reciting Surah al-Fatihah
C) Saying 'Ameen' after Fatihah
D) Performing sajdat al-tilawah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely distinguishes wajib from fard: wajibat are obligatory but their omission does not invalidate the prayer; compensation is via sajdat al-sahw.

Takbirat al-Tahrimah: Condition or Pillar?
Inter-madhhab dispute over the nature of takbirat al-tahrimah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school categorizes takbirat al-tahrimah as a condition (shart) rather than a pillar (rukn), and identify the practical consequence of this distinction.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is a condition, not a pillar – its separation from prayer is shown by the Quranic 'fa'.

This passage tackles a fundamental inter-madhhab dispute: What exactly is the legal nature of takbirat al-tahrimah? Is it an integral part of the prayer (rukn) or an external prerequisite (shart)? The answer has direct implications for how we understand the structure of salah and what actions are permitted after the takbir. Let us follow the Hanafi argument as presented by the commentator of Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
State the two competing positions
Identify from the text that Hanafis call takbirat al-tahrimah a 'shart' (condition), while al-Shafi'i calls it a 'rukn' (pillar). Note the immediate practical consequence given in the text: a person may change from fard to nafl without repeating the takbir.
The terms shart and rukn are defined in the key terms.
2
Extract the Hanafi proof from the Quran
Locate the verse 'wa dhakara isma rabbihi fasalla' (87:15). The Hanafi argument hinges on the conjunctive 'fa' (then). In Arabic grammar, 'fa' implies sequence and separation (maghayara). Thus the mention (takbir) is separate from the prayer.
This is a linguistic proof based on the literal meaning of the conjunction.
3
Understand the non-repetition argument
The commentator adds that, unlike other pillars (ruku', sujud) which repeat in every rak'ah, the takbirat al-tahrimah is said only once at the beginning. This is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) supporting the condition status.
Non-repetition is a practical indicator of external connection.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is clear: if one says takbir intending fard, he may change to nafl without a new takbir according to Hanafis. The Shafi'i would require a new takbir because the original takbir is integral to the first prayer and cannot serve another.
This shows that the classification is not merely theoretical.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi (relied upon for fatwa). The narrator of Al-Hidayah endorses it as the correct view. Recognize that the proof from the Quranic 'fa' is decisive in the Hanafi usul framework.
Al-Marghinani and later Hanafi masters affirm this position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اذا شرع في الصلوة كبر لما تلونا وقال عليه السلام تحريمها التكبير وهو شرط عندنا خلافا للشافعي حتى ان من يحرم للفرض كان له ان يؤدى بها التطوع وهو يقول انه يشترط لها ما يشترط السائر الاركان وهذا اية الركنية ولنا انه عطف الصلوة عليه في قوله تعالى و ذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّى ومقتضاه المغايرة ولهذا لا يتكرر كتكرر الاركان ومراعاة الشرائط لما يتصل به من القيام
ترجمہ اور جب نماز شروع کرے تو تکبیر کہے اس آیت کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے تلاوت کی اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا نماز کی تحریم تکبیر ہے اور یہ ہمارے نزدیک شرط ہے امام شافعی کا خلاف ہے حتی کہ جو کوئی فرض کا تحریمہ باند ھے تو اس کو جائز ہے کہ اس تحریمہ سے نفل ادا کرے اور امام شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ تحریمہ کے لئے ہر وہ چیز شرط ہے جو دوسرے ارکان کے لئے شرط ہے اور یہ بات اس کے رکن ہونے کی علامت ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول و ذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّی میں تکبیر مذکور پر نماز کا عطف کیا گیا ہے اور عطف کا مقتضی مغایرت ہے اور اسی وجہ سے تکبیر مکر نہیں ہوتی جیسا کہ دوسرے ارکان مکرر ہوتے ہیں۔ اور شرائط کی رعایت اس
And when he begins the prayer, he should say the takbir because of the verse we recited, and the Prophet (s) said: 'Its tahrim (prohibition of worldly acts) is the takbir.' And it is a condition (shart) according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, to the extent that if someone performs the tahrimah (opening takbir) for a fard prayer, it is permissible for him to perform a nafl prayer with that same takbir. Al-Shafi'i says that for the tahrimah, all the conditions required for other pillars are required, and this is a sign of its being a pillar (rukn). Our proof is that Allah's saying 'And he mentions the name of his Lord, then prays' (Quran 87:15) places the prayer after the mention, and the implication of conjunctive 'then' is difference (maghayara). Therefore, the takbir does not repeat like the other pillars, and it is associated with the conditions that are attached to standing.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the legal nature of takbirat al-tahrimah (the opening takbir). The Hanafi position, stated first, is that it is a condition (shart) of prayer, not a pillar (rukn). The key practical consequence is that if one intends a fard prayer with the takbir, one may use that same intention to perform a nafl prayer without renewing the takbir, because the takbir itself does not specify the type of prayer; it merely prohibits worldly actions and begins the state of consecration. The Shafi'i position is that it is a rukn (pillar), analogous to other pillars, and thus requires the same conditions. The Hanafi proof from the Qur'an (Surah al-A'la: 'wa dhakara isma rabbihi fasalla') is that the verb 'dhakara' (mentioning) is separate from 'salla' (praying) due to the conjunctive 'fa' (then), indicating that the dhikr (takbir) is independent from the prayer. Moreover, in practice, the takbir is not repeated within the prayer like other pillars (e.g., ruku' and sujud are repeated in each rak'ah), further supporting that it is a preliminary condition rather than an integral part of the prayer. This distinction is crucial for understanding the structure of prayer in Hanafi fiqh and has implications for the validity of changing intentions after the takbir.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbirat al-tahrimah): The opening takbir ('Allahu Akbar') that begins the prayer and prohibits worldly actions.
شرط (shart): A condition that must be present for the prayer to be valid, but is not part of the prayer's essence.
رکن (rukn): An integral part of the prayer that cannot be omitted; its omission invalidates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the status of takbirat al-tahrimah in prayer?
A) It is a pillar (rukn) like ruku' and sujud
B) It is a condition (shart) that must be present for validity
C) It is a sunnah whose omission requires sajdat al-sahw
D) It is a recommended act with no effect on validity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of takbirat al-tahrimah as a condition (shart) rather than a pillar (rukn) is supported by the Quranic conjunction 'fa' and the non-repetition of the takbir, permitting flexibility in changing intention within the prayer.

Definitions of Wajib and Sunnah in Hanafi Prayer
Commentary defining wajib, sunnah, and adab in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the Hanafi categories of wajib, sunnah, and adab in prayer, and identify which acts fall under each category.

Core Idea
Wajib in Hanafi prayer is a distinct obligated category whose forgetful omission requires sajdah sahw, not repetition.

In Hanafi fiqh, the terms wajib, sunnah, and adab carry precise meanings that affect the validity and compensation of prayer. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies these definitions by listing the wajibat of prayer and distinguishing them from sunan and adab. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for correctly applying the rules of sajdah sahw and for appreciating the Hanafi approach to prayer obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms defined
Look for the definitions of wajib, sunnah, and adab in the passage. Note the key characteristics: wajib omission requires sajdah sahw, sunnah is consistent practice, adab is occasional.
2
Extract the list of wajibat
The passage enumerates several wajib acts in prayer: reciting Fatihah, adding a surah, maintaining order in repeated actions, tashahhud in the first sitting, qunut in witr, Eid takbirs, loud/silent recitation accordingly.
3
Understand the consequence
For each wajib, forgetful omission requires sajdah sahw but does not invalidate prayer. This is the defining feature of wajib in Hanafi school.
4
Distinguish sunnah and adab
Sunnah is what the Prophet consistently performed and never abandoned without excuse (e.g., thana, ta'awwudh). Adab is occasional (e.g., extra tasbihat). Omission of sunnah is not compensated, omission of adab is less serious.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Hanafis classify reciting Fatihah as wajib; Shafi'is consider it a rukn. This affects the consequence: in Hanafi, forgetful omission requires sajdah sahw; in Shafi'i, the prayer is invalid if Fatihah is omitted.

صاحب ہدایہ نے اس عبارت کے آخر میں جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ سنت سے مراد ما ثبت بالسنتہ ہے اور چونکہ واجب بھی سنت سے ثابت ہوتا ہے اس لئے واجبات پر سنت کا اطلاق کر دیا گیا۔ لیکن صاحب ہدایہ کا یہ جواب صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں جمع بین الحقیقة والمجاز لازم آتا ہے پر اس طور پر کہ سنت سے سنن مراد لینا بطریق حقیقت ہے اور واجبات مراد لینا بطریق مجاز ہے پس چونکہ یہاں دونوں مراد ہیں اس لئے حقیقت اور مجاز کو جمع کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ جواب مصنف قدوری کے قول فهو سنت سے مراد ثابت بالستہ ہے اور واجبات اور سنن جو اس باب میں مذکور ہیں وہ اس لفظ کے تحت بطریق حقیقت داخل ہیں پرن مع بین الحقیقیہ والمجاز کا اشکال واقع نہیں ہوگا۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے واجبات شمار کراتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ جیسے سورۃ فاتحہ کا پڑھنا واجب ہے اور فاتحہ کے ساتھ سورت ملانا واجب ہے۔ اور جو افعال ایک رکعت میں مکر شروع ہوئے ہیں ان میں ترتیب کی رعایت رکھنا بھی واجب ہے چنانچہ اگر کسی نے بھول کر رکعت بولی کا دوسرا سجدہ چھوڑ دیا اور کھڑے ہو کر نماز پوری کر لی پھر اس کو یاد آیا تو وہ مترو کہ سجدہ ادا کرے اور ترک ترتیب کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو کرے۔ یہ یاد آ نا سلام سے پہلے ہو یا سلام کے بعد بشر طیکہ کوئی مفسد صلوۃ امر پیش نہ آیا ہو۔ اور پہلا قعدہ قعدہ ائیر میں تشہد پڑھنا وتر میں دعائے قنوت پڑھنا عیدین کی تکبیریں اور جہری نمازوں میں جبر کرنا اور سری نمازوں میں اتفاء کرنا بھی واجب ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر ان میں سے کوئی ایک ترک ہو گیا تو سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا۔ فائدہ یہاں واجب سے مراد یہ ہے کہ جس کے بغیر نماز درست ہو جائے لیکن اس کے سہوترک سے سجدۂ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اور سنت سے مراد یہ ہے کہ جس کو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے موا بت کے ساتھ کیا ہو اور بغیر عذر کبھی ترک نہ کیا ہو جیسے ثاء تعود تکبیرات رکوع وجود۔ نماز کے کچھ آداب ہیں اور نماز میں ادب وہ ہے جس کو حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کبھی کبھار کیا اور اس پر مواظبت نہ فرمائی ہو۔ جیسے رکوع اور سجدے میں تین پر تسبیحات کی زیادتی اور قرأت مسنونہ سے زائد قرآت کرنا۔
The author of Hidayah responded at the end of this passage saying that by 'sunnah' is meant what is established by the Sunnah, and since wajib is also established by the Sunnah, the term 'sunnah' is applied to wajibat. But this response of the author of Hidayah is not correct, because in that case combining the literal and metaphorical meanings would be necessary, in that taking 'sunnah' to mean sunan is literal, and taking it to mean wajibat is metaphorical; since both are intended here, combining literal and metaphorical would be necessary. The response: By the statement of the author of Quduri 'so it is sunnah', what is meant is established by the Sunnah, and the wajibat and sunan mentioned in this chapter are included under this word in a literal sense, so the problem of combining literal and metaphorical will not occur. The author of Hidayah, while enumerating the wajibat, said: such as reciting Surah Fatihah is wajib, and adding a surah with Fatihah is wajib. And maintaining order in the actions that are repeatedly done in one rak'ah is also wajib; so if someone forgetfully missed the second sajdah of a rak'ah, then stood up and completed the prayer, then he remembers, he should perform the missed sajdah and perform sajdah sahw due to violation of order. This remembering may be before salam or after, provided no invalidator of prayer has occurred. And in the first sitting (qa'dah ula), reciting tashahhud, reciting qunut dua in witr, the takbirs of the two Eids, loud recitation in loud prayers, and silent recitation in silent prayers are also wajib. For this reason, if any one of these is omitted, sajdah sahw becomes wajib. Benefit: Here 'wajib' means that without which the prayer is valid, but its forgetful omission necessitates sajdah sahw. And 'sunnah' means that which the Prophet (peace be upon him) did consistently and never abandoned without excuse, such as the thana, ta'awwudh, takbirs of ruku' and sujud. There are some adab of prayer, and adab in prayer is that which the Prophet (peace be upon him) did occasionally and did not persist in, such as increasing the tasbihat beyond three in ruku' and sujud, and reciting more than the prescribed recitation.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling clarifying the terminology used in the Hanafi school for prayer. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah, commenting on a response from the author of Hidayah, explains that the term 'sunnah' in the Hidayah's chapter heading refers to what is established by the Sunnah, which includes both wajibat (obligatory acts that require sajdah sahw) and sunan (emphasized supererogatory acts). Then he lists the known wajibat of prayer: reciting Fatihah, adding a surah, maintaining order in repeated actions (like sajdahs), tashahhud in the first sitting, qunut in witr, takbirs of Eid, etc. If any of these is omitted forgetfully, sajdah sahw is required. He then distinguishes sunnah (continuous practice of the Prophet) from adab (occasional practice). This distinction is crucial for understanding the compensatory nature of sajdah sahw in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An act whose omission forgetfully requires sajdah sahw, but does not invalidate the prayer.
سنة (sunnah): An act that the Prophet consistently performed and never abandoned without excuse.
أدب (adab): An act that the Prophet performed occasionally and did not persist in.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Wajib in Hanafi prayer is a distinct obligated category whose forgetful omission requires sajdah sahw, while sunnah requires no compensation and adab is occasional.

Ruling that raising hands with takbir is sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during the opening takbir and explain the proof from the Prophet's consistent practice.

Core Idea
Raising hands with takbir is sunnah, not wajib; omission does not invalidate prayer.

This lesson clarifies the nature of raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) during the opening takbir of salah. The Hanafi school classifies this act as a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), based on the Prophet's continuous practice. Understanding this ruling helps avoid the common misconception that omitting it requires compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The passage states that raising hands with the takbir is sunnah. Identify the act (raf' al-yadayn) and its legal category (sunnah).
2

The proof is the Prophet's consistent practice (muwazabah). Recognize that in Hanafi usul, the Prophet's continuous practice indicates sunnah status.
Muwazabah is a form of evidence for sunnah mu'akkadah.
3
Analyze the Wording for Simultaneity
The phrase 'with the takbir' (مع التكبير) indicates that the raising must be simultaneous with the utterance. Note that this is a condition for correctly performing the sunnah, not a condition of validity.
If raised before or after, the sunnah is not fulfilled but the prayer remains valid.

Takbir Tahrimah: Condition or Pillar?
Explains the Hanafi position on Takbir Tahrimah as a condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that Takbir Tahrimah is a condition (shart) for prayer, derive the Quranic evidence from the conjunction in Surah al-A'la, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
Takbir Tahrimah is a condition, not a pillar—proved by Quranic conjunction and its non-repetition.

The opening takbir of prayer, known as Takbir Tahrimah, is a foundational element of salah. Yet the schools differ on its precise legal status: is it a condition external to the prayer or a pillar integral to it? This lesson explores the Hanafi position as presented in Al-Hidayah, the Shafi'i objection based on qiyas, and the textual evidence that decides the issue.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly restate that the Hanafi school holds Takbir Tahrimah to be a condition (shart) for prayer, not a pillar (rukn).
A condition is external to the act; a pillar is part of the act itself.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i considers Takbir Tahrimah to be a pillar (rukn) of prayer. Understand the basis of this view.
The Shafi'i position relies on qiyas (analogy) with other pillars.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i argument: the same preconditions (purity, covering awrah, qibla, intention, time) apply to Takbir Tahrimah as to other pillars, so it must be a pillar by analogy.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses two main proofs: (a) the Quranic verse where 'prayer' is conjuncted to 'mention of the Lord's name' (the takbir) — conjunction requires difference, so takbir cannot be part of prayer; (b) unlike other pillars, takbir is not repeated in prayer, indicating it is a condition.
The Hanafi also respond to the Shafi'i qiyas by arguing that the preconditions are for the standing that follows takbir, not for the takbir itself.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: according to Hanafis, one may perform a voluntary prayer with the same takbir as an obligatory prayer because a condition can serve multiple acts; according to Shafi'is, this is invalid because a pillar belongs exclusively to one prayer.
This is a clear example of ikhtilaf affecting daily practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفۃ الصلوة
قیام کی وجہ سے ہے جو اس کے ساتھ متصل ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ، جب نماز شروع کرنے کا ارادہ کرے نماز خواہ فرض ہو خواہ فل تو تکبیر تحریمہ کھڑے ہو کر کہے پس اگر کسی نے بیٹھ کر کیا الکبر کہی پھر کھڑا ہو گیا تو وہ نماز شروع کرنے والا نہیں ہو گا۔ اور اگر کوئی شخص نماز میں شرکت کے ارادے سے آیا حالانکہ امام رکوع میں ۔ ترجمہ پس اس نے اپنی پشت جھکاتے ہوئے تکبیر کہی تو اس صورت میں اگر یہ شخص تکبیر کہتے وقت قیام سے قریب تر ہے تو جائز ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ بتارت اگر کسی نے امام کو رکوع میں پایا پھر اس نے تکبیر رکوع کے ارادے سے کھڑے ہو کر تکبیر کہی تو بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ اس کا ارادہ لغو ہے وہ پہلے دو نہ حالت قیام میں اس کی تکبیر تحریمہ کے لئے قرار دی جائے گی۔
دلیل وہ آیت ہے جو سابق میں گذر چکی یعنی و رنگ فکر اور دوسری دلیل حضور کا قول تحریمها التکبیر ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ تکبیر تحریمہ ہمارے نزدیک شرط ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک رکن ہے ثمرہ اختلاف اس طرح ظاہر ہو گا کہ ہمارے نزدیک چونکہ تحریمہ شرط ہے اس لئے فرض کے تحریمہ سے نفل ادا کرنا جائز ہوگا۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک چونکہ رکن ہے اس لئے . فرض کے تحریمہ سے نفل ادا کر نا جائز نہیں ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شرط کے ساتھ متعدد نمازیں ادا کرنا جائز ہے لیکن ایک رکن کے ساتھ جائے نہیں۔ بہر حال تکبیر تحریمہ کے رکن ہونے پر امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تکبیر تحریمہ کے لئے ہر وہ چیز شرط ہے جو دوسرے ارکان کے لئے طحاوی ۔ شرط ہے جیسے طہارت ستر عورت استقبال قبلہ نیت اور وقت یعنی یہ چیزیں جس طرح قیام قرآت رکوع اور سجدہ وغیرہ ارکان کے لئے شرط ہونے کی علامت ہے یعنی دوسرے ارکان پر قیاس کر کے اس کو بھی رکن قرار دیا جائے گا۔ ہیں اس طرح تکبیر تحریمہ کے لئے بھی شرط ہیں اور جس چیز کے لئے وہ باتیں شرط ہوں جو تمام ارکان کے لئے شرط ہیں تو اس چیز کے رکن ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول و ذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّی میں نماز کا عطف ذکر اسم رب یعنی تکبیر تحریمہ پر کیا ہے اور عطف تقاضا کرتا ہے مغایرت کا یعنی معطوف علیہ اور معطوف کے درمیان تغایر ضروری ہے۔ پس اگر کبیر کور کن مانا جائے تو کل کا عطف جز پر لازم آئے گا اور چونکہ کل اس جز کو بھی شامل ہے اس لئے عطف شئ على نفسه لازم آئے گا اور یہ ناجائز ہے۔ اس وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ تکبیر تحریمہ رکن نہیں بلکہ شرط ہے اور چونکہ شرط شئی شئی سے خارج ہوتی ہے اس لئے تکبیر تحریمہ اور نماز کے درمیان تغایر ہوگا اور عطف درست ہوگا پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ تکبیر تحریمہ نماز کی شرط ہے نہ کہ رکن ۔ تکبیر تحریمہ رکن نہیں ورنہ دوسرے ارکان کی طرح تکبیر تحریمہ مکر ر ہوتی۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح دوسرے ارکان نماز میں مکر رہوتے ہیں کبیر تحریمہ کر نہیں ہوتی پس یہ اس بات کی علامت ہے کہ شروع کرتے ومراعاة الشرائط سے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب ہے جو اب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ شرائط ( طہارت ستر عورت وغیرہ) کی رعایت نفس تحریمہ کے لئے نہیں ہے بلکہ قیام جوتحریمہ سے متصل ہے اس کے لئے ہے اور وہ رکن ہے پس اس سے تحریمہ کارکن ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔
Chapter on Description of Prayer. Because of standing that is connected to it. Explanation of Issue: When one intends to start prayer, whether obligatory or voluntary, he must say the Takbir Tahrimah while standing. If someone said 'Allahu Akbar' while sitting and then stood up, he has not started the prayer. And if a person comes with the intention of joining the prayer while the Imam is in ruku' – then he said the takbir while bending his back – in this case, if this person is closer to standing when he says the takbir, it is permissible; otherwise not. Likewise, if someone finds the Imam in ruku' and then says the takbir for ruku' while standing, that is also permissible, because his intention is void and his takbir will be considered as Takbir Tahrimah in the state of standing. The evidence is the verse that passed earlier, and the second evidence is the Prophet's saying: 'Its prohibition is the takbir.' The author of Hidayah said: Takbir Tahrimah is a condition (shart) according to us, and according to Imam Shafi'i it is a pillar (rukn). The practical consequence of the difference is that according to us, since it is a condition, it is permissible to perform a voluntary prayer with the takbir of an obligatory prayer. According to Imam Shafi'i, since it is a pillar, it is not permissible. The reason is that it is permissible to perform multiple prayers with one condition, but not with one pillar. Anyway, Imam Shafi'i's evidence for it being a pillar is that everything that is a condition for other pillars is also a condition for Takbir Tahrimah, such as purity, covering awrah, facing qibla, intention, and time. Just as these are conditions for the pillars like standing, recitation, ruku', and sujud, so by analogy (qiyas) Takbir Tahrimah should also be a pillar. Our evidence is that in the saying of Allah: 'and mentioned the name of his Lord and prayed,' prayer is conjuncted (atf) to the mention of the name of the Lord, i.e., Takbir Tahrimah, and conjunction requires difference between the conjuncted and the conjuncted to. So if takbir is considered a part of prayer, then the conjunction of the whole to a part would occur, and since the whole includes that part, it would be conjunction of a thing to itself, which is invalid. Therefore, we say Takbir Tahrimah is not a pillar but a condition. Since a condition is external to the thing, there will be difference between Takbir Tahrimah and prayer, and the conjunction will be valid. Thus it is proven that Takbir Tahrimah is a condition of prayer, not a pillar. Another evidence: unlike other pillars that are repeated in prayer, Takbir Tahrimah is not repeated, indicating it is a condition. The response to Imam Shafi'i's evidence from conditions is that the observance of those conditions (purity, covering awrah, etc.) is not for the takbir itself but for the standing that is connected to it, which is a pillar. Therefore, this does not prove the takbir is a pillar.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding Takbir Tahrimah. The author of Al-Hidayah states that according to the Hanafi school, Takbir Tahrimah is a condition (shart) for prayer, not a pillar (rukn). Imam al-Shafi'i holds it to be a pillar. The practical difference is that if one performs a voluntary prayer using the same takbir as an obligatory prayer, it is permissible in the Hanafi school because a condition can serve multiple acts, whereas a pillar cannot. The Shafi'i evidence uses qiyas: since the same preconditions (tahara, satr, qibla, niyya, time) apply to both Takbir Tahrimah and other pillars, it should be treated as a pillar. The Hanafi response relies on the Qur'anic verse (Surah al-A'la 87:15) where 'prayer' is conjuncted to 'mention of the name of the Lord.' Conjunction (atf) implies difference, so takbir cannot be part of prayer. Additionally, unlike other pillars that are repeated in prayer, takbir occurs only once, further indicating it is a condition external to the prayer.

Key Terms
تکبیر تحریمہ (Takbir Tahrimah): The opening takbir that prohibits worldly actions and initiates the prayer.
شرط (shart): A condition external to the act; its presence is necessary for validity but it is not part of the act itself.
رکن (rukn): A pillar integral to the act; its omission invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of Takbir Tahrimah in prayer?
A) It is a pillar (rukn).
B) It is a condition (shart).
C) It is recommended (sunnah).
D) It is obligatory (wajib).

Key Takeaway
Takbir Tahrimah is a condition (shart) for prayer, not a pillar (rukn), based on the Quranic conjunction and its non-repetition.

Salah — Prayer

Raising Hands in Prayer: Timing and Height
Ruling and fiqh of raising hands in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands in prayer, explain the preferred timing (before takbir), and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position on height.

Core Idea
Raising hands in prayer is sunnah muakkadah; the Hanafi asahh view raises hands before takbir, to the earlobes.

This lesson examines a classic passage from al-Hidayah that addresses two practical aspects of the opening takbir: when to raise the hands and to what height. While the basic ruling that raf' al-yadayn is sunnah is agreed upon, there is an important intra-Hanafi difference on whether hands should be raised simultaneously with the takbir or just before it. Additionally, the Hanafi school differs from the Shafi'i school on the height to which the hands should be raised. By working through the text, you will understand the proofs and the reasoning behind the preferred Hanafi practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that raising hands with the takbir (raf' al-yadayn) is sunnah. Determine the specific hukm level: sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
The proof of sunniyyah is the Prophet's consistency (muwazabah) with occasional omission.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on timing
Two views exist: simultaneous raising (Abu Yusuf, al-Tahawi) vs. raising before takbir (majority). Identify which is 'asahh' and why.
The wording 'ma'a al-takbir' suggests simultaneity, but the majority prefer precedence.
3
Examine the rational proof (ta'lil)
The passage presents a logical argument: raising hands negates greatness from other than Allah, while saying takbir affirms it for Allah. Negation precedes affirmation, like in the shahadah.
This rational proof is used to support the precedence view.
4
Review the hadith evidence for timing
The hadith of Wail ibn Hajar (hands before takbir) is cited. The contradicting hadith of Anas (takbir before hands) is mentioned but not resolved here; the asahh view relies on the former.
The author of Hidayah does not use Wail's hadith directly due to apparent contradiction, but the asahh view still holds.
5
Compare the height dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is
Hanafis raise hands to earlobes (thumbs aligned); Shafi'is raise to shoulders. Identify the proofs: Hanafis cite Wail, al-Bara', Anas; Shafi'is cite Abu Humayd.
The Hanafi response interprets the Shafi'i proof as applying to cases of excuse.

و يرفع يديه حتى يحاذى بابهاميه شحمة اذنيه، وعند الشافعي يرفع الى منكبيه، وعلى هذا تكبيرة القنوت والاعياد والجنازة، له حديث ابي حميد الساعدي قال: كان النبي عليه السلام اذا كبر رفع يديه الى منكبيه، الإعلام الاصم، وهو بما قلناه، ومارواه يحمل على حالة العذر ولنا رواية وائل بن حجر و البراء وانس ان النبي عليه السلام كان اذا كبر رفع يديه حذاء اذنيه ولان رفع اليد
And he raises his hands with the takbir, and this is sunnah, because the Prophet peace be upon him consistently did it, and this wording indicates the condition of simultaneity. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf and related from al-Tahawi. The most correct (asahh) is that he first raises his hands then says the takbir, because his action is negation of pride from other than Allah, and negation is given precedence. Explanation: He said that a man raises his hands with the takbir, and raising hands at the beginning of prayer is sunnah because the Prophet consistently did it, sometimes with occasional omission. Then there is difference of opinion regarding the preferred time. Shaykh al-Islam and Qadikhan said that raising hands and saying takbir should be simultaneous; the expression of al-Quduri also indicates this because he said 'yarfa' yadayhi ma'a al-takbir' and the word 'ma'a' indicates simultaneity. This is the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam al-Tahawi also acted upon it. The author of Hidayah said that in the madhhab the most correct (asahh) is that he first raises his hands then says the takbir; this is held by the generality of the mashayikh. The evidence is that in his action there is the meaning of negation, and in his statement there is the meaning of affirmation: when he raises his hands, he negates greatness from other than Allah, and when he says 'Allahu Akbar', he affirms greatness for Allah. And in negation and affirmation, negation takes precedence, just as in the kalimah of shahadah negation is given precedence. Therefore, it is preferable to raise hands first then say takbir. The saying of 'asahh' is also supported by the hadith of Wail ibn Hajar: 'When the Prophet stood for prayer, he would raise his hands then say takbir.' But the author of Hidayah did not use this hadith because the hadith of Anas contradicts it: 'When the Prophet began prayer, he would say takbir then raise his hands.' (Sharh al-Niqayah) The hands should be raised until his thumbs are parallel to the lobes of his ears. According to al-Shafi'i, he raises to his shoulders; likewise for takbir of qunut, 'Id, and funeral prayer. He has the hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi: 'When the Prophet said takbir, he raised his hands to his shoulders.' The deaf informant? And what we have said; and what he narrated is interpreted as a case of excuse. We have the narration of Wail ibn Hajar, al-Bara', and Anas that the Prophet when he said takbir raised his hands to the level of his ears, and because raising the hand...
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage covers two fiqh issues: the timing of raising hands in relation to takbir, and the height to which they are raised. It begins by stating that raising hands is sunnah (proven by the Prophet's consistency), and notes that the wording of the matn (with 'ma'a') suggests simultaneity. This is the view of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam al-Tahawi. However, the 'asahh' view of the madhhab, supported by the majority of mashayikh including the author of al-Hidayah, is that hands should be raised first, then the takbir should be said. The reasoning is that raising hands negates greatness for other than Allah, while saying takbir affirms it for Allah; negation precedes affirmation, as in the shahadah. This is further supported by the hadith of Wail ibn Hajar. The apparent contradiction with the hadith of Anas is noted but the author does not resolve it here. On the issue of height, the Hanafi position is to raise hands until the thumbs align with the earlobes. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that hands should be raised to the shoulders. The Hanafis cite hadiths from Wail, al-Bara', and Anas; the Shafi'i proof is from Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi, which the Hanafis interpret as applying when there is an excuse (e.g., in crowded conditions).

Key Terms
رفع الیدین (Raf' al-Yadayn): Raising the hands during the opening takbir of prayer.
مقارنت (Muqaranah): Simultaneity of raising hands and saying takbir.
سنت (Sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed, occasionally without blame.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the 'asahh' view in the Hanafi school, what is the preferred timing for raising hands in prayer?
A) Hands raised after the takbir.
B) Hands raised simultaneously with the takbir.
C) Hands raised before the takbir.
D) Hands raised only during the funeral prayer.

Key Takeaway
Raising hands in prayer is sunnah muakkadah; the Hanafi asahh view is to raise hands before the takbir to the earlobes.

Timing of Raising Hands: With Takbir or Before?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of raf' al-yadayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions regarding the timing of raising hands at the start of prayer and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
The preferred Hanafi view: raise hands first, then say takbir – negation precedes affirmation.

Raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) at the start of prayer is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) in the Hanafi school. However, the precise moment of raising – simultaneously with takbir or just before it – has been a point of discussion among Hanafi jurists. This lesson unpacks the intra-madhhab dispute, evaluates the proofs, and identifies the relied-upon position according to the author of al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the disputed act is (raf' al-yadayn) and its legal status (sunnah muakkadah). Note that the ruling itself is agreed upon; the dispute is about the optimal timing.
2
State the two positions
Position 1: Raise hands simultaneously with saying takbir (Quduri, Abu Yusuf, Tahawi). Position 2: Raise hands first, then say takbir (generality of mashayikh, asahh view in Hidayah).
3
Examine the evidence for each
For position 2: Rational argument – raising hands negates pride for other than Allah (nafi), saying takbir affirms for Allah (ithbat), and nafi precedes ithbat. Also hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr. For position 1: Expression 'ma'a al-takbir' in Quduri's text and hadith of Anas.
The hadith of Wa'il uses 'thumma' (then), while Anas's hadith places takbir before raising. Both are ahad hadith.
4
Determine the tarjih (preference) and mufta bihi
The author of Hidayah declares the view of raising first as 'asahh' (most correct), supported by the majority of mashayikh and the rational principle of nafi preceding ithbat. The mufta bihi is to raise hands first, then say takbir.
The other position is also valid; the difference is in virtue (afdaliyyah), not validity.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم الكبرياء عن غير الله تعالى والنفى مقدم وهو المروى عن ابى يوسف والمحكى عن الطحاوى والاصح انه ويرفع يديه اولا ثم يكبر، لان فعله نفى

شروع کرتے تو تکبیر کہتے پھر اپنے دونوں ہاتھ اٹھاتے۔ (شرح نقایہ )
Chapter of the Description of Prayer. Ashraf al-Bidaya Urdu Sharh Hidaya Volume Two. 'Pride/Greatness is from other than Allah, and negation is prioritized, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf and related from al-Tahawi, and the most correct is that he raises his hands first then says takbir, because his action is negation.' Translation: And (a man) raises his two hands with the takbir, and this is sunnah because the Prophet (ﷺ) persisted upon it. And this word indicates the condition of concomitance, and it is narrated from Abu Yusuf and related from al-Tahawi, and the most correct is that he raises both hands first then says takbir, because his action is negation of pride from other than Allah, and negation is prioritized. Explanation: He said that a man raises his two hands simultaneously with takbir, and raising hands at the start of prayer is sunnah because the Prophet (ﷺ) persisted upon it with occasional omission, and this is a sign of its being sunnah. Then there is disagreement about what is the most excellent time for raising hands. Shaykh al-Islam and Qadi Khan said that raising hands and saying takbir should be simultaneous, and the expression of al-Quduri also indicates this because 'Allamah al-Quduri said 'yarfa'u yadayhi ma'a al-takbir' and the word 'ma'a' denotes concomitance. This is the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf, and Imam al-Tahawi also acted upon this. The author of al-Hidayah said that in the madhhab the most correct is that he raises both hands first then says takbir, and the generality of the mashayikh hold this. The proof is that in his action there is the meaning of negation and in his saying there is the meaning of affirmation, such that when this person raises his hands he negates pride from other than Allah, and when he says Allahu Akbar he affirms pride for Allah. And in negation and affirmation, negation takes precedence over affirmation, just as in the kalimah of shahadah negation is given priority. For this reason, the most excellent is to raise both hands first then say takbir. The most correct view is also supported by the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr, the wording of the hadith here: 'an-nabiyya sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam hina qama ila as-salah yarfa'u yadayhi thumma yukabbir' meaning when the Prophet (ﷺ) stood for prayer he raised his two hands then said takbir. But the author of al-Hidayah did not use this hadith because the hadith of Anas contradicts it, the hadith: Anas said, 'kana Rasulullahi idha iftataha as-salah kabbara thumma rafa'a yadayhi' - Hadrat Anas (رضي الله عنه) says that when the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) began prayer he said takbir then raised his two hands. (Sharh al-Niqayah)
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) at the start of prayer. The base text states that raising hands is sunnah and mentions two views: raising with takbir (reported from Abu Yusuf and Tahawi) and raising before takbir (the most correct view). The commentator explains that the word 'ma'a' in Quduri's expression indicates simultaneity, but the preferred view in the madhhab according to the generality of mashayikh is to raise first, based on a rational argument: raising hands negates pride for other than Allah (action of negation), and saying takbir affirms it for Allah (saying of affirmation), and negation precedes affirmation. This is like the shahadah where negation (la ilaha) comes before affirmation (illa Allah). Support is also drawn from the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr, but the author of Hidayah does not cite it because the hadith of Anas (raising after takbir) contradicts it, indicating that both timings are permissible but the order is preferred. Thus, the mufta bihi is to raise hands first, then say takbir.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising both hands during takbir al-tahrimah or other takbirs in prayer.
تكبير تحریمہ (takbir al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer.
نفی (nafi): Negation; in this context, the action of raising hands negates pride for anyone other than Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the asahh (most correct) position in the Hanafi madhhab, when should a man raise his hands at the start of prayer?
A) After saying takbir
B) Simultaneously with takbir
C) Before saying takbir
D) Only during qunut

Key Takeaway
The most correct Hanafi position is to raise hands first, then say takbir, following the principle of negation before affirmation and the majority of mashayikh.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Extent of Raising Hands: To Ears or Shoulders
Inter-madhhab dispute with proofs and rational argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the height of raising hands during takbir al-tahrimah, explain its evidence, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Raising hands to the ears is the Hanafi sunnah; the Shafi'i sunnah is to shoulders – the dispute is about which hadith is preferred.

This passage from the Hidayah presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute on the manner of raising hands at the start of prayer. The Hanafi school, based on multiple hadiths and a rational argument, holds that the thumbs should align with the earlobes. The Shafi'i school, relying on the hadith of Abu Humaid, raises hands to the shoulders. Understanding this dispute clarifies the distinction between authentic proofs and the method of tarjih (preference) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school says about the height of raising hands. The passage states: hands are raised until the thumbs align with the earlobes.
This applies to takbir al-tahrimah, qunut, Eid, and Janazah takbirs.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that hands should be raised to the shoulders. This is the opposing view in the dispute.
One narration from Ahmad also follows the shoulder position.
3
Examine the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi in Bukhari: the Prophet raised his hands to his shoulders during takbir.
The hadith is sahih and directly contradicts the Hanafi position.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds with (a) stronger narrations (Wa'il, Bara', Anas) showing ear-level raising, and (b) a rational argument that raising hands signals the deaf, which is most effective at ear level. The hadith of Abu Humaid is interpreted as a case of excuse.
This shows how multiple evidences are weighed in Hanafi methodology.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis raise to ears, Shafi'is to shoulders. Both consider it sunnah, so the prayer remains valid either way, but the sunnah is performed differently.
In a mixed congregation, following the imam's practice is recommended for harmony.

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت اپنے دونوں ہاتھوں کو اس قدر اٹھائے کہ دونوں انگوٹھے دونوں کانوں کی لو کے محاذ کی ( مقابل ) ہو جائیں۔ امام شافعی اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ کندھوں تک اٹھائے یہی ایک روایت امام احمد سے ہے۔ یہی اختلاف قنوت عیدین اور جنازہ کی تکبیر کے وقت ہاتھ اٹھانے میں ہے۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل حدیث ابی حمید ہے عن محمد بن عمر وبن عطاء انه كان جالسامع نفر من اصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال فذ كرنا صلاة رسول الله فقال ابو حميد الساعدى انا كنت احفظكم لصلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأيته اذا كبر جعل يديه حذاء منكبيه ( بخاری ) محمد بن عمرو بن عطاء سے روایت ہے کہ وہ اصحاب نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کی ایک جماعت کے ساتھ بیٹھے ہوئے تھے محمد بن عمرد کہتے ہیں کہ ہم نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی نماز کا ذکر کیا تو ابوحمید الساعدی نے کہا کہ میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی نماز کو محفوظ کر لیتا تھا میں نے آپ کو دیکھا کہ جب آپ تکبیر کہتے تو اپنے دونوں ہاتھ اپنے دونوں کندھوں کے مقابل کرتے ۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے یہ حدیث ان الفاظ کے ساتھ ذکر کی ہے کان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا كبر رفع يديه الى منكبيه ان دونوں حدیثوں سے ثابت ہوا کہ حضور تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت دونوں ہاتھ کندھوں تک اٹھاتے تھے۔
ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو وائل بن حجر براء بن عازب اور حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالی عنہم نے روایت کیا ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم كان اذاكبر رفع يديه حذاء اذينه يعنى حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم جب تکبیر کہتے تو اپنے دونوں ہاتھ اپنے کانوں کے مقابل کر کے اٹھاتے۔ (حاکم) اور دار قطنی نے حضرت انس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے یہ حدیث ان الفاظ کے ساتھ نقل کی ہے قال كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا افتتح الصلوة كبر ثم رفع يديه حتى يحاذى ابهاميه اذنيه جب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نماز شروع فرماتے تو تکبیر کہتے پھر اپنے دونوں ہاتھ اٹھاتے یہاں تک کہ اپنے دونوں انگوٹھوں کو دونوں کانوں کے مقابل کر لیتے۔ ان دونوں حدیثوں سے ثابت ہوا کہ تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت آپ نے دونوں ہاتھ اس قدرا ٹھائے کہ کانوں کے محاذی ہو گئے۔
ہمارے مذہب کی تائید میں عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت ہاتھ اٹھانا بہرے آدمی کو نماز شروع ہونے کی اطلاع دینے کے لئے ہے اور یہ اطلاع اس طریقہ کے ساتھ ہو گی جو ہم نے کہا یعنی کانوں تک ہاتھ اٹھانے کے ساتھ کیونکہ جب امام کانوں تک ہاتھ لائے گا تو بہرہ آدمی جان لے گا کہ تکبیر کہی گئی لہذا وہ خود بھی تکبیر کہہ کر نماز شروع کر دے گا۔ اعتراض: اگر یہ اعتراض کیا جائے کہ تکبیر کے وقت ہاتھ اٹھانا اگر بہرے آدمی کو باخبر کرنے کے لئے ہے تو منفر د کانوں تک ہاتھ نہ
Hands should be raised to the earlobes or to the shoulders... Statements of the jurists. And he raises his hands such that his thumbs align with his earlobes, and according to al-Shafi'i he raises them to his shoulders, and this difference applies to the takbir of qunut, Eid, and Janazah. He has the hadith of Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi who said: The Prophet (ﷺ) when he said takbir raised his hands to his shoulders. The signaling to the deaf is what we have said, and what he narrated is interpreted as a case of excuse. And we have the narration of Wa'il ibn Hujr, al-Bara', and Anas that the Prophet (ﷺ) when he said takbir raised his hands up to his ears. And because raising the hand... [Page 30] Chapter of Description of Prayer. Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume One. Translation: And he raises his two hands until he aligns his two thumbs with his two earlobes. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i he raises them to his two shoulders, and on this difference are the takbir of qunut, the takbir of the two Eids, and the takbir of Janazah. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi (رضي الله عنه) who said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) when he said takbir raised his two hands to his two shoulders. And our proof is the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr, al-Bara', and Anas (رضي الله عنهم) that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) when he said takbir raised his two hands up to his two ears, and because raising the hand is to inform the deaf person, and that is done in the manner we said, and the hadith that Abu Humaid narrated is interpreted as a case of excuse. Explanation of the issue: At the time of takbir al-tahrimah, he should raise his two hands such that the two thumbs align with the two earlobes. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik said he should raise to the shoulders, and this is one narration from Imam Ahmad. This same difference applies to the raising of hands at the takbir of qunut, the two Eids, and Janazah. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: the hadith of Abu Humaid from Muhammad ibn 'Amr ibn 'Ata' that he was sitting with a group of the Prophet's companions, and they mentioned the prayer of the Messenger of Allah, so Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi said: I am the one among you who remembers the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ). I saw him when he said takbir he placed his hands up to his shoulders. (Bukhari) Muhammad ibn 'Amr ibn 'Ata' narrated: ... The author of al-Hidayah mentioned this hadith with these words: 'kana an-nabiyyu sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam idha kabbara rafa'a yadayhi ila mankibayhi'. From both these hadiths it is established that the Prophet (ﷺ) used to raise his hands to his shoulders at takbir al-tahrimah. Our proof is the hadith that Wa'il ibn Hujr, al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, and Hadrat Anas (رضي الله عنهم) narrated: 'an-nabiyya sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam kana idha kabbara rafa'a yadayhi hidda'a udhunayhi' meaning the Prophet (ﷺ) when he said takbir raised his two hands up to his ears. (Hakim) And Dar Qutni narrated from Hadrat Anas (رضي الله عنه) this hadith with these words: 'kana Rasulu Allahi sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam idha iftataha as-salah kabbara thumma rafa'a yadayhi hatta yuhadhi ibhamahu udhunayhi'. From both these hadiths it is established that at takbir al-tahrimah he raised his hands so much that they aligned with his ears. In support of our madhhab, there is a rational proof: raising hands at takbir al-tahrimah is to inform the deaf person about the start of prayer, and this information will be done in the manner we stated, i.e., by raising hands to the ears, because when the imam brings his hands to his ears, the deaf person will know that takbir has been said, so he will also say takbir and begin prayer. Objection: If it is objected that raising hands at the time of takbir is to inform the deaf person, then a person praying alone would not raise hands to the ears...
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school (and Maliki and one narration of Ahmad) and the Shafi'i school regarding the height to which hands should be raised at takbir al-tahrimah. The commentator first presents the Hanafi position: hands are raised so that the thumbs align with the earlobes. The Shafi'i position is to raise them to the shoulders. This difference applies also to takbirs in qunut, Eid, and Janazah prayers. The proof for the Shafi'i position is the hadith of Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi recorded in Bukhari, which states that the Prophet raised his hands to his shoulders. The Hanafi proof consists of: (1) hadiths from Wa'il ibn Hujr, al-Bara', and Anas that the Prophet raised his hands to his ears; (2) a rational argument that raising hands is to signal to the deaf person who might be behind the imam, and the most effective signal is raising to the ears, as the deaf person can see the hands at ear level. The hadith of Abu Humaid is interpreted as referring to a situation of excuse (e.g., when the imam is in a crowded place or has a reason not to raise fully). The author of Hidayah clarifies that the disputed issue is specifically the height, and the practical consequence is which sunnah to follow. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is to raise to the ears.

Key Terms
شحمة الأذن (shahmat al-udhun): The soft lower part of the ear (earlobe). Used as the marker for the height of hand raising in Hanafi fiqh.
منكب (mankib): Shoulder; the joint between arm and torso. Used as the reference by Shafi'is.
إعلام الأصم (i'lam al-asamm): Signaling to the deaf person; the rational basis for raising hands to ears so the deaf can see the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, to what height should a person raise his hands when saying takbir al-tahrimah?
A) To the shoulders
B) To the chin
C) Until the thumbs align with the earlobes
D) Until the hands are above the head

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school raises hands to the ears for takbir, based on multiple hadiths and a rational argument; the Shafi'i school raises to shoulders, and both are valid sunnah practices.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Raising Hands to Ears During Takbir al-Tahrimah
Explains Hanafi view on raising hands to ears with proofs and response to Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during takbir al-tahrimah, explain the Hanafi proof (naqli and aqli), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Prophet raised hands to his ears; the raising to shoulders was due to an excuse like cold weather.

The opening takbir is a key pillar of prayer, and the manner of raising hands is a well-known difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This lesson examines the Hanafi position that a man raises his hands until his thumbs align with his earlobes, the evidence from hadith and rational analogy, and the response to the Shafi'i view based on the hadith of Abu Humayd. We also explore the reconciliation offered by later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Recognize that the act is raising hands during takbir al-tahrimah, and the dispute is about the level: ears vs shoulders.
The same dispute applies to takbirs of qunut, Eid, and janazah.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its proof
The Hanafi ruling is to raise hands to the ears (thumbs at earlobes). Proof: hadiths of Wa'il ibn Hujr, Bara', and Anas stating the Prophet raised hands opposite his ears. Also a rational argument: raising hands is to inform a deaf person, best achieved by raising to ears.
The rational argument helps understand the wisdom behind the ruling.
3
Identify the Shafi'i ruling and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Malik, one narration from Ahmad) holds that hands are raised to the shoulders. Their proof is the hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi that the Prophet raised his hands to his shoulders.
This hadith is found in Sahih al-Bukhari.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response interprets Abu Humayd's hadith as being due to an excuse (e.g., cold weather causing thick clothing), as evidenced by Wa'il ibn Hujr's observation. Alternatively, a reconciliation: the word 'hand' includes the forearm, so the palm is at ear level while the arm is at shoulder level.
This shows how apparent contradictions are resolved within the Hanafi methodology.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in Hanafi mosques, worshippers raise hands to ears; in Shafi'i mosques, to shoulders. Both are valid according to their respective schools.
Understanding this difference fosters tolerance of legitimate ikhtilaf.

Chapter: Description of Prayer. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume one. Translation: And he raises his both hands until he makes his thumbs opposite the lobes of his ears. And according to Imam Shafi'i, he raises them to his shoulders, and on this same difference is the takbir of qunut, the takbir of the two Eids, and the takbir of janazah. The proof of Imam Shafi'i is the hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: When the Prophet, peace be upon him, said the takbir, he raised his hands to his shoulders. And our proof is the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr, Bara', and Anas, may Allah be pleased with them, that when the Prophet, peace be upon him, said the takbir, he used to raise his hands opposite his ears; and because raising the hands is for informing a deaf person, and this will be in the manner we have stated. And the hadith that Abu Humayd narrated will be interpreted as due to an excuse. Explanation: The ruling is that at the time of takbir al-tahrimah, he should raise his hands such that both thumbs become level with the lobes of the ears. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik said: raise to the shoulders; and one narration from Imam Ahmad is similar. This same difference applies to raising hands during the takbir of qunut, Eid, and janazah. The proof of Imam Shafi'i is the hadith of Abu Humayd: from Muhammad ibn 'Amr ibn 'Ata' that he was sitting with a group of the Prophet's companions, and they mentioned the prayer of the Messenger of Allah. Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi said: I am the most knowledgeable of you regarding the prayer of the Messenger of Allah; I saw that when he said the takbir, he placed his hands level with his shoulders. (Bukhari). The author of al-Hidayah mentioned this hadith with these words: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, when he said the takbir, raised his hands to his shoulders.' From both these hadiths it is established that the Prophet used to raise both hands to the shoulders at the time of takbir al-tahrimah. Our proof is the hadith narrated by Wa'il ibn Hujr, Bara' ibn 'Azib, and Anas, may Allah be pleased with them, that when the Prophet said the takbir, he raised his hands opposite his ears. (Hakim) And al-Daraqutni narrated from Anas with these words: 'When the Messenger of Allah began the prayer, he said the takbir then raised his hands until his thumbs were opposite his ears.' From both these hadiths it is established that at the time of takbir al-tahrimah, he raised his hands so that they were level with the ears. Supporting our school is a rational proof: raising hands at takbir al-tahrimah is to inform a deaf person that prayer has started, and this information is given in the manner we have stated, i.e., by raising hands to the ears, because when the imam brings his hands to the ears, the deaf person will know that the takbir has been said, so he too will say the takbir and begin prayer. Objection: If it is objected that if raising hands at takbir is to inform a deaf person, then a person praying alone should not raise hands to the ears because this cause is not present in his case. Reply: The answer is that the original is to pray in congregation; Allah says, 'And bow with those who bow.' So a lonely person's prayer is rare, and a rare thing is not considered, because the principle is: 'The rare is like non-existent.' Difficulty: But then there is a difficulty: if so, then for a follower (muqtadi) there is no need to raise hands to the ears. Reply: It is possible that the deaf person is in the last row and cannot see the imam, so in such a case he will start prayer by seeing those followers in front of him; therefore for the followers too, it is necessary to raise hands to the ears. The author of al-Hidayah said that the hadith of Abu Humayd presented by Imam Shafi'i is interpreted as being due to an excuse. Thus it is narrated from Wa'il ibn Hujr that he said: I came to Madinah and found them raising their hands to the ears; then I came to them the next year, and they were wearing cloaks and hoods due to severe cold, and I found them raising their hands to the shoulders. Wa'il ibn Hujr made clear in this hadith that their confining to raising hands to the shoulders was due to their clothing. So it is known that the hadith 'to the shoulders' is interpreted as due to an excuse. The author of Sharh al-Nuqayah reconciled between the two hadiths in this manner: that the word 'hand' applies to the palm and the part above it; so it is possible that the edge of the forearm and the upper arm are opposite the shoulders, while the actual palm is at the level of the ears. Now there is no contradiction between the two narrations.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the position of raising hands during the opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah) in prayer. The Hanafi school holds that a man should raise his hands until his thumbs are aligned with his earlobes. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that he should raise them to his shoulders; one narration from Imam Ahmad agrees. The same difference applies to raising hands during the takbirs of qunut, Eid, and janazah. The author presents the proofs of both sides. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Abu Humayd al-Sa'idi, which states that the Prophet raised his hands to his shoulders. The Hanafi proof consists of multiple hadiths: those of Wa'il ibn Hujr, Bara' ibn 'Azib, and Anas ibn Malik, which state that the Prophet raised his hands opposite his ears. Additionally, a rational argument is given: raising hands is to inform a deaf person of the commencement of prayer, and the most effective way is to raise them to the ears, as this is a visible signal. The passage then addresses objections: (1) If it is for a deaf person, why does a person praying alone raise his hands? The reply is that the original practice is congregation; solitary prayer is rare and not considered normative. (2) If the deaf person is in the back row, he might not see the imam but can see those in front, so followers also need to raise hands to the ears. The author then resolves the apparent contradiction between the two sets of hadiths: the hadith of raising to shoulders is interpreted as being due to an excuse (such as severe cold or thick clothing), as reported by Wa'il ibn Hujr. Finally, a reconciliation by the author of Sharh al-Nuqayah is provided: the word 'hand' can include the forearm, so it is possible that the upper part of the arm is at shoulder level while the palm is at ear level, eliminating any contradiction.

Key Terms
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during the opening takbir of prayer.
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates the prayer and prohibits (tuharrim) worldly actions.
محاذی (muhadhi): Opposite or level with; used for the thumbs being level with the earlobes.

Women Raising Hands to Shoulders During Takbir
States the Hanafi ruling for women's hand-raising, with a brief intra-madhhab difference and justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for women's hand-raising during the opening takbir and explain the reason for the preferred position based on modesty.

Core Idea
A woman raises hands to shoulders for greater modesty; this is the relied-upon Hanafi opinion.

While both men and women raise their hands during the opening takbir, the Hanafi school differentiates the position based on the principle of modesty (satr). The source clearly states the correct (sahih) position: a woman raises her hands to her shoulders. It also mentions a weaker narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that allows raising to the ears, but the relied-upon view is the shoulders. Understanding this ruling helps women follow the sunnah appropriately and enhances their prayer experience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Pinpoint that the act is raising the hands during takbir al-tahrimah. The ruling for women is sunnah (recommended) by consensus, but the specific manner differs from men.
2
State the Preferred Position
The correct (sahih) position is that a woman raises her hands to her shoulders, not to her ears. This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the school.
3
Note the Intra-Hanafi Difference
A narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Abu Hanifa said a woman raises to her ears, like a man, because the palm is not ‘awrah. However, this is a weaker (nawadir) transmission.
The reason for the weaker view: raising hands is actualized by the palms, and a woman's palms are not ‘awrah, so she is equal to a man.
4
Understand the Reason for the Preference
The preferred view (shoulders) is based on modesty: it is more concealing (astar) for the woman. This aligns with the general Hanafi emphasis on covering for women in prayer.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice, a woman should raise her hands to shoulder height. If she raises to her ears, her prayer is still valid because the act remains sunnah, but she has not followed the preferred sunnah.

And the woman raises her hands opposite her shoulders; this is correct, because it is more concealing for her. Translation: And a woman raises her hands opposite her shoulders; this is correct, because this method is more concealing for a woman. Explanation: At the time of takbir al-tahrimah, a woman raises her hands to her shoulders; this is the correct statement. And Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam A'zam (Abu Hanifa) that a woman raises her hands to her ears. The reason for Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration is that raising the hands is actualized by the palms, and it has passed earlier that a woman's palm is not 'awrah (i.e., it can be uncovered). So in raising hands to the ears, woman and man are equal. And the reason for the correct statement is that raising hands to the shoulders is more concealing for a woman, so for a woman raising hands to the shoulders is appropriate.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement specific to women: during the opening takbir, a woman should raise her hands to her shoulders, not to her ears. The text states that this is the correct (sahih) position, and the reason given is modesty—it is more concealing (astar laha). There is a minority intra-Hanafi transmission from Hasan ibn Ziyad that a woman raises her hands to the ears like a man, based on the fact that a woman's palms are not 'awrah, so the same rule applies. However, the relied-upon position (the 'sahih qawl') is that she raises to the shoulders because it is more modest. The commentary explains that the correct view prioritizes modesty for women in prayer, which is consistent with the Hanafi school's emphasis on covering and concealment for women during worship.

Key Terms
ستر (satr): Concealment or modesty; here it means the action of covering oneself more completely.
قول صحیح (qawl sahih): The correct or relied-upon opinion within the school.

Hanafi Response on Raising Hands and Ruling for Women
Hanafi inter-madhhab dispute on raf' al-yadayn with Shafi'is and ruling for women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on raising hands in prayer (raf' al-yadayn) and distinguish the ruling for men and women, citing the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr and the principle of modesty.

Core Idea
The sunnah for men is to raise hands to ears; for women to shoulders—based on the maxim that rare excuses do not change the norm.

This passage addresses an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the level of raising hands in takbirat al-ihram. The author defends the Hanafi view that men raise to ears and women to shoulders, using prophetic narrations and legal reasoning. You will learn how the Hanafi school responds to the Shafi'i proof and how the ruling for women is derived from the principle of modesty.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position for men and followers
Identify what the Hanafi school holds: men raise hands to ears; followers also raise to ears, even behind the imam.
The maxim 'al-nadir ka'l-ma'dum' supports that rare exceptions do not override the norm.
2
Identify the opposing Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school cites the hadith of Abu Hamid al-Sa'idi that the Prophet raised hands to the shoulders.
This hadith appears in several collections.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi response uses the narration of Wa'il ibn Hujr, which shows that shoulder-level raising was due to severe cold (an excuse), not the norm.
The legal principle: a practice under duress does not abrogate the general rule.
4
Understand the reconciliation of narrations
Author of 'Sharh al-Niqayah' reconciled by noting that 'hand' includes palm and forearm, so the palm can be at ears while the wrist is at shoulders.
This eliminates any apparent contradiction.
5
Apply the ruling for women based on modesty
Women raise hands to the shoulders, not ears, because it is more concealing (astar). This is the correct view (huwa al-sahih), though a weak narration from Abu Hanifa says ears.
The mufta bihi is shoulder-level for women.
