ترجمہ اور عورت اپنے دونوں ہاتھ اٹھائے اپنے مونڈھوں کے مقابل یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ یہ طریقہ عورت کے لئے زیادہ پردہ کا ہے۔ تشریح تکبیر تحریمہ کے وقت عورت اپنے مونڈھوں تک ہاتھ اٹھائے صحیح قول یہی ہے اور حسن بن زیاد نے امام اعظم سے روایت کی کہ عورت اپنے ہاتھ کانوں تک اٹھائے روایت حسن بن زیاد کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ رفع یدین ہتھیلیوں سے متحقق ہوتا ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ عورت کی تھیلی عورت نہیں ہے پس کانوں تک ہاتھ اٹھانے میں عورت اور مرد دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اور قول صحیح کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مونڈھوں تک ہاتھ اٹھانے میں عورت کے واسطے زیادہ پردہ ہے اس لئے عورت کے واسطے مونڈھوں تکہ ہاتھ اٹھا نا مناسب ہے۔
He raises because this cause is not found in his case. Answer: The answer to this is that the original is to perform (prayer) with congregation; the divine command is: 'Bow with those who bow' (Quran 2:43). So performing prayer in an exceptional manner is rare (nadir), and the rule is that the rare is like non-existent. Objection: Then there is an objection that if so, then for a follower (muqtadi) there is no need to raise hands to the ears. Answer: It is possible that a deaf person may be in the last row and cannot see the imam; in such a case he will start prayer only by looking at those ahead of him, so raising hands to the ears is necessary for followers as well. The author of Hidayah said that the hadith of Abu Hamid presented by Imam Shafi'i is interpreted as a situation of excuse. Indeed, it is narrated from Wa'il ibn Hujr that he said: 'I came to Madinah and found them raising their hands to the ears. Then I came to them the following year and they were wearing cloaks and hoods due to severe cold, and I found them raising their hands to the shoulders.' Wa'il ibn Hujr (may Allah be pleased with him) explained that these people's restricting to raising hands to the shoulders was due to their clothing. So it became clear that the hadith 'to the shoulders' is interpreted as a situation of excuse. The author of Sharh al-Niqayah reconciled between the two hadiths in this way: that the word 'hand' (yad) applies to the palm and above, so it is possible that the edge of the palm and the wrist are opposite the shoulders while the palm itself is in line with the ears; thus there is no contradiction between the two narrations. A woman raises her hands to the level of her shoulders. And the woman raises her hands to the level of her shoulders; this is the correct view, because it is more concealing for her. Translation: And a woman raises her hands to the level of her shoulders; this is correct, because this method is more covering for her. Explanation: At the time of takbirat al-ihram, a woman raises her hands to her shoulders; this is the correct saying. And Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam A'zam that a woman raises her hands to her ears; the reason for the narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad is that raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) is realized with the palms, and it has passed earlier that a woman's palm is not 'awrah; thus in raising hands to the ears, women and men are equal. And the reason for the correct saying is that raising hands to the shoulders is more concealing for a woman, so raising hands to the shoulders is suitable for a woman.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the method of raising hands in prayer (raf' al-yadayn), followed by the specific ruling for women. The author first presents a response to an objection: some argue that followers (muqtadis) do not need to raise hands because they rely on the imam's action. However, the Hanafi response, based on the Quranic command to 'bow with those who bow,' establishes that congregational prayer is the norm, and an exceptional situation (like not seeing the imam) is considered rare (nadir) and thus disregarded as per the legal maxim 'al-nadir ka'l-ma'dum' (the rare is like non-existent). Then the author addresses the hadith of Abu Hamid al-Sa'idi, which Imam Shafi'i uses to argue for raising hands only to the shoulders. The Hanafi response, via the narration of Wa'il ibn Hujr, explains that the people in that hadith raised to shoulders due to severe cold and thick clothing—an excuse. Thus, the general practice is to raise to the ears. Additionally, a reconciliation by Sharh al-Niqayah suggests that the hand is a comprehensive term including palm and forearm, so the palm can be at ears while the edge at shoulders. Finally, the passage gives the Hanafi ruling for women: they raise hands to the shoulders, not the ears, based on the principle of modesty (sitr). This is the correct view (huwa al-sahih), although Hasan ibn Ziyad transmitted a narration from Abu Hanifa that women also raise to ears. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is the shoulder-level due to greater concealment.

Key Terms
رفع الیدین (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands at the beginning of prayer (takbirat al-ihram) and at other times like bowing and standing up.
المقتدی (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind the imam.
النادر کالمعدوم (al-nadir ka'l-ma'dum): A legal maxim meaning that a rare occurrence is treated as non-existent in legal rulings.

Key Takeaway

Valid Substitutes for Takbirat al-Ihram: The Four Imams' Views
Dispute on valid substitute phrases for Allahu Akbar in prayer opening

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the four imams on valid substitute phrases for the opening takbir, identify the Hanafi position, and explain the linguistic and scriptural arguments behind each view.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, any glorification opens prayer; for Malik, only 'Allahu Akbar' is valid.

The takbirat al-ihram is the opening phrase of every prayer. But what if a person says something else? The four imams differed on whether substitutions are allowed. This passage presents their arguments, with the Hanafi school taking the broadest view, grounded in the linguistic meaning of takbir as glorification.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
The issue is whether phrases other than 'Allahu Akbar' are valid for the opening takbir in prayer.
The core question: permissible substitutions.
2
List each imam's position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa & Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, al-Shafi'i, and Malik. Note the number of phrases allowed.
Malik: 1; Shafi'i: 2; Abu Yusuf: 3; Abu Hanifa & Muhammad: any glorification.
3
Examine the proofs
For each imam, note their dalil: Malik cites tawqif (restriction to transmitted words); Shafi'i cites the emphasis added by 'al-'; Abu Yusuf cites equivalence of af'alu and fa'il forms; Abu Hanifa & Muhammad cite the linguistic meaning of takbir.
Hanafi proof is linguistic (dalil aqli).
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi may begin prayer with 'Allah Ajall' or 'Subhanallah', while a Maliki would need to repeat the prayer if he does so.
This affects validity of prayer for followers of different schools.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text indicates the relied-upon Hanafi position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: any glorification is valid.
This is the fatwa position in the Hanafi school.

ترجمہ پھر اگر اس نے تکبیر کے بدلے اللہ اجل یا اللہ اعظم کہا یا الرحمن اكبر يا لا اله الا اللہ یا اس کے علاوہ اللہ تعالی کے اسماء میں سے ( کوئی اور اسم لایا ) تو طرفین کے نزدیک کافی ہے اور ابو یوسف نے ساتھ جائز ہے کیونکہ یہی منقول ہے اور اصل اس میں توقیف ہے۔ اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ الف اور لام کا داخل کرنا شاء میں زیادہ مبالغہ کرتا ہے تو الا کبر اکبر کے قائم مقام ہوا۔ اور ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ انعل اور فعیل اللہ تعالے کے صفات میں برابر ہیں۔ بر خلاف اس کے جب وہ شخص اچھی طرح نہیں کہہ سکتا کیونکہ وہ صرف معنی پر قادر ہے اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تکبیر لغت میں تعظیم کا نام ہے اور یہ تعظیم حاصل ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں افتتاح کے الفاظ کا بیان ہے چنانچہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہر اس لفظ سے نماز شروع کرنا جائز ہے جو اللہ تعالیٰ کی تعظیم پر دلالت کرے خواہ اللہ اکبر ہویا اللہ الاب يا الله الكبير يا الله اجل يا الله اعظم یا الرحمن اكبر يالا اله الا الله يا الحمد الله ياسبحان اللہ یا اللہ کے اسماء میں سے اور کسی اسم سے شروع کرے سب جائز ہے امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اگر اچھی طرح تکبیر کہنے پر قادر ہو تو صرف تین الفاظ ( الله اكبر الله الاكبر الله الكبير ) میں سے کسی ایک لفظ کے ساتھ نماز شروع کرنا جائز ہے ان کے علاوہ کسی لفظ کے ساتھ جائز نہیں ہے۔ ساتھ جائز ہے یہی امام احمد بن حنبل کا قول ہے۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ صرف اللہ اکبر اور اللہ الاکبر کے ساتھ شروع کرنا جائز ہے اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ فقط اللہ اکبر کے امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے صرف اللہ اکبر منقول ہے۔ اور اصل اس میں توقیف ہے یعنی شمارع علیہ السلام کا واقف کرانا اور شارع علیہ السلام سے صرف اللہ اکبر منقول ہے لہذا اس کے علاوہ دوسرے الفاظ کے ساتھ نماز شروع کرنا درست نہیں ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بلاشبہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے الله اکبر منقول ہے لیکن اللہ الاکبر الف لام کے ساتھ مفید حصر ہونے کی وجہ سے ثناء باری میں ابلغ ہے اس لئے یہ بھی اللہ اکبر کے قائم مقام ہوگا ۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی صفات میں افعل کے وزن پر اسم تفضیل اور فعیل یمعنی قاعل سب برابر ہیں کیونکہ اللہ
If instead of the takbir he says 'Allah Ajall' or 'Allah A'zam' or 'al-Rahman Akbar' or 'La ilaha illallah' or other names of Allah, it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: If he knows the takbir well, it is not valid except his saying 'Allahu Akbar' or 'Allah al-Akbar' or 'Allah al-Kabir'. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not valid except with the first two. Malik said: It is not valid except with the first, because that is what is transmitted, and the principle in this is restriction (tawqif). Al-Shafi'i says: Adding the definite article (alif lam) is more emphatic in praise, so it stands in place of 'akbar'. Abu Yusuf says: 'af'alu' and 'fa'il' are equivalent in the attributes of Allah, unlike when he does not know it well, because he is only capable of the meaning. Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) proof is that takbir linguistically means glorification, and such glorification is achieved. Translation: Then if he instead of takbir says 'Allah Ajall' or 'Allah A'zam' or 'al-Rahman Akbar' or 'La ilaha illallah' or other names of Allah, it is sufficient according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: If he can say the takbir well, it is not valid except his saying 'Allahu Akbar' or 'Allah al-Akbar' or 'Allah al-Kabir'. Imam Shafi'i said: It is only valid with the first two (Allahu Akbar and Allah al-Akbar). Imam Malik said: It is only valid with the first (Allahu Akbar) because that is what is transmitted, and the principle in this is restriction. Imam Shafi'i says: The insertion of alif lam makes the praise more emphatic, so 'Allah al-Akbar' stands in the place of 'Allahu Akbar'. Abu Yusuf says: 'af'alu' and 'fa'il' are equivalent in the attributes of Allah. Contrary to when the person cannot say it well, because he is only capable of the meaning. And the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that takbir linguistically means glorification, and such glorification is achieved. Explanation: In this statement, the words of the opening (iftitah) are discussed. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is permissible to begin prayer with every word that indicates glorification of Allah, whether 'Allahu Akbar' or 'Allah al-Akbar' or 'Allah al-Kabir' or 'Allah Ajall' or 'Allah A'zam' or 'al-Rahman Akbar' or 'La ilaha illallah' or 'al-Hamdulillah' or 'Subhanallah' or any of Allah's names. Imam Abu Yusuf said: If he is capable of saying the takbir well, then he may only begin with one of three words (Allahu Akbar, Allah al-Akbar, Allah al-Kabir); it is not valid to begin with any other word. This is also the saying of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Imam Shafi'i said: It is only valid to begin with 'Allahu Akbar' and 'Allah al-Akbar'. Imam Malik said: Only with 'Allahu Akbar'. Imam Malik's proof is that only 'Allahu Akbar' is transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him), and the principle in this is restriction (tawqif). Therefore, beginning prayer with other words is not correct. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that undoubtedly 'Allahu Akbar' is transmitted from the Prophet, but 'Allah al-Akbar' with the definite article is more emphatic in praise of Allah, so it stands in place of 'Allahu Akbar'. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that in the attributes of Allah, 'af'alu' (comparative/superlative) and 'fa'il' (active participle) are equivalent, because Allah... (text ends)
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of using phrases other than 'Allahu Akbar' for the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram). The Hanafi school's position (as held by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that any word that linguistically denotes glorification of Allah is sufficient, including 'Allah Ajall', 'Allah A'zam', 'al-Rahman Akbar', 'La ilaha illallah', etc. Their proof is that 'takbir' linguistically means 'glorification', so any phrase that conveys glorification achieves the purpose. Imam Abu Yusuf restricts this to three specific phrases: 'Allahu Akbar', 'Allah al-Akbar', and 'Allah al-Kabir', but only if the person is capable of saying the proper takbir; if not, then any glorification suffices. Imam al-Shafi'i allows only 'Allahu Akbar' and 'Allah al-Akbar', arguing that the definite article adds emphasis. Imam Malik restricts it to only 'Allahu Akbar', citing that only this is transmitted from the Prophet (tawqif). The author then elaborates in Urdu: According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, any name or phrase indicating glorification is valid; for Abu Yusuf, only three; for Shafi'i, two; for Malaki, only the first. The reasoning of each imam is provided. The passage ends with Abu Yusuf's argument that in Allah's attributes, the comparative form (af'alu) and the active participle (fa'il) are equivalent, but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbir): The phrase 'Allahu Akbar' (Allah is the Greatest), used to begin prayer and at various points.
توقیف (tawqif): Restriction to what is transmitted from the Prophet (revealed or sunnah), not allowing qiyas or personal opinion.
اسم تفضیل (ism tafdil): Comparative/superlative noun form in Arabic (e.g., 'akbar', 'ajall').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, if someone starts prayer by saying 'Allah Ajall' (Allah is more Majestic) instead of 'Allahu Akbar', is the prayer valid?
A) Yes, because it is a word of glorification
B) No, only 'Allahu Akbar' is valid
C) Yes, only if the person cannot say 'Allahu Akbar'
D) No, only 'Allahu Akbar' and 'Allah al-Akbar' are valid

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, any word of glorification can substitute for 'Allahu Akbar' in the opening takbir, reflecting the linguistic meaning of takbir.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Substitution of Divine Names for Allahu Akbar in Opening Takbir
Presents the ruling on using alternative phrases for the opening takbir according to various imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on alternative opening takbir phrases, identify the proofs of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, al-Shafi'i, and Malik, and explain the practical differences (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Takbir is valid with any word of glorification—meaning over form.

The opening takbir is the first pillar of prayer, but must it be the exact phrase 'Allahu Akbar'? Classical Hanafi scholarship debated this question extensively. This lesson unpacks the inter-madhhab dispute and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf. You will see how linguistic analysis, Quranic evidence, and the principle of tawqif shape each school's ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: any expression indicating glorification suffices for the opening takbir. Note that this is based on the linguistic meaning of takbir.
This position is broader than that of other schools.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
State Abu Yusuf's restriction to three specific Arabic phrases if the person can say them. Understand his argument that af'al and fa'il are equal in Allah's attributes.
3
Analyse the inter-madhhab proofs
Examine the proofs of al-Shafi'i (only 'Allahu Akbar' and 'Allahu al-Akbar') based on more emphatic praise, and Malik (only 'Allahu Akbar') based on tawqif. Compare with the Hanafi linguistic proof from Quran.
4
Trace the argument from the Quranic verses
See how verses 74:3 and 12:31 are used to show that takbir means glorification, achieved by any word of glorification. Understand the wajh al-dalalah.
5
Determine the thamarah and the mufta bihi
Identify the practical consequence: what phrases can be used in each school. Conclude that the Hanafi relied-upon position is the broader view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
This view allows maximum flexibility in worship.

باب صفۃ الصلوة

فان قال بدل التكبير الله اجل او اعظم او الرحمن اكبر او لا اله الا الله او غيره من اسماء الله تعالى اجزاء عند ابي حنيفة و محمد وقال ابويوسف ان كان يحسن التكبير لم يجز الا قوله الله اكبر او الله الأكبر او الله الكبير وقال الشافعى لا يجوز الا بالاولين وقال مالك لا يجوز الا بالاول لانه هو المنقول والأصل في التوقيف والشافعي يقول ادخال الالف واللام ابلغ فى الثناء فقام مقامه وابويوسف يقول ان افعل وفعيلا في صفات الله تعالى سواء بخلاف ما اذا كان لا يحسن لانه لايقدر الا على المعنى ولهما ان التكبير هو التعظيم لغة وهو حاصل

ترجمہ پھر اگر اس نے تکبیر کے بدلے اللہ اجل یا اللہ اعظم کہا یا الرحمن اكبر يا لا اله الا اللہ یا اس کے علاوہ اللہ تعالی کے اسماء میں سے ( کوئی اور اسم لایا ) تو طرفین کے نزدیک کافی ہے اور ابو یوسف نے کے ساتھ جائز ہے کیونکہ یہی منقول ہے اور اصل اس میں توقیف ہے۔ اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ الف اور لام کا داخل کرنا ثناء میں زیادہ مبالغہ کرتا ہے تو الاكبر اكبر کے قائم مقام ہوا۔ اور ابو یوسف فرماتے دلیل یہ ہے کہ بلاشبہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے الله اکبر منقول ہے لیکن اللہ الاكبر الف لام کے ساتھ مفید حصر ہونے کی وجہ سے ثناء باری میں ابلغ ہے اس لئے یہ بھی اللہ اکبر کے قائم مقام ہوگا ۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی صفات میں افعل کے وزن پر اسم تفضیل اور فعیل بمعنی فاعل سب برابر ہیں کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کی صفات میں زیادتی ثابت کرنا مراد نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے کہ اصل کبریائی میں اللہ تعالیٰ جل شانہ کا کوئی مساوی نہیں یہاں تک کہ افعل کے صیغہ کو زیادتی کے لئے قرار دیا جائے جیسا کہ بندوں کے اوصاف میں ہوتا ہے لہذا افعل اور فعیل صفات باری میں دونوں برابر ہوں گے اس کے برخلاف اگر وہ شخص اچھی طرح تکبیر نہیں کہہ سکتا تو جس طرح اس سے ہو سکے تعظیم کے معنی ادا کردے کیونکہ یہ شخص صرف معنی پر قادر ہے الفاظ تکبیر پر قادر نہیں ۔ طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لغت میں تکبیر کے معنی تعظیم کے ہیں باری تعالٰی کا قول ہے وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبِّرْ یعنی بڑا کر اور فَلَمَّا رَأَيْنَهُ أَكْبَرْنَهُ یعنی اس نے بڑی تعظیم کی اور تعظیم کے معنی ان تمام الفاظ سے حاصل ہو جاتے ہیں جو ہم نے ذکر کئے ہیں اس لئے نماز کا افتتاح ہر اس لفظ سے ہو سکتا ہے جو اللہ کی تعظیم پر دلالت کرے۔
Chapter on the description of prayer. If instead of the takbir he says 'Allah ajall' or 'Allah a'zam' or 'al-Rahman akbar' or 'la ilaha illa Allah' or other names of Allah, it suffices according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: if he knows the takbir well, nothing suffices except his saying 'Allahu Akbar' or 'Allahu al-Akbar' or 'Allahu al-Kabir'. Al-Shafi'i said: it is not permissible except with the first two. Malik said: it is not permissible except with the first, because it is the transmitted (word) and the principle in this is restriction (tawqif). Al-Shafi'i says: inserting 'alif lam' is more emphatic in praise, so it takes its place. Abu Yusuf says: 'af'al' and 'fa'il' in the attributes of Allah are the same, contrary to when he does not know (the takbir) because he is only able (to convey) the meaning. And the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that takbir linguistically means glorification, and that is achieved. Translation (Urdu): Then if he substitutes for the takbir and says 'Allah ajall' or 'Allah a'zam' or 'al-Rahman akbar' or 'la ilaha illa Allah' or any other name from the names of Allah, it is sufficient according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said that if he can say the takbir well, it is not permissible except with his saying 'Allahu Akbar' or 'Allahu al-Akbar' or 'Allahu al-Kabir'. Imam al-Shafi'i said that only the first two phrases are permissible. Imam Malik said that only the first phrase is permissible because it alone is transmitted and the principle in this is restriction. Imam al-Shafi'i says that inserting 'alif lam' in praise is more emphatic, so 'al-Akbar' takes the place of 'Akbar'. Abu Yusuf says that 'af'al' and 'fa'il' are equal in the attributes of Allah. Contrary to when the person cannot say it well, because he is only able to convey the meaning. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that takbir linguistically means glorification, and that glorification is achieved. Explanation: This phrase explains the words of the opening (of prayer). According to the two sides, it is permissible to start prayer with any word that indicates glorification of Allah, whether 'Allahu Akbar', 'Allahu al-Akbar', 'Allahu al-Kabir', 'Allah Ajal', 'Allah A'zam', 'al-Rahman Akbar', 'la ilaha illa Allah', 'al-Hamdu lillah', 'Subhan Allah', or any other name of Allah; all are permissible. Imam Abu Yusuf said that if he can say the takbir well, it is only permissible to start prayer with one of three phrases: 'Allahu Akbar', 'Allahu al-Akbar', 'Allahu al-Kabir'; with any other phrase it is not permissible. This is also the saying of Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal. Imam al-Shafi'i said that starting prayer is only permissible with 'Allahu Akbar' and 'Allahu al-Akbar'. Imam Malik said only with 'Allahu Akbar'. Imam Malik's proof is that only 'Allahu Akbar' is transmitted from the Prophet (peace be upon him), and the principle in this is restriction (tawqif). Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that undoubtedly 'Allahu Akbar' is transmitted, but 'Allahu al-Akbar' with 'alif lam' is more emphatic in praise of Allah, so it takes the place of 'Allahu Akbar'. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that in Allah's attributes, the patterns 'af'al' (superlative) and 'fa'il' (active participle) are all equal because in Allah's attributes, no increase is intended; since in His original greatness no one is equal to Him, the 'af'al' form is not used to indicate superiority as in human attributes; therefore 'af'al' and 'fa'il' are equal in attributes of Allah. In contrast, if the person cannot say the takbir well, he should convey the meaning of glorification as best he can, because he is only able (to convey) the meaning, not the exact words. The proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that takbir linguistically means glorification. Allah says: 'And your Lord magnify' (Quran 74:3) meaning glorify, and 'When they saw him, they magnified him' (Quran 12:31) meaning they greatly glorified him. The meaning of glorification is achieved by all the words we have mentioned, so the opening of prayer can be done with any word that indicates glorification of Allah.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of substituting other divine names or phrases for the standard 'Allahu Akbar' when beginning the prayer. The base ruling: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, any expression that conveys the meaning of glorifying Allah suffices for the opening takbir. Abu Yusuf restricts this to three specific Arabic phrases if the person is capable of saying 'Allahu Akbar' correctly; if incapable, any phrase in any language suffices. Imam al-Shafi'i allows only 'Allahu Akbar' and 'Allahu al-Akbar', while Imam Malik permits only 'Allahu Akbar'. The commentator (Ashraf Ul Hadaya) then provides the reasoning behind each position. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad base their view on the linguistic meaning of takbir as glorification, supported by Quranic verses (Surah al-Muddaththir 74:3 and Surah Yusuf 12:31). They argue that since the purpose is to express Allah's greatness, any word that achieves this meaning is valid. Abu Yusuf's distinction between 'af'al' and 'fa'il' forms in Allah's attributes is based on the principle that in the Divine, patterns indicating superiority are not relevant because Allah is incomparable; thus 'Allahu al-Kabir' and 'Allahu Akbar' are equivalent. Al-Shafi'i's acceptance of 'Allahu al-Akbar' is due to the added emphasis of the definite article, while Malik's strict restriction follows the literal transmitted practice. The passage also notes that if a person cannot recite the Arabic phrases correctly, all scholars agree that they may use any word that conveys glorification, even in non-Arabic. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as it is based on the broader linguistic and Quranic evidence.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' or any phrase that means glorification of Allah; linguistically it means 'to magnify'.
افعل (af'al): The Arabic pattern for the elative/superlative (e.g., akbar). In Allah's attributes, Abu Yusuf argues it is equivalent to fa'il (active participle) because no superiority is intended.
توقیف (tawqif): The principle that acts of worship must be based on transmitted texts (Quran and Sunnah) without personal reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), which of the following phrases is valid for the opening takbir?
A) Only 'Allahu Akbar'
B) Only 'Allahu Akbar' and 'Allahu al-Akbar'
C) Any word that means glorification of Allah, e.g., 'Allah A'zam'
D) Only Arabic phrases with the pattern 'af'al'

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is valid with any phrase that conveys glorification of Allah, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Using Persian in Prayer and Slaughter: Hanafi Positions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Persian in prayer/slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding using Persian in prayer and slaughter, identify the scriptural proofs for each, and explain the mufta bihi (operative) ruling.

Core Idea
The relied-upon Hanafi position requires Arabic for prayer recitation if capable, but allows any language for tasmiyah over slaughter.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: may a person who knows Arabic use Persian in prayer and slaughter? Abu Hanifa’s permissive view is often misunderstood as the operative ruling, but the text reports his retraction. We will unpack the proofs of the three imams and clarify the final relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage covers three acts: opening the prayer (takbir), reciting Qur'an in prayer, and saying tasmiyah over slaughter. Note each imam's ruling per scenario.
Muhammad sometimes sides with Abu Hanifa (on Arabic opening) and sometimes with Abu Yusuf (on Persian opening).
2
Trace Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa cites Quran 26:196 — the Qur'an existed in previous scriptures in non-Arabic languages, so meaning is primary. Hence, Persian suffices.
He still considers it sinful if done unnecessarily due to violating transmitted Sunnah.
3
Trace the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that 'Qur'an' is specifically Arabic composition (manzum 'Arabi). Recitation must be in Arabic; only in inability is meaning accepted (like gestures). Tasmiyah is different because it is dhikr, which is achieved in any language.
This distinction between Qur'an (Arabic text) and dhikr (any language) is key.
4
Note the reported retraction
The text states that Abu Hanifa reportedly retracted to the Sahibayn's view. The relied-upon (mu'tamad) position is therefore the Sahibayn's.
This shifts the operative ruling from permissive to restrictive for prayer acts.
5
Apply to khutbah, tashahhud, and adhan
The same difference applies to khutbah and tashahhud. For adhan, customary practice (ta'aruf) is considered rather than strict Arabic.
Adhan is not recitation; it is invocation, so local custom prevails.

Ruling on reciting in Persian, statements of jurists and proofs. If he begins the prayer in Persian or recites in it in prayer, or slaughters and says the tasmiyah in Persian while he knows Arabic, it suffices according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is not sufficient except in the case of slaughter. If he does not know Arabic, it suffices. As for the discussion on opening (the prayer), Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa regarding Arabic, and with Abu Yusuf regarding Persian, because the Arabic language has a merit that other languages lack. As for the discussion on recitation (in prayer), the proof of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the Qur'an is a name for Arabic composition, as the text declares, except that in case of inability, one is content with the meaning, like making gestures. This is contrary to the tasmiyah (saying Bismillah over slaughter), because dhikr (remembrance) is achieved in every language. And for Abu Hanifa, the proof is the verse of Allah: 'And indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples' (Quran 26:196), and it was not in this language (Arabic) in those scriptures, and for this reason it is permissible in case of inability, but he becomes sinful for violating the transmitted Sunnah. And it is permissible in any language other than Persian; this is the correct view, because of the verse we recited, and the meaning does not differ with different languages. The disagreement is regarding its being counted (as valid recitation), and there is no disagreement that it does not invalidate (the prayer). And it is reported that he (Abu Hanifa) retracted in the original issue to their view (the Sahibayn), and reliance is upon that. The khutbah and tashahhud follow this same difference, and in the adhan, custom is considered. Translation (Urdu): So if he begins prayer in Persian or recites in prayer in Persian, or slaughters an animal and says the tasmiyah in Persian while he can express in Arabic, it will be sufficient according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two (Sahibayn) said it is not permissible except in the slaughter. As for the words of opening, Imam Muhammad is with Imam Abu Hanifa in Arabic and with Imam Abu Yusuf in Persian, because Arabic has a special merit that other languages do not have. As for the discussion on recitation, the proof of the two (Sahibayn) is that the Qur'an is the name of Arabic speech, as the text declares, except that in case of inability, one is content with the meaning, as one is content with gestures. This is contrary to the tasmiyah because dhikr is achieved in every language. And the proof of Abu Hanifa is the saying of Allah: 'And indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples,' and it was not in this language (Arabic) in those scriptures, and for this reason it is permissible in case of inability, but he becomes sinful due to violating the transmitted Sunnah. And it is permissible in any language other than Persian; this is the correct saying, because of the verse we recited, and meanings do not differ due to differences in languages. The disagreement is regarding its being counted (as valid), and there is no disagreement that it does not cause invalidation. And it is narrated that Imam Abu Hanifa retracted in the original issue to the saying of the two (Sahibayn), and reliance is upon it. The khutbah and tashahhud follow this difference, and in the adhan, customary practice is considered.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the use of Persian (and by extension, non-Arabic languages) in three contexts: opening the prayer (takbir), recitation of Qur'an in prayer, and saying the tasmiyah (Bismillah) over slaughter. The ruling also applies to the khutbah, tashahhud, and adhan, though with some nuances. The central figures are Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf (qadi), and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn collectively, though Muhammad sometimes sides with Abu Hanifa). When a person is capable of Arabic: Abu Hanifa permits opening the prayer, recitation, and tasmiyah in Persian. The Sahibayn restrict this: they do not permit opening or recitation in Persian (they require Arabic), but they do permit tasmiyah in any language because the remembrance of Allah (dhikr) is achieved through any language. For recitation in prayer, Abu Hanifa relies on the verse 'Indeed it (the Qur'an) is in the scriptures of the former peoples' (Surah al-Shu'ara 26:196), arguing that the divine message was revealed in different languages in previous scriptures, so the meaning is what matters. The Sahibayn argue that the Qur'an is specifically an Arabic composition (munzam 'Arabi), as stated in texts, and therefore its recitation must be in Arabic; however, if a person is completely unable (ajz), they may substitute the meaning, similar to how a mute person gestures in prayer. In such case, Abu Hanifa agrees that non-Arabic recitation is valid but the person commits a sin for violating the transmitted Sunnah. The passage also notes that the relied-upon view (mu'tamad) is that of the Sahibayn, based on a narration that Abu Hanifa himself retracted to their position. For the adhan, the criterion is customary practice ('urf/ta'aruf), meaning it should be in the language understood by the community, not necessarily Arabic.

Key Terms
قرآن (Qur'an): The revealed scripture; according to the Sahibayn, it is specifically an Arabic composition (munzam 'Arabi) as opposed to its meaning alone.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' (In the name of Allah) over slaughter. All Hanafis agree it is valid in any language because it is dhikr.
سنت متوارثہ (sunnah mutawarithah): The continuously transmitted practice of the Prophet and the early community; deviating from it in worship is sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is valid and no sin
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
C) The prayer is valid but the person is sinful
D) The prayer is valid only if he also recites in Arabic later

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position requires Arabic for prayer recitation and opening if one is capable, but permits any language for tasmiyah over slaughter due to the distinction between Qur'anic recitation and dhikr.

Using Persian in Prayer: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Persian in worship acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on using Persian in prayer and state the mufta bihi position for a capable person.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits Persian in prayer for all; Sahibayn restrict it to inability except for tasmiyah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a person capable of Arabic may use Persian in various acts of worship, including the opening takbir, Quran recitation, and tasmiyah. The disagreement hinges on the definition of 'Quran' and the special merit of the Arabic language. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh proofs within the Hanafi school and identify the operative position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts in dispute
List the acts mentioned: opening takbir, qira'ah, tasmiyah, khutbah, tashahhud, and adhan. The dispute focuses on whether Persian suffices for a person capable of Arabic.
Note that tasmiyah has a separate ruling according to Sahibayn.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that Persian suffices for all these acts, even if one is capable of Arabic, because meaning is paramount. However, he considers it sinful (makruh tahrimi) to abandon the transmitted sunna.
He cites Quran 26:196 to show the Quran existed in meaning in previous scriptures.
3
State Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that Persian does NOT suffice for the capable person except in the case of tasmiyah, because Quran is Arabic composition and Arabic has special merit. For tasmiyah, dhikr is achieved in any language.
Imam Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa on Arabic opening (e.g., any Arabic word of tazim) but with Abu Yusuf on Persian opening.
4
Analyze the dalil
Abu Hanifa's proof is Quran 26:196: 'And indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples.' This shows that the essence of the Quran is the meaning, not the Arabic wording. Sahibayn's proof is the definition of Quran as Arabic composition and the hadith 'I am Arab...' (implied).
The dalala of the verse is zanni—it indicates meaning but does not directly permit translation in prayer.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Sahibayn: a person capable of Arabic must use Arabic for takbir, qira'ah, etc. Tasmiyah is an exception. The report that Abu Hanifa retracted to this view strengthens its authority.
Thus, for a capable person, Persian prayer is invalid in the sense that it does not fulfill the obligation (though the prayer itself is not nullified).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان افتتح الصلوة بالفارسية او قرأ فيها بالفارسية او ذبح وسمى بالفارسية وهو يحسن العربية اجزاه عند أبي حنيفة وقالا لا يجزيه الا فى الذبيحة وان لم يحسن العربية اجزاه اما الكلام فى الافتتاح فمحمد مع ابي حنيفة في العربية ومع ابي يوسف فى الفارسية لان لغة العرب لها من المزية ماليس لغيرها واما الكلام في القراءة فوجه قولهما ان القرآن اسم لمنظوم عربى كما نطق به النص الا ان عند العجز يكتفى بالمعنى كالايماء بخلاف التسمية لان الذكر يحصل بكل لسان ولابي حنيفة قوله تعالى وَإِنَّهُ لَفِی زُبُرِ الْأَوَّلِينَ ولَم يكن فيها بهذه اللغة ولهذا يجوز عند العجز الا انه يصير مسياً لمخالفة السنة المتوارثة ويجوزباى لسان كان سوى الفارسية هو الصحيح لما تلونا والمعنى لا يختلف باختلاف اللغات والخلاف في الاعتداد ولا خلاف فى انه لافساد ويروى رجوعه في اصل المسئلة الى قولهما وعليه الاعتماد والخطبة والتشهد على هذا الاختلاف وفي الاذان يعتبر التعارف
If he opens the prayer in Persian, or recites in it, or slaughters and says the tasmiyah in Persian while he is capable of Arabic, it suffices according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it does not suffice except in the case of the slaughtered animal. And if he is not capable of Arabic, it suffices. As for the discussion concerning the opening (takbir): Muhammad agrees with Abu Hanifa regarding Arabic, and with Abu Yusuf regarding Persian, because the Arabic language has a merit that others do not have. As for the discussion concerning recitation: the basis of their (Sahibayn's) statement is that 'Quran' is a name for Arabic composition, as the text (nass) clearly states. However, in the case of inability, one suffices with the meaning, like pointing (ima'), contrary to the tasmiyah because dhikr is attained in any language. And Abu Hanifa's proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'And indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples' and it was not in these scriptures in this language. Thus it is permissible in case of inability, but he becomes sinful because of opposing the transmitted sunna. And it is valid in any language other than Persian, that is the correct (view) based on what we recited, and meaning does not differ due to difference of languages. And the disagreement is concerning its validity (i'tidad), and there is no disagreement that it is not invalidating. And it is reported that he (Abu Hanifa) returned in the original issue to their statement, and upon it is reliance. And the khutbah and tashahhud follow this disagreement, and in the adhan that which is known (ta'aruf) is considered.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute examining the permissibility of using Persian (and by extension non-Arabic languages) in various acts of worship: the opening takbir of prayer, recitation of Quran, the tasmiyah upon slaughter, the khutbah, tashahhud, and adhan. The central issue is whether a person who is capable of Arabic may use Persian or another language. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is permissible in all these acts, provided that the words convey the meaning of glorification or recitation. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) restrict this permissibility only to cases where the person is incapable of Arabic, except for the tasmiyah upon slaughter, which they permit in any language because the objective there is dhikr (remembrance). The reasoning revolves around the definition of 'Quran' (is it Arabic composition or essentially meaning?) and the special merit of the Arabic language. The passage also notes that Imam Muhammad aligns with Abu Hanifa on opening takbir in Arabic (i.e., any Arabic word of glorification is acceptable) but aligns with Abu Yusuf on Persian (i.e., Persian is not acceptable if capable of Arabic). For recitation, the Sahibayn argue that Quran is defined as Arabic composition, so recitation in other languages does not fulfill the obligation except in cases of inability, similar to how a person unable to bow points. Abu Hanifa argues that the Quran existed in meaning in previous scriptures, so translation suffices. The passage concludes that the relied-upon view is that recitation in any language other than Persian (i.e., any non-Arabic language) is permissible, but the dispute is about whether it counts as valid recitation (i'tidad) for fulfilling the obligation, not about invalidating the prayer. It also mentions a report that Abu Hanifa retracted to the Sahibayn's view, and that the khutbah and tashahhud follow the same disagreement, while adhan is based on common usage (ta'aruf).

Key Terms
افتتاح (iftitah): The opening of the prayer with takbir tahrima or any word of glorification
تسمية (tasmiyah): Uttering 'Bismillah' upon slaughtering an animal
اعتداد (i'tidad): Counting or considering the act as valid for fulfilling the obligation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on using Persian for tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) upon slaughter for a person capable of Arabic?
A) It is invalid according to all.
B) It is valid according to all.
C) It is valid only according to Abu Hanifa.
D) It is valid only according to Sahibayn.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a person capable of Arabic must use Arabic for takbir and qira'ah; Persian is not sufficient except in case of inability, while tasmiyah is an exception valid in any language.

Reciting Quran in Non-Arabic During Prayer: The Hanafi Dispute
Detailed exposition of a Hanafi legal dispute with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on reciting Quran in non-Arabic during prayer and evaluate the evidence for each view.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi: non-Arabic recitation does not fulfill the obligation for one capable of Arabic.

This passage addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: can one recite the Quran in Persian (or any non-Arabic language) during prayer? Imam Abu Hanifa initially permitted it based on the meaning of the Quran, while his two primary students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, required Arabic for those capable. Later, the Imam is reported to have retracted, making the Sahibayn's view the operative ruling. Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi jurists weigh textual evidence and the role of language in devotional acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling context
The act in question is qira'ah (Quran recitation) during prayer, which is fard. The dispute is whether reciting a translation fulfills this obligation for someone capable of Arabic.
Qira'ah is a pillar (rukn) of prayer in the Hanafi school.
2
State Abu Hanifa's initial position and evidence
Abu Hanifa held that reciting in Persian (or any language) is permissible and fulfills the obligation. His evidence: (1) Quran was in earlier scriptures in meaning only (Surah al-Shu'ara 196); (2) Salman al-Farisi sent Surah Fatihah in Persian to Persians, and the Prophet did not object.
Abu Hanifa considered the Quran to be the name of meaning, not the Arabic wording.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani held that if one is capable of Arabic, reciting in non-Arabic is not permissible and does not fulfill the obligation. Their evidence: (1) Arabic has special virtue (hadith on superiority); (2) Quran is defined as an Arabic composition (Quran 12:2, 39:28).
Imam Muhammad splits on takbir: he agrees with Abu Hanifa on iftitah (any glorification) but with Abu Yusuf on takbir proper.
4
Analyze the retraction and mufta bihi
Abu Bakr al-Razi narrated that Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted to the Sahibayn's view. Later Hanafi authorities rely on this, making the Sahibayn's position the mufta bihi: non-Arabic recitation is not permissible for one capable of Arabic.
Despite the dispute, both sides agreed that prayer does not become invalid, though later some Sahibayn said it does.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Consider a person capable of Arabic who recites Surah Fatihah in English in fajr prayer. According to the mufta bihi, this does not fulfill the obligation of qira'ah; the prayer is valid but the recitation must be repeated in Arabic (or the prayer repeated). In contrast, Abu Hanifa would have considered it valid.
If the person is incapable of Arabic, all agree any language is permissible.

Source Text

باب سنة الصلوة
تشریح فارسی زبان میں نماز شروع کرنا اور نماز کے اندر فارسی میں قرآت کرنا بیجہ پر فارسی زبان میں تسمیہ کہنا مثلا بنام خدائے بزرگ سیکھ لی۔ کہنا حضرت امام اعظم کے نزدیک جائز ہے خواہ عربی زبان پر قدرت ہو یا قدرت نہ ہو۔ اور صاحبین نے کہا کہ اگر عربی زبان پر قادر ہے کہ نماز فارسی میں ادا کرنا جائز نہیں ہے البتہ ذبیحہ پر فارسی زبان میں بلکہ ہر زبان میں تسمیہ جائز ہے اور اگر عربی زبان پر قدرت نہ ہوتو فارسی میر سب جائز ہیں۔
قرآت اور تکبیر تحریمہ میں کام یہ ہے کہ حضرت امام محمد عربی زبان میں ادا کرنے میں امام ابوحنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں یعنی جس طرح امام ابوحنیفہ نزدیک ہر اس کلمہ سے نماز شروع کرنا جائز ہے جو تعظیم باری تعالی پر دلالت کرے اسی طرح امام محمد کے نزدیک بھی ہر کلمہ تعظیم کے ساتھ اجازت افتتان نماز جائز ہے اور فارسی زبان میں ادا کرنے میں امام ابو یوسف کے ساتھ ہیں حتی کہ سوائے عربی کے دوسری زبان میں تکبیر کہنا ان کو چونک۔ محمد کے نزدیک بھی نا جائز ہے حاصل یہ کہ عربی پر قدرت کی صورت میں غیر عربی میں تکبیر تحریمہ کہنا صاحبین کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے اور دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ عربی زبان کو ایک خاص فضیلت حاصل ہے جو کسی اور زبان کو حاصل نہیں ہے ۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول ہے تفضیل لسان فارسی زیاد العرب على سائر الالسنة انا عربي والقرآن عربی و لسان اهل الجنة عربی زبان عرب کو تمام زبانوں پر فضیات حاصل اختلاف ہے میں عربی ہوں، قرآن عربی ہے اور اہل جنت کی زبان عربی ہے۔ ز با کلام قرآت تو صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس چیز کا نماز میں امر کیا گیا ہے وہ قرآت قرآن ہے اور قرآن اس نظم عربی کا نام ہے؟ بارے میں معنی پر دلالت کرے اور مصاحف میں مکتوب ہے اور ہماری طرف نقل تواتر کے ساتھ منقول ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا انَّا جَعَلْنَاهُ قَران جائے گا عربیا اور فرمایا قرانًا عربيًا غير ذى عوج حاصل یہ کہ نامور پر قرآت قرآن ہے اور وہ عربی میں ہے اس لئے عربی زبان میں قرآت اگر قرآت کرنا فرض ہو گا اس کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ حالت بجز میں بھی نظم عربی کو ترک نہ کیا جائے مگر بات یہ ہے کہ بجز کے وقت معنی پر اکتفا اس لیے کیا رکوع اور سجد ہ ضروری نہیں۔ گیا تا کہ آکلیف مالا ليطلق لازم نہ آئے جیسے اگر کوئی شخص رکوع مسجدہ پر قادر نہ ہو تو اس کے لئے رکوع اور سجدے کا اشارہ کافی ہے مین کایات ابوبک میں اس ۔ بر خلاف ذبح کے وقت تسمیہ کے کہ وہ فارسی میں جائز ہے اگر چہ وہ عربی پر قدرت رکھتا ہو کیونکہ مقصود تسمیہ سے ذکر ہے۔ اللہ تعالی نے فرمایا ہے وَلَانَا كُلُوا مِمَّالَمُ يُذكر اسم اللہ علیہ اور ذکر ہر زبان میں حاصل ہو جاتا ہے خواہ عربی پر قادر ہو یا قادر نہ ہو۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرما او انه لفی زبر الاولین یعنی قرآن پہلی کتابوں میں موجود ہے اور یہ بات معلوم لوگ جاتے ہے کہ قرآن پہلی کتابوں میں نظم عربی کے ساتھ موجود نہیں تھا پر متعین ہو گیا کہ پہلی کتابوں میں اس کے معنی موجود تھے پس ثابت ہوا کہ قرآن معنی کا نام ہے نہ کہ نظم کا اور جب قرآن علی سبیل الترجمہ فارسی میں پڑ ھا جائے تو وہ اس کے معنی پر مشتمل ہونے کی وجہ سے جائز ہوگا کیونکہ قرآت قرآن پائی گئی اور چونکہ قرآن پہلی کتابوں میں نظم عربی کے ساتھ موجود نہیں تھا اس لئے نظم عربی پر عدم قدرت کے وقت فارسی زبان میں قرآت کرنا جائز ہے لیکن گنہ گار ہوگا کیونکہ اس نے سنت متوارثہ کی مخالفت کی ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل فارس نے حضرت سلمان فارسی رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کولکھا کہ ان کے لئے فارسی زبان میں سورہ فاتحہ لکھ کر بیچ فقد قي وان افتت سلمان فارسی نے فارسی زبان میں سورۃ فاتحہ لکھ کر بیچ دی وہ لوگ اس کو نماز میں پڑھتے رہے یہاں تک کہ انہوں نے عربی زبان سیکھ لی۔ سلمان فارسی نے لکھنے کے بعد رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی خدمت میں پیش کی تھی آپ نے اس پر کوئی نکیر نہیں فرمائی ۔ اس سے بھی ثابت ہوا کہ نماز میں بزبان فارسی قرآت کرنا جائز ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح فارسی زبان میں نماز کے اندر قرأت کرنا جائز ہے اسی طرح فارسی کے علاوہ ہر زبان میں قرآت جائز ہے یہی صحیح قول ہے۔
اور ابوسعید کا قول یہ ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ نے صرف فارسی زبان میں قرآت کرنا جائز قرار دیا ہے فارسی کے علاوہ دوسری زبانوں میں اجازت نہیں دی ہے وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ فارسی زبان کو عربی سے قرب ہے اس لئے فارسی میں قرآت کی اجازت دی گئی اور دوسری زبانوں کو چونکہ یہ قرب حاصل نہیں اس لئے ان میں قرآت کرنا جائز نہیں ۔ اور قول صحیح کی دلیل آیت و انه لفنى زبر الاولین ہے کیونکہ قرآن پہلی کتابوں میں جس طرح عربی زبان میں نہیں تھا اسی طرح فوری زبان میں بھی نہیں تھا۔ اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآن کو دوسری زبان میں منتقل کرتے وقت اعتماد معنی پر ہوگا اور معنی زبانوں کے اختلاف سے نہیں بدلتے لہذا تر کی بہندی وغیرہ ہر زبان میں جائز ہے۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے کہا کہ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان غیر عربی میں قرآت کے جواز و عدم جواز کا جو اختلاف ہے وہ اس بارے میں ہے کہ غیر عربی میں قرآت معتبر ہوگی یا نہیں ؟ حتی کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اگر غیر عربی میں قرآت کی تو فرض قرآت ادا ہو جائے گا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ادا نہ ہوگا۔ اور اس میں کچھ اختلاف نہیں کہ غیر عربی میں قرآت سے نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی یعنی غیر عربی میں اگر قرآت کی تو بالا تفاق نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی۔
علامہ ابن الہمام نے لکھا ہے کہ نجم الدین نسفی اور قاضی خان نے لکھا ہے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ ابو بکر رازی نے روایت کیا کہ اصل مسئلہ میں امام صاحب نے صاحبین کے قول کی طرف رجوع کیا یعنی حضرت امام اعظم بھی آخر میں اس کے قائل ہو گئے تھے کہ نماز کے اندر غیر عربی میں قرآت جائز نہیں ہے اور اس پر اعتماد ہے۔
Chapter on the description of prayer. Explanation: Beginning prayer in Persian and reciting Quran in Persian during prayer, also saying Bismillah in Persian on slaughtering, e.g. saying 'banam-e-khuda-e-buzurg' – according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is permissible whether one is capable of Arabic or not. The two companions (Sahibayn) said: If one is capable of Arabic, then performing prayer in Persian is not permissible; however, for slaughtering, saying Bismillah in Persian, indeed in any language, is permissible. If one is not capable of Arabic, then Persian etc. are all permissible. Regarding recitation and the opening takbir: Imam Muhammad agrees with Imam Abu Hanifa in that one may begin prayer with any word indicating glorification of Allah, but agrees with Imam Abu Yusuf in that reciting the takbir in a non-Arabic language is impermissible for one capable of Arabic. The summary: for one capable of Arabic, saying the opening takbir in non-Arabic is impermissible according to the Sahibayn. Their proof: the Arabic language has a special virtue not found in other languages. The Prophet said: 'I am Arab, the Quran is Arabic, and the language of the people of Paradise is Arabic; the Arabic language is superior to all languages.' Regarding recitation, the Sahibayn's proof: what is commanded in prayer is recitation of the Quran, and Quran is the name of this Arabic composition, which indicates meaning and is written in the mushafs and transmitted to us by tawatur. Allah said: 'Indeed, We have made it an Arabic Quran' and 'Arabic Quran without any crookedness.' So recitation of the Quran is required, and it is in Arabic. Therefore, if recitation is obligatory, it requires that the Arabic wording not be abandoned even in necessity, except that in necessity one suffices with meaning because bowing and prostration are not required, to avoid burdening beyond capacity, just as if a person cannot bow and prostrate, gesture is sufficient. Unlike slaughtering where saying Bismillah in Persian is permissible even if one is capable of Arabic because the purpose is remembrance. Allah said: 'Eat of that over which the name of Allah has been mentioned,' and remembrance is achieved in any language whether one is capable of Arabic or not. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof: Allah said: 'And indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples,' meaning the Quran was present in earlier books, and it is known that it was not in Arabic wording in those books, so it is established that the Quran is the name of meaning, not wording. When one recites it in Persian as a translation, it is permissible because it contains the meaning, so Quran recitation is achieved. Since it was not in Arabic wording in earlier books, reciting in Persian when unable to speak Arabic is permissible, but one will be sinful for opposing the transmitted Sunnah. Second proof: The people of Persia wrote to Salman al-Farisi asking him to write Surah Fatihah in Persian. He wrote it and sent it, and they used to recite it in prayer until they learned Arabic. He presented it to the Prophet who did not object. This proves that reciting in Persian in prayer is permissible. The author of Hidayah says: Just as reciting in Persian in prayer is permissible, similarly recitation in every language is permissible; this is the correct statement. Abu Sa'id's view: Imam Abu Hanifa only permitted Persian because of its closeness to Arabic; other languages are not allowed. The proof of the correct view is the verse 'and it is in the scriptures of the former peoples' because the Quran was not in Arabic nor in Persian in those scriptures. Another proof: when translating the Quran, reliance is on meaning, and meaning does not change with different languages, so translation into Hindi etc. is permissible in any language. The author of Hidayah said: The dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding permissibility of recitation in non-Arabic is about whether it is valid (i.e., fulfills the obligation). According to Imam, if one recites in non-Arabic, the obligatory recitation is fulfilled; according to them, it is not. There is no disagreement that recitation in non-Arabic does not invalidate the prayer. Ibn al-Humam wrote that Najm al-Din al-Nasafi and Qadi Khan wrote that according to the Sahibayn the prayer becomes invalid. Abu Bakr al-Razi narrated that Imam Abu Hanifa retracted to the view of the Sahibayn, i.e., he eventually held that recitation in non-Arabic is not permissible, and this is the relied-upon view.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This is a substantial passage detailing the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding reciting the Quran in non-Arabic languages during prayer. It begins by stating the general ruling: Imam Abu Hanifa permits beginning prayer and reciting in Persian regardless of ability in Arabic, while the Sahibayn restrict this to those who cannot speak Arabic. For slaughtering, all agree that saying Bismillah in any language is permissible because the purpose is remembrance. The passage then delves into the positions of Imam Muhammad on the opening takbir: he joins Abu Hanifa in allowing any word of glorification for beginning prayer (iftitah) but joins Abu Yusuf in disallowing non-Arabic for the takbir if one can speak Arabic. The Sahibayn's evidence is the special virtue of Arabic, a hadith stating its superiority, and that the Quran is defined as this Arabic composition. Abu Hanifa's evidence includes the verse that the Quran was in earlier scriptures in meaning only, not Arabic wording, and the incident of Salman al-Farisi sending Surah Fatihah in Persian, which the Prophet tacitly approved. The author of Hidayah affirms that permissibility extends to all languages, not just Persian. He also clarifies that the dispute is about whether non-Arabic recitation fulfills the obligatory recitation, not about the validity of prayer itself (though some later scholars report differing views). Finally, a narration from Abu Bakr al-Razi states that Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted to the Sahibayn's position, and that is the relied-upon view. Thus the operative ruling for fatwa is that recitation in non-Arabic is not permissible for one capable of Arabic.

Key Terms
قرآت (qira'ah): Recitation of the Quran during prayer, which is obligatory (fard) according to Hanafis.
تکبیر تحریمہ (takbir al-tahrimah): The opening 'Allahu Akbar' that begins the prayer and prohibits worldly actions.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' (in the name of Allah), especially over slaughtering.
صاحبین (sahibayn): The two primary students of Abu Hanifa: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting Quran in Persian during prayer for a person capable of Arabic?
A) Permissible and fulfills the obligation
B) Permissible but does not fulfill the obligation
C) Not permissible; prayer becomes invalid if done
D) Not permissible; prayer remains valid but obligation not fulfilled

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that reciting Quran in a non-Arabic language during prayer is not permissible for one capable of Arabic, though the prayer remains valid.

Khutbah, Tashahhud, and Adhan: Language Dispute and Recognition
Extension of language dispute to khutbah/tashahhud; adhan ruling on recognition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on non-Arabic khutbah and tashahhud, and explain the condition for valid adhan in Persian.

Core Idea
For khutbah and tashahhud, the language dispute mirrors qira'ah; for adhan, validity hinges on recognition, not language.

This passage extends the same intra-Hanafi dispute about non-Arabic recitation to two other prayer components: khutbah (Friday sermon) and tashahhud (testification). It then provides a distinct ruling for adhan (call to prayer), where the purpose is announcement, so recognition is key.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute applied to khutbah and tashahhud
The passage states that the same difference (i.e., regarding permissibility of non-Arabic recitation) exists for khutbah and tashahhud. Recognize that Abu Hanifa allows non-Arabic, while Sahibayn require Arabic.
This mirrors the earlier dispute about qira'ah in prayer.
2
Understand the adhan ruling from al-Mabsut
The passage cites a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that adhan in Persian is permissible if people recognize it as adhan; otherwise not. The condition is recognition, not the language itself.
The purpose of adhan is announcement (i'lam).
3
Distinguish between the two rulings
For khutbah and tashahhud, the dispute is about language permissibility; for adhan, the condition is functional: people must know it is adhan. This is a different criterion.
Thus, even in Arabic, if people don't recognize it, it may not fulfill the purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خطبہ اور التحیات میں یہی اختلاف ہے یعنی امام صاحب کے نزدیک غیر عربی میں جائز ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے اور اذان میں تعارف معتبر ہے مبسوط میں مذکور ہے کہ حسن بن زیاد نے امام ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کیا ہے کہ اگر فارسی زبان میں اذان دی اور لوگ جانتے ہیں کہ یہ اذان ہے تو جائز ہے اور اگر لوگ اس کے اذان ہونے سے واقف نہ ہوں تو جائز نہیں اس لئے مقصود اذان سے اعلام ہے اور لوگوں کے نہ جانے کی وجہ سے یہ مقصود حاصل نہیں ہوا۔
Khutbah and tashahhud have the same difference: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is permissible in non-Arabic; according to the Sahibayn, it is not permissible. In adhan, recognition is considered. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut that Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa: if one gives adhan in Persian and people know that it is adhan, then it is permissible; if people are not aware that it is adhan, then it is not permissible because the purpose of adhan is announcement, and due to people not knowing, this purpose is not achieved.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage applies the same intra-Hanafi dispute about non-Arabic recitation to two other elements of prayer: the khutbah (Friday sermon) and tashahhud (testification). It then addresses a distinct ruling for adhan (call to prayer). The key point for adhan is that its purpose is announcement (i'lam), so the condition is that the listeners recognize it as adhan. If given in Persian and understood as adhan, it is valid; otherwise not. This ruling is based on a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered before Friday prayer or Eid prayer.
تشہد (tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting in prayer: 'At-tahiyyatu lillahi...'
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, consisting of specific phrases announcing the prayer time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad in al-Mabsut, when is adhan in Persian permissible?
A) Only if the muezzin cannot speak Arabic.
B) Only if it is recited in addition to the Arabic adhan.
C) When the listeners know that it is adhan.
D) It is never permissible.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on language in khutbah and tashahhud mirrors the recitation dispute, while adhan has a separate condition: recognition by listeners.

Recitation in Non-Arabic Languages in Prayer: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-madhhab dispute on reciting Quran in non-Arabic in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding recitation of Quran in non-Arabic during prayer, identify the proofs used, and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Recitation in non-Arabic may fulfill fard qira'ah per Abu Hanifa, but the relied-upon view requires Arabic.

This passage from the Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about whether the obligatory recitation (fard qira'ah) can be performed in a language other than Arabic. The issue arises from the story of Salman al-Farsi, who wrote Surah al-Fatihah in Persian, and the Prophet's tacit approval. The Hanafi school debated the validity of non-Arabic recitation, with Imam Abu Hanifa initially permitting it in all languages, while his students Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) disagreed. The passage also records a later retraction by Abu Hanifa and extends the discussion to other formulas like khutbah, tahiyyat, and even the adhan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
What is being disputed? Recitation of Quran in non-Arabic during prayer, specifically whether it fulfills the fard qira'ah (obligatory recitation). The core question: Does reciting a translation fulfill the obligation?
Fard qira'ah is the minimum recitation required in prayer; its fulfillment is essential for the prayer's correctness.
2
State the Hanafi positions
Imam Abu Hanifa (initial view): recitation in any language permissible and fulfills fard. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): only Arabic fulfills fard; non-Arabic recitation is insufficient. Later, Abu Hanifa retracted to the Sahibayn's view, and this is the mufta bihi.
The Hidayah author declares permissibility in all languages as the correct statement, but then reports the retraction.
3
Examine the proofs
Abu Hanifa's dalil: (1) Hadith of Salman al-Farsi – Prophet's tacit approval of Persian Fatihah. (2) Quran 26:196 – previous scriptures were not in Arabic, implying meaning transcends language. Sahibayn's dalil: translation is not the Quran itself; the hadith may be a temporary concession for new Muslims.
The verse is used to show that divine revelation can be in non-Arabic forms, but its application to translation is contested.
4
Analyze the practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf)
If one recites in Persian, per Abu Hanifa's initial view: fard fulfilled, prayer valid. Per Sahibayn: fard not fulfilled, prayer valid but compensation (sajdah sahw or repetition) required. The later narration (Ibn al-Humam) states Sahibayn considered prayer invalid.
All agree the prayer is not automatically invalid; the dispute is about fulfillment of fard.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and why
The relied-upon position is that non-Arabic recitation does not fulfill fard qira'ah. This is based on Abu Hanifa's retraction, the Sahibayn's view, and later authorities like Najm al-Din al-Nasafi, Qadhi Khan, and Ibn al-Humam. The Hidayah's correct statement is overridden by the retraction.
This is a common pattern: the initial ra'y of Abu Hanifa may be overridden by his own ruju' or the consensus of the Sahibayn.

Source Text

علامہ ابن الہمام نے لکھا ہے کہ نجم الدین نسفی اور قاضی خان نے لکھا ہے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ ابو بکر رازی نے روایت کیا کہ اصل مسئلہ میں امام صاحب نے صاحبین کے قول کی طرف رجوع کیا یعنی حضرت امام اعظم بھی آخر میں اس کے قائل ہو گئے تھے کہ نماز کے اندر غیر عربی میں قرآت جائز نہیں ہے اور اس پر اعتماد ہے۔

Chapter: Description of Prayer. Ashraf al-Bidayah, commentary of Urdu Hidayah, volume 2. Salman al-Farsi wrote Surah al-Fatihah in Persian and sold it. Those people kept reciting it in prayer until they learned Arabic. After writing it, Salman al-Farsi presented it to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and he did not disapprove of it. This also proves that reciting Quran in Persian in prayer is permissible. The author of Hidayah says: Just as recitation in the Persian language is permissible in prayer, similarly recitation in every language besides Persian is permissible. This is the correct statement. And Abu Sa'id's statement is that Imam Abu Hanifa declared recitation only in Persian permissible, and did not permit other languages besides Persian. The reason is that the Persian language is close to Arabic, so permission was given for recitation in Persian, and since other languages do not have this closeness, recitation in them is not permissible. The proof of the correct statement is the verse: 'And indeed it is in the scriptures of the former peoples' (al-Shu'ara 196) because the Quran was not in Arabic in the previous books, nor was it in Persian. And the second proof is that when transferring the Quran to another language, reliance is on the meaning, and meaning does not change with the difference of languages, therefore translation in Turkish, Hindi, etc., is permissible in every language. The author of Hidayah said: The difference between Imam Sahib and the Sahibayn regarding the permissibility or impermissibility of recitation in non-Arabic is about whether recitation in non-Arabic is considered valid or not. Thus, according to Imam Sahib, if one recites in non-Arabic, the obligatory recitation (fard qira'ah) is fulfilled, while according to the Sahibayn, it is not fulfilled. And there is no disagreement that recitation in non-Arabic does not invalidate the prayer, i.e., if one recites in non-Arabic, by consensus the prayer does not become invalid. Allamah Ibn al-Humam wrote that Najm al-Din al-Nasafi and Qadhi Khan wrote that according to the Sahibayn, the prayer becomes invalid. Abu Bakr al-Razi narrated that on this issue, Imam Sahib reverted to the statement of the Sahibayn, i.e., Imam A'zam also eventually adopted the view that recitation in non-Arabic in prayer is not permissible, and this is relied upon. The same difference exists in the Khutbah and al-Tahiyyat: according to Imam Sahib, it is permissible in non-Arabic, and according to the Sahibayn, it is not permissible. And in the adhan, notification is considered. It is mentioned in al-Mabsut that Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa: If the adhan is given in Persian and the people know that it is the adhan, it is permissible, and if the people are not aware that it is the adhan, it is not permissible, because the purpose of the adhan is notification, and due to the people not knowing, this purpose is not achieved.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding recitation of the Quran in non-Arabic languages during prayer. The author begins with the story of Salman al-Farsi, who wrote Surah al-Fatihah in Persian, and the Prophet's tacit approval, establishing a basis for permissibility. The author of Hidayah declares the correct view to be that recitation in any language (not just Persian) is permissible. However, a contrary opinion attributed to Abu Sa'id limits permission to Persian alone, citing its closeness to Arabic. The passage then presents the core dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) as one of validity: for Abu Hanifa, recitation in non-Arabic fulfills the obligatory recitation (fard qira'ah); for the Sahibayn, it does not. Notably, all agree that the prayer itself is not invalidated, though a later narration from Ibn al-Humam claims the Sahibayn considered it invalid. The passage also reports that Imam Abu Hanifa eventually retracted his view and adopted the Sahibayn's position, and this retraction is relied upon. The same dispute applies to Khutbah and al-Tahiyyat. Finally, regarding adhan, a separate ruling from Hasan ibn Ziyad permits Persian adhan if the people recognize it as adhan, otherwise not, since the purpose is notification.

Key Terms
قرأت (qira'ah): Recitation of Quranic verses during prayer, specifically the obligatory portion (fard qira'ah).
غير عربي (ghayr 'arabi): Any language other than Arabic, used here in the context of Quran recitation in salah.
صاحبين (Sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two primary students of Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only Persian is permissible because of its closeness to Arabic.
B) Recitation in non-Arabic is not permissible.
C) Recitation is permissible in every language.
D) Recitation in non-Arabic invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that fard qira'ah must be in Arabic; non-Arabic recitation does not fulfill the obligation, though the prayer remains valid.

Opening Prayer with Supplicatory Phrases: The Condition of Pure Exaltation
Ruling statement with expansion on the condition of pure exaltation in takbir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on beginning salah with supplicatory phrases, identify which phrases are impermissible, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding 'Allahumma'.

Core Idea
The opening words of salah must be pure exaltation; any phrase containing a request invalidates the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine a crucial condition for the opening takbir in Hanafi fiqh: it must be a phrase of pure exaltation (ta'dhim khalis). The text from al-Hidayah, expanded by al-'Inayah, rules that phrases like 'Allahumma ighfir li' are impermissible because they mix worship with personal need. The passage also records a difference of opinion about the single word 'Allahumma'—is it a pure address or does it imply a request? Understanding this distinction is essential for valid prayer initiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is beginning the salah (takbirat al-ihram). The condition is that the phrase must be pure exaltation, free from any personal request or need.
This condition is derived from the requirement that the opening must be solely for Allah's glorification.
2
State the ruling for explicit supplication
The text explicitly rules that 'Allahumma ighfir li' is not permissible because it is mixed with personal need, thus not pure exaltation.
Such phrases are invalid beginnings; the prayer must be repeated.
3
Extend to other phrases
The commentary lists other phrases that likewise imply a request: 'astaghfirullah', 'a'udhu billah', 'bismillah', etc. All are impermissible.
Any phrase that is not purely exalting falls under this ruling.
4
Analyze the dispute on 'Allahumma'
Two views: Basrans consider 'Allahumma' permissible as a pure address; Kufans consider it impermissible because its full meaning 'O Allah, intend for us good' implies a request. The relied-upon view is the Kufan position.
This shows that even a single word can be problematic if it carries supplicatory connotation.
5
Apply the condition to new phrases
Given a phrase, determine if it is pure exaltation or contains any element of request. If it contains a request, it cannot be used to open the prayer.
Examples: 'Allahu Akbar' is pure; 'Ya Allah' is similar to 'Allahumma' and disputed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللهم اغفر لی کے ساتھ نماز شروع کرنے کا حکم
وأن افتتح الصلوة باللهم اغفرلى لا تجوز لانه مشوب بحاجتة فلم يكن تعظيما خالصا وان افتتح بقوله اللهم فقد قيل يجزيه لان معناه يا الله وقد قيل لا يجزيه لان معناه يا الله امنا بخير في سان سؤالا
ترجمہ اور اگر اللهم اغفرلی سے نماز شروع کی تو جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اس کی حاجت کے ساتھ مخلوط ہے تو خالص تقضی پہلے ہوئی۔ اور اگر اللہم سے شروع کی تو کہا گیا کہ کافی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کے معنی ہیں یا اللہ اور کہا گیا کہ کافی نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے معنی یعنی نمازی اے اللہ ہمارا قصد فرما خیر کے ساتھ پس یہ سوال ہوا۔

Ruling on starting prayer with 'Allahumma ighfir li'. And if he begins the prayer with 'Allahumma ighfir li', it is not permissible because it is mixed with his personal need, so it is not pure exaltation. And if he begins with 'Allahumma', it has been said that it suffices because its meaning is 'O Allah', and it has been said that it does not suffice because its meaning is 'O Allah, intend for us good', so it becomes a request. Translation: And if the prayer is begun with 'Allahumma ighfir li', it is not permissible, because it is mixed with his need, so it is not for pure exaltation. The same applies to all words that do not indicate pure exaltation but imply a request, such as 'astaghfirullah', 'a'udhu billah', 'inna lillah', 'masha Allah', 'la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah', and 'bismillah'. If the prayer is begun with 'Allahumma', there is disagreement. One group holds it is permissible because 'Allahumma' means 'O Allah' and there is no mixing with need; this is the view of the Basrans. Another group holds it is not permissible because its meaning is 'O Allah, intend for us good', so it becomes a request; this is the view of the Kufans. (al-'Inayah)
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hidayah regarding the opening words of prayer (takbirat al-ihram). The ruling states that beginning the prayer with 'Allahumma ighfir li' (O Allah, forgive me) is not permissible because the phrase contains a personal supplication, which is not pure exaltation of Allah. The author explains that the opening words of prayer must be solely for the purpose of exaltation (ta'dhim), and any phrase that includes a request (su'al) taints this purity. The commentary lists other examples: 'astaghfirullah', 'a'udhu billah', etc. As for 'Allahumma' alone, there is a difference of opinion: the Basrans (including some Hanafis) consider it permissible because it is simply a form of address meaning 'O Allah', without any request. The Kufans (including many Hanafis) consider it impermissible because the full meaning 'O Allah, intend for us good' implies a request. The relied-upon view is the Kufan view, as indicated in the text by the term 'jā'iz-nī' (not permissible) from al-'Inayah.

Key Terms
اللهم (Allahumma): A vocative form of Allah, meaning 'O Allah'. The passage debates whether it implies an implicit request.
تعظيم خالص (ta'dhim khalis): Pure exaltation, the required quality of the opening phrase of prayer, free from any element of personal request.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi relied-upon position, what is the ruling on opening salah with the word 'Allahumma' alone?
A) Permissible, because it means 'O Allah' and is a pure address.
B) Not permissible, because it implies a request for goodness.
C) Permissible only if followed by 'Allahu Akbar'.
D) Makruh tanzihi (disliked but valid).

Key Takeaway
The opening phrase of salah must be pure exaltation; any phrase containing a personal request – explicitly or implicitly – invalidates the prayer.
