Hand Placement in Prayer: Under the Navel
Hanafi ruling with inter-madhhab evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on placing the right hand on the left under the navel during prayer, explain the hadith evidence, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Maliki and Shafi'i schools.

Core Idea
Placing the right hand on the left under the navel is Sunnah, proven by a hadith, and refutes both Maliki irsal and Shafi'i chest placement.

Hand placement during standing (qiyam) is a distinctive feature of prayer form. The Hanafi school, based on a specific hadith, teaches that the right hand should be placed on the left under the navel. This lesson examines that ruling, its evidence, and how it differs from the Maliki and Shafi'i practices, helping you understand the legal reasoning behind the difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by identifying exactly what the Hanafi school rules: the worshipper places the right hand on the left hand under the navel during standing positions that include prescribed dhikr.
Note that this applies during qiyam after takbir, but not during qawma (standing after ruku).
2
Identify the opponents and their views
The passage mentions two opposing practices: the Maliki school lets hands hang freely (irsal), and the Shafi'i school places hands on the chest. Identify these positions clearly.
These are the main non-Hanafi positions on hand placement.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The cited hadith: 'From the Sunnah is placing the right hand on the left under the navel.' Understand that Hanafis treat this as a strong proof (zanni al-thubut but accepted) that establishes the practice as Sunnah mu'akkadah.
The phrase 'min al-sunnah' indicates an established prophetic practice, not a wajib.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to opponents
The passage asserts that this hadith is a proof (hujja) against Malik and al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi reasoning is that the hadith directly supports under-navel placement, and that this placement is closer to reverence (ta'zim), which is the objective of prayer.
The Hanafi school does not accept the opposing proofs as stronger.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence of this difference is in the physical form of prayer: Hanafis fold hands under navel, Shafi'is on chest, and Malikis let them hang. This affects the appearance and reward of the prayer.
Each school considers its practice sunnah and the others as less preferred or even makruh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نماز میں ہاتھ باندھنے کا طریقہ اور ہاتھ کہاں باندھے جائیں... اقوال فقہاء
قال ويعتمد بيده اليمنى على اليسرى تحت السرة، لقوله عليه السلام من السنة وضع اليمين على الصدر ولا کو بائیں۔ الشمال تحت السرة وهو حجة على مالك فى الارسال وعلى الشافعى في الوضع على الصدر ولا الوضع تحت السرة اقرب الى التعظيم وهو المقصود ثم الاعتماد سنة القيام عند ابي حنيفة و ابي يوسف حتى لا يرسل حالة الثناء والاصل ان كل قيام فيه ذكر مسنون يعتمد فيه ومالا فلا هو الصحيح فيعتمد في ركنا أفضل حالة القنوت وصلوة الجنازه ويرسل فى القومة وبين تكبيرات الاعياد
ترجمہ مصنف نے کہا کہ ٹیک لے اپنے دائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ہاتھ پر ناف کے نیچے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ناف کے یا دائیں ہاتھ کا انہیں پر رکھنا سنت ہے اور یہ حدیث امام مالک کے خلاف حجت ہے ہاتھ چھوڑنے میں اور امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ۔ رضی اللہ تعہ سینہ پر ہاتھ باندھنے میں اور اس لئے کہ زیر ناف رکھا تعظیم کے زیادہ قریب ہے اور تعظیم ہی مقصود ہے پھر اعتماد شیخین کے نزدیک قیام سنت مراد سنت ہے حتی کہ ثناء کی حالت میں ہاتھوں کو نہیں چھوڑے گا۔ اور اصل یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ قیام جس میں کوئی ذکر مسنون ہو اس میں ہاتھ باندھے اور جو قیام اس صفت کا نہ ہو اس میں مسنون نہیں ہے یہی قول صحیح ہے پس ہاتھ باند ھے حالت قنوت میں اور جناز و کی نماز میں اور بانی افضل ہے۔ چھوڑے قومہ میں اور عیدین کی تکبیروں میں۔ تشریح اس عبارت کے تحت اعتماد میں چار مسئلے ہیں: کیا نماز میں اپنا دایاں ہاتھ بائیں ہاتھ پر رکھے یا نہیں؟
کس طرح رکھے؟ (۳) ، کہاں رکھے؟ ، ۴ کب رکھے؟
The method of folding hands in prayer and where to place them... Statements of jurists. He said: He leans with his right hand on his left under the navel, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'It is from the Sunnah to place the right hand on the left under the navel.' This hadith is a proof against Malik regarding letting the hands hang, and against al-Shafi'i regarding placing them on the chest. And because placing under the navel is closer to reverence, and reverence is the objective. Then, leaning (i'timad) is Sunnah during standing according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, such that he should not let his hands hang during the recitation of thana'. The principle is: every standing in which there is a prescribed dhikr, he leans (folds hands) therein; and when there is not, then not. This is the correct position. So he leans (folds) in rukna? (perhaps a typo) better, during qunut and the funeral prayer, and he lets his hands hang during the qawma (standing after ruku') and between the takbirs of the duas of 'Id. Translation: The author said: He leans his right hand on his left under the navel. Because the Prophet said that placing the right hand on the left under the navel is Sunnah. This hadith is a proof against Imam Malik in letting the hands hang, and against Imam al-Shafi'i in placing on the chest. And because placing under the navel is closer to reverence, and reverence is the objective. Then, leaning (i'timad) is Sunnah during standing according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), so much so that he does not let his hands hang during the state of thana'. The principle is: every standing in which there is a prescribed dhikr, he folds his hands, and when there is no such dhikr, it is not prescribed. This is the correct saying. So he folds his hands during qunut and the funeral prayer, and it is better for the one leading. He lets his hands hang during the qawma and between the takbirs of the 'Id prayers. Commentary: Under this passage regarding leaning (i'timad), there are four issues: 1) Should one place his right hand on his left in prayer or not? 2) How to place? 3) Where to place? 4) When to place?
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary details the Hanafi ruling on hand placement (qabd) during prayer. It begins by stating the ruling: the worshipper should place his right hand on his left under the navel. The evidence is a hadith declaring this practice to be from the Sunnah. This ruling serves as a refutation of the Maliki school, which prefers letting the hands hang (irsal), and the Shafi'i school, which places the hands on the chest. The Hanafi position is that placement under the navel is more conducive to humility and reverence. The passage then discusses the principle of i'timad (leaning/folding hands): it is Sunnah during any standing in which a prescribed dhikr is recited, such as during thana' (opening supplication), qunut, and the funeral prayer. It is not prescribed during the qawma (standing after ruku') or between the takbirs of 'Id prayer. The commentary specifies that according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, i'timad during qiyam is Sunnah, meaning one should not release his hands even during thana'. The correct view is that the practice is tied to dhikr. The passage concludes by outlining four issues: whether to fold, how, where, and when.

Key Terms
اعتماد (i'timad): Leaning or placing the hands in prayer, specifically folding the right hand over the left during standing.
قومة (qawma): The standing after rising from ruku', immediately before prostrating.
ارسال (irsal): Letting the hands hang freely at the sides during standing, as practiced by Maliki school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the hadith about hand placement a proof against Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i?
A) Because Malik lets hands hang and Shafi'i places on chest, while the hadith says under navel.
B) Because Malik and Shafi'i do not consider any hand placement.
C) Because the hadith is weak and both reject it.
D) Because the hadith commands placing hands on the chest only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on hand placement under the navel is grounded in a hadith that establishes it as Sunnah and refutes both the Maliki and Shafi'i positions, with application tied to standings that include prescribed dhikr.

Ruling on Starting Prayer with Supplications
Ruling with proof on pure glorification vs supplication in prayer opening.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling that starting prayer with a supplication is invalid and EXPLAIN the ikhtilaf regarding 'Allahumma'.

Core Idea
Starting prayer requires pure glorification; any phrase implying a request invalidates the opening.

In the chapter on the description of prayer, the Hanafi school emphasizes that the words after the opening takbir must be purely for the glorification of Allah. This lesson examines two phrases: 'Allahummaghfirli', which clearly contains a request, and 'Allahumma', which is debated. The key is to understand the difference between pure glorification and supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Starting prayer with 'Allahummaghfirli' and 'Allahumma'. The ruling for the former is invalid (ja'iz nahi).
The act is the opening statement after the takbir.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is linguistic analysis: 'Allahummaghfirli' is a supplication, thus mixed with a need (hajah), not pure glorification.
The same reasoning applies to phrases like 'Astaghfirullah' etc.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'ighfir li' is a request, so the entire phrase becomes a request. For 'Allahumma', the Kufan interpretation includes an implied request.
The specific words or structure that yield the ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion on 'Allahumma': Basrans consider it pure vocative; Kufans interpret it as a request.
The source identifies these two groups.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi school relies on the Kufan view, so starting with 'Allahumma' alone is also not permissible.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفة الصلوة
ترجمہ: اور اگر «اللهم اغفر لي» سے نماز شروع کی تو جائز نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ وہ اس کی حاجت کے ساتھ مخلوط ہے، تو خالص تعظیم نہیں رہی۔ اور اگر «اللهم» سے شروع کی تو کہا گیا کہ کافی ہے، کیونکہ اس کے معنی ہیں «یا اللہ» اور کہا گیا کہ کافی نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس کے معنی ہیں «یا اللہ اقصدنا بخیر» پس یہ سوال ہوا۔
تشریح: اور اگر نماز «اللهم اغفر لي» کے ساتھ شروع کی تو جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وہ اس کی حاجت کے ساتھ مخلوط ہے، پس چونکہ وہ خالص تعظیم کے لئے نہیں رہا، اس لئے اس کے ساتھ نماز شروع کرنا جائز نہیں ہوگا۔ یہی حال ان تمام الفاظ کا ہے جو نہ صرف تعظیم پر دلالت کریں بلکہ صراحتاً یا معنیً سوال کو متضمن ہوں، جیسے «استغفر الله»، «أعوذ بالله»، «إن شاء الله»، «ما شاء الله»، «لا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله»، اور «بسم الله»۔ اور اگر «اللهم» کے ساتھ نماز شروع کی تو اس میں اختلاف ہے: ایک جماعت کی رائے یہ ہے کہ جائز ہے، کیونکہ «اللهم» کا معنی ہے «یا اللہ» اور فی نفسہ اللہ کا ذکر ہے، اس میں حاجت وغیرہ کی کوئی آمیزش نہیں ہے۔ یہ قول اہل بصرہ کا ہے۔ اور ایک جماعت کا خیال ہے کہ «اللهم» کے ساتھ نماز شروع کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اس کے معنی ہیں «یا اللہ اُمَّنا بخیر» یعنی اقصدنا بخیر، اے اللہ ہمارے ساتھ بھلائی کا ارادہ فرما۔ ظاہر ہے کہ اس صورت میں یہ کلمہ خالص تعظیم پر دلالت کرنے والا نہیں ہوا، اس لئے اس کلمہ کے ساتھ نماز شروع کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہ قول اہل کوفہ کا ہے۔ (عنایہ)
Chapter of Description of Prayer. Translation: If one starts prayer with 'Allahumma ghfir li', it is not permissible, because it is mixed with a need, so it is no longer pure glorification. And if one starts with 'Allahumma', it was said that it suffices, because its meaning is 'O Allah', and it was said that it does not suffice, because its meaning is 'O Allah, intend good for us', so it becomes a request. Commentary: If one starts prayer with 'Allahumma ghfir li', it is not permissible, because it is mixed with a need, so since it is not for pure glorification, starting prayer with it is not permissible. The same applies to all words that do not merely indicate glorification but explicitly or implicitly include a request, such as 'Astaghfirullah', 'A'udhu billah', 'In sha Allah', 'Ma sha Allah', 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah', and 'Bismillah'. And if one starts prayer with 'Allahumma', there is a difference of opinion: one group holds that it is permissible, because 'Allahumma' means 'O Allah', and it is inherently the mention of Allah, with no mixture of request. This is the view of the Basrans. Another group holds that starting prayer with 'Allahumma' is not permissible, because its meaning is 'O Allah, lead us with good' i.e., intend good for us, O Allah. Obviously in this case the word does not indicate pure glorification, so starting prayer with this word is not permissible. This is the view of the Kufans. (from 'Inayah)
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on the description of prayer. It addresses the permissibility of starting prayer with particular phrases. The author first states that starting with 'Allahumma ghfir li' (O Allah, forgive me) is invalid because it is a supplication mixed with a personal need, thus not pure glorification of Allah. The same ruling applies to any phrase that contains a request, such as 'Astaghfirullah' (I seek forgiveness from Allah) or 'A'udhu billah' (I seek refuge with Allah). Then the passage discusses 'Allahumma' (O Allah). There is an ikhtilaf: the Basrans permit it because 'Allahumma' is simply an exclamation meaning 'O Allah' with no additional request. The Kufans (the dominant view in the Hanafi school) disallow it because they analyze 'Allumma' as 'ya Allah umma bi khayr' (O Allah, lead us with good), which implies a request and thus lacks pure glorification. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that one should not start prayer with 'Allahumma' alone; the opening takbir should be followed immediately by the thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma) without any intervening word. However, if one does start with 'Allahumma', some later scholars consider it valid while makruh.

Key Terms
اللهم اغفر لي (Allahumma ghfir li): A phrase meaning 'O Allah, forgive me' used as a supplication.
اللهم (Allahumma): A vocative form meaning 'O Allah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not permissible to start prayer with 'Allahummaghfirli'?
A) Because it contains a request for forgiveness, mixing supplication with glorification.
B) Because it is too long.
C) Because it is not in Arabic.
D) Because it is only for the imam.

Key Takeaway
The opening of prayer must be pure glorification; any phrase that includes a request, explicitly or implicitly, invalidates the prayer.

Placing Hands in Prayer: Hanafi Sunnah vs. Maliki Irsal
Ruling that placing right hand over left in prayer is sunnah, with proof and refutation of Malik's view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement in prayer as sunnah mu'akkadah, distinguish it from the Maliki position, and explain the key proofs and their significance.

Core Idea
Placing the right on the left in prayer is a confirmed sunnah, not a mere option.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses the first of four issues regarding hand placement in prayer: whether to place the right hand over the left. The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that doing so is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), supported by the Prophet's persistent practice and explicit command. In contrast, Imam Malik considers leaving the hands loose (irsal) as the primary practice ('azimah) and clasping as a concession (rukhsah). Understanding this dispute clarifies the basis of the Hanafi ruling and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act: placing the right hand on the left in prayer. The three Hanafi imams consider it sunnah mu'akkadah.
Sunnah mu'akkadah means confirmed and regularly practiced, not obligatory. Omission does not invalidate prayer.
2
Identify the opposing Maliki view
Imam Malik holds that irsal (leaving hands loose) is the 'azimah (primary ruling) and that i'timad (placing) is a rukhsah (concession).
'Azimah is the stronger, stricter ruling; rukhsah is a relaxation.
3
Examine the Hanafi proofs
Look at the hadith: 'Inna ma'shar al-anbiya…' (command to take left with right), the athar from Ali stating it is sunnah, and the Abu Dawud narration where the Prophet corrected Ibn Mas'ud.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni proof, but its strength comes from multiple supporting narrations.
4
Understand the Hanafi refutation of Malik
The text asserts that these narrations are evidence against Malik's view, establishing that placing is sunnah and that irsal is not sunnah.
The commentary also notes a scribal error in the Hidayah where 'Ali' was changed to 'alayhi al-salam'.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For a Hanafi, placing hands is recommended and omission is not sinful but less perfect. For a Maliki, leaving hands loose is the default, and placing is a concession.
When a Hanafi follows a Maliki imam, he should follow the imam's practice regarding hand placement to avoid dispute?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح: اس عبارت کے تحت اعتماد میں چار مسئلے ہیں:
(1) کیا نماز میں اپنا دایاں ہاتھ بائیں ہاتھ پر رکھے یا نہیں؟
پہلے مسئلہ میں ہمارے علماء ثلاثہ کا قول یہ ہے کہ نماز میں دایاں ہاتھ بائیں پر رکھنا مسنون ہے، اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ ارسال کرنے یعنی نماز میں ہاتھ چھوڑے رکھے، اور جی چاہے تو باندھ لے۔ پس امام مالک کے نزدیک ارسال عزیمت اور اعتماد (ہاتھ رکھنا) رخصت ہے۔
ہمارے علماء کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ ﷺ نے اس پر مداومت فرمائی، اور فرمایا: «إنا معشر الأنبياء أمرنا أن نأخذ شمائلنا بأيماننا في الصلاة» یعنی ہم انبیاء کی جماعت کو حکم دیا گیا کہ ہم نماز میں اپنے دائیں ہاتھ سے بائیں ہاتھ کو پکڑیں۔
اور حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ نے فرمایا: «من السنة أن يصنع المصلي يمينه على شماله تحت السرة في الصلاة» صاحب ہدایہ نے یہ اثر ان الفاظ کے ساتھ ذکر کیا: «إن من السنة وضع اليمين على الشمال تحت السرة» دونوں کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ نے فرمایا کہ نماز میں دائیں ہاتھ کا بائیں ہاتھ پر رکھنا مسنون ہے۔
یہاں یہ بات قابل ذکر ہے کہ ہدایہ کے اصل نسخہ میں یہ عبارت یوں تھی: «لقول علي إن من السنة» لیکن نادان لکھنے والوں نے اس کو «لقوله عليه السلام» کر دیا۔
اور ابوداؤد میں ہے: عن ابن مسعود أنه كان يصلي فوضع يده اليسرى على اليمنى فرآه النبي ﷺ فوضع يده اليمنى على اليسرى۔ ابن مسعود رضی اللہ عنہ سے روایت ہے کہ وہ نماز پڑھتے تھے اور انہوں نے اپنا بایاں ہاتھ دائیں پر رکھا، حضور ﷺ نے دیکھا تو ابن مسعود کا دایاں ہاتھ بائیں پر رکھ دیا۔
بہر حال ان روایات سے ثابت ہوا کہ مسنون دائیں ہاتھ کا بائیں پر رکھنا ہے، اور یہ احادیث امام مالک کے خلاف حجت ہیں، اور ارسال کی عدم سنیت ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ (عنایہ)
Commentary: Under this phrase there are four issues regarding i'timad (leaning): (1) Should one place his right hand on his left in prayer or not? In the first issue, the view of our three scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that placing the right hand on the left in prayer is sunnah. Imam Malik said to leave them loose (irsal), i.e., keep hands hanging, and if one wishes he may clasp them. So according to Malik, irsal is the 'azimah and i'timad is rukhsah. Our scholars' proof is that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ persisted upon this, and he said: 'We, the company of prophets, have been commanded to take our left hands with our right hands in prayer.' And Ali (رضي الله عنه) said: 'It is from the sunnah that the worshipper places his right hand on his left under the navel in prayer.' The author of Hidayah mentioned this athar with the words: 'Indeed from the sunnah is placing the right on the left under the navel.' The gist is that Ali said placing the right on the left in prayer is sunnah. It is noteworthy that in the original manuscript of Hidayah the phrase was 'liquawli 'Ali inna min al-sunnah' but ignorant scribes changed it to 'liquawlihi 'alayhi al-salam'. And in Abu Dawud it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that he was praying and placed his left hand on his right; the Prophet ﷺ saw him and placed his right hand on his left. So these narrations prove that the sunnah is to place the right on the left, and these hadiths are proof against Malik, and the lack of sunnah of irsal is established. (from 'Inayah)
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the Hidayah's matn on hand placement. It presents the first of four issues: whether to place hands. The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that placing the right hand on the left in prayer is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah). Imam Malik holds that leaving the hands loose (irsal) is the preferred practice ('azimah) and clasping is a concession (rukhsah). The Hanafi proof comes from multiple hadiths: a prophetic statement (though its chain is debated), the practice of Prophet ﷺ, an athar from Ali (رضي الله عنه) explicitly stating it is sunnah to place the right on the left under the navel, and a narration from Abu Dawud about Ibn Mas'ud being corrected by the Prophet ﷺ. The commentary also notes a scribal error in the Hidayah text where 'Ali' was changed to 'alayhi al-salam' (peace be upon him) by mistake. The evidence establishes that the sunnah is to place hands, thus refuting Malik's preference for irsal.

Key Terms
ارسال (irsal): Leaving the hands hanging loose at the sides during prayer.
اعتماد (i'timad): Placing one hand on the other in prayer, i.e., clasping hands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on placing the right hand over the left in prayer?
A) It is fard.
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
C) It is mubah (optional).
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Placing the right hand on the left in prayer is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) in the Hanafi school, supported by prophetic command and practice, and this view differs from the Maliki preference for irsal.

Second Issue: Manner of Placing Hands
Description of specific hand placement in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi sunnah method of placing the right hand on the left in prayer and distinguish it from other methods.

Core Idea
The Hanafi sunnah: palm on back, thumb and little finger grip the wrist.

In this lesson, we examine the specific manner (kayfiyyah) of placing the right hand on the left during prayer (qiyam). This is a sunnah mu'akkadah practice that the Hanafi school has detailed from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding the exact description helps ensure our prayer follows the most complete form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the passage describes the kayfiyyah (manner) of placing the right hand on the left during prayer, a sunnah act within qiyam.
2
Locate the key terms
Identify the body parts mentioned: palm (kaff), back (zahr), thumb (ibham), little finger (khinsir), wrist (gitta/pahuncha).
The term 'gitta' is colloquial for wrist.
3
Visualize the position
Mentally picture the right palm placed on the back of the left hand, with the right thumb and little finger gripping the left wrist.
4
Note the hukm
Understand that this is a sunnah mu'akkadah act; omitting it does not invalidate prayer but one loses reward.
The ruling is sunnah, not fard or wajib.
5
Contrast with other methods
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may place hands on the chest or interlock fingers; Hanafis consider the described method as the most complete.
This is a distinguishing feature of the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرا مسئلہ: کیفیت وضع کا ہے یعنی دائیں ہاتھ کو بائیں ہاتھ پر رکھنے کی کیفیت کیا ہے؟ سو اس کی کیفیت یہ ہے کہ دائیں ہاتھ کی ہتھیلی کو بائیں ہاتھ کی ہتھیلی کی پشت پر رکھے، اور دائیں ہاتھ کے انگوٹھے اور چھنگلی انگلی سے بائیں ہاتھ کا گٹا (پہنچا) پکڑے۔
The second issue: regarding the manner of placement, i.e., what is the manner of placing the right hand on the left? So its manner is that he places the palm of the right hand on the back of the left hand, and with the thumb and little finger of the right hand, he grasps the wrist of the left hand.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling describing the sunnah manner of clasping hands in prayer. The Hanafi school specifies that the palm of the right hand is placed on the back of the left hand (not interlocking fingers), and the thumb and little finger (or sometimes the thumb and index finger) are used to grip the left wrist. This method is considered the most complete form of i'timad and is the preferred practice in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
کیفیت وضع (kayfiyyat al-wad'): The specific described manner of placing the right hand on the left in prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah for hand placement in prayer is to place the right palm on the back of the left hand and grip the left wrist with the right thumb and little finger.

Hand Placement in Prayer: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute with Shafi'i on hand placement, with Hanafi proofs and refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hand placement in prayer, identify the Shafi'i proof and its Hanafi refutation, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf between the two schools.

Core Idea
Hanafis place hands under navel; Shafi'is on chest. Both are valid, but the Hanafi proof is the athar of Ali.

This passage addresses a well-known ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding where to place the hands during prayer. The Hanafi school, following the athar of Ali (رضي الله عنه) and the principle of humility, holds that the hands should be placed under the navel. Imam Shafi'i, on the other hand, argues for placement on the chest, citing the Qur'anic verse 'wanhar' and the idea of protecting the chest. In this lesson, we will dissect the proofs of both sides and understand why the Hanafi position is considered superior within our school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the preferred (afdal) placement is under the navel. This is classified as sunnah mu'akkadah. The text begins with 'according to us (Hanafis), the superior is to clasp hands under the navel'.
The phrase 'afdal' indicates preference, not obligation.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Imam Shafi'i places hands on the chest. His proof is the Qur'anic verse 'wanhar' (Surah al-Kawthar, 2), which he interprets as placing the right hand on the left on the chest. He also argues that the chest is the seat of faith and should be protected.
Some exegetes are cited as supporting this interpretation.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi response refutes the interpretation of 'wanhar' by stating that it actually refers to sacrificing the sacrificial animal after Eid prayer, not hand placement. The verse is about sacrifice, not prayer posture.
The author of 'Inayah explains this tafsir.
4
Examine the Hanafi proofs
The primary Hanafi proof is the athar of Ali (رضي الله عنه): 'Indeed from the sunnah is placing the right on the left under the navel'. The word 'sunnah' here indicates Prophetic practice. Additionally, placing under the navel demonstrates greater humility (ta'dhim) and avoids resemblance to the People of the Book.
The author of Kifayah adds that it also helps cover the 'awrah.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf is simple: Hanafis place hands under the navel, Shafi'is on the chest. Both practices are valid within their respective schools, but the Hanafi mufta bihi is under the navel.
The difference is in preference, not validity of prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تیسرا مسئلہ: ہاتھ رکھنے کی جگہ کا ہے۔ پس ہمارے نزدیک افضل یہ ہے کہ زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھے، اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک سینہ پر ہاتھ رکھنا افضل ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل: باری تعالیٰ کا قول «فصل لربك وانحر» یعنی اپنے رب کے واسطے نماز پڑھ اور دایاں ہاتھ بائیں پر سینہ پر رکھے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام اور صاحب عنایہ نے فرمایا کہ مفسرین نے کہا کہ «وانحر» سے دائیں ہاتھ کا بائیں پر سینہ پر رکھنا مراد ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ سینہ نور ایمان کی جگہ ہے، لہٰذا نماز کے اندر اپنے ہاتھ سے اس کی حفاظت کرنا اولیٰ ہے۔
ہماری دلیل: حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ کا اثر ہے یعنی «إن من السنة وضع اليمين على الشمال تحت السرة» اور لفظ «سنت» سے بالعموم رسول اللہ ﷺ کی سنت مراد ہوتی ہے، پس ثابت ہوا کہ زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھنا مسنون ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھنے میں تعظیم ہے اور نماز کے اندر تعظیم ہی مقصود ہوتی ہے، اس لئے بھی زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھنا اولیٰ ہے۔
صاحب کفایہ نے لکھا ہے کہ زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھنے میں اہل کتاب کے ساتھ تشبہ سے بعد ہو جاتا ہے اور ستر عورت سے قرب ہو جاتا ہے، اس لئے بھی زیر ناف ہاتھ باندھنا اولیٰ ہے۔
اور امام شافعی کا «وانحر» سے استدلال کرنا درست نہیں ہے، کیونکہ آیت میں «وانحر» سے مراد عید کی نماز کے بعد قربانی کے جانور کا نحر (ذبح) کرنا ہے۔ (عنایہ)
The third issue: regarding the place of placing hands. So according to us (Hanafis), the superior (afdal) is to clasp hands under the navel. According to Imam Shafi'i, placing hands on the chest is superior. Imam Shafi'i's proof: the saying of Allah Most High: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice [anhar]' meaning: pray to your Lord and place the right hand on the left on the chest. Allama Ibn al-Humam and the author of 'Inayah said that the exegetes said that 'wanhar' means placing the right hand on the left on the chest. His second proof is that the chest is the place of the light of faith, so it is more appropriate to protect it with one's hands during prayer. Our (Hanafi) proof: the athar of Ali (رضي الله عنه): 'Indeed from the sunnah is placing the right on the left under the navel', and the word 'sunnah' generally refers to the sunnah of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, so it is established that clasping under the navel is sunnah. The second proof is that placing hands under the navel contains greater humility (ta'dhim), and humility is the purpose of prayer, so for this reason also placing under the navel is superior. The author of Kifayah wrote that placing under the navel avoids resemblance to the People of the Book and is closer to covering the 'awrah, so for this reason also it is superior. And Imam Shafi'i's deduction from 'wanhar' is not correct, because 'wanhar' in the verse refers to sacrificing the sacrificial animal after the 'Eid prayer. (from 'Inayah)
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage addresses the location of hand placement in prayer, a well-known ikhtilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi school (following the athar of Ali and the emphasis on humility) holds that hands should be placed under the navel. Imam Shafi'i holds that they should be placed on the chest, citing the verse 'fisalli li rabbika wanhar' (Surah al-Kawthar) which he interprets as placing hands on the chest during prayer. The Hanafi commentary refutes this by stating that 'wanhar' in the verse actually means the ritual sacrifice after Eid prayer, not hand placement. Additionally, Hanafis argue that placing hands under the navel is more conducive to humility (ta'dhim) and also avoids imitation of the People of the Book (who are reported to place hands on the chest). The athar from Ali is considered authoritative because the word 'sunnah' in it refers to the Prophet's practice. Thus, the Hanafi position is that under the navel is superior.

Key Terms
تحت السرة (tahta al-surrah): Below the navel, the recommended placement for hands in prayer according to Hanafis.
وانحر (wanhar): A word from Surah al-Kawthar (verse 2), interpreted by Shafi'is as placing hands on chest, but Hanafis interpret as sacrificial slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Qur'anic verse 'wanhar'.
B) The athar of Ali (رضي الله عنه).
C) The practice of the People of the Book.
D) The need to protect the chest.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school places hands under the navel based on the explicit athar of Ali (رضي الله عنه) and the principles of humility and avoiding resemblance to others; the Shafi'i position based on 'wanhar' is refuted by tafsir.

Ruling on Folding Hands in Prayer (Sunnah vs Imam Malik)
Establishes sunnah of hand-folding and refutes Imam Malik's position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on folding hands in prayer and explain the Hanafi proofs against Imam Malik's position.

Core Idea
Placing the right hand on the left in prayer is a confirmed sunnah, not a concession.

The posture of the hands during prayer is a point of difference between the Hanafi and Maliki schools. The Hanafi school, relying on the Prophet's practice and explicit statements, holds that folding the hands is a strong sunnah. Imam Malik treats it as a concession, preferring to leave the hands loose. This lesson examines the evidence and the basis for the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds regarding hand placement in prayer.
The text says 'daayan haath bayen par rakhna masnun hai' (placing right hand on left is sunnah).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognise that Imam Malik considers leaving the hands loose (irsal) as the primary ruling (azima) and folding as a concession (rukhsa).
The text states Imam Malik's view: 'irsal azimat aur i'timad rukhsat hai'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand that Imam Malik's proof is based on the general permissibility of leaving hands loose, citing some Companion practices.
The passage does not elaborate on Maliki evidence; it is inferred from common knowledge.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses three proofs: the Prophet's persistent practice, his explicit command, and the statement of Ali and the incident of Ibn Mas'ud.
The hadith 'ana ma'shar al-anbiya'...' is a direct command, and the correction of Ibn Mas'ud shows prophetic endorsement.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is that Hanafis routinely fold hands, while Malikis may choose either but prefer loose. Both practices are valid.
The thamarah (fruit of disagreement) is the actual posture in prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفة الصلوة
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم پہلے مسئلہ میں ہمارے علما ثلاثہ کا قول یہ ہے کہ نماز میں دایاں ہاتھ بائیں پر رکھنا مسنون ہے اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ ارسال کرنے یعنی نماز میں ہاتھ چھوڑے رکھے اور جی چاہے تو باندھ لے پس امام مالک کے نزدیک ارسال عزیمت اور اعتماد ( ہاتھ رکھنا ) رخصت ہے۔ ہمارے علماء کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ جی نے اس پر مداومت فرمائی اور فرمایا انا معشر الانبياء امرنا بان ناخذ شمائلنا بایما ننافی الصلاة یعنی ہم انبیاء کی جماعت کو حکم دیا گیا کہ ہم نماز میں اپنے دائیں ہاتھ سے بائیں ہاتھ کو پکڑیں۔ اور حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالٰی عنہ نے فرما یا من السنة ان يصنع المصلى يمينه على شماله تحت السرة في الصلاة صاحب ہدایہ نے یہ اثر ان الفاظ کے ساتھ ذکر کیا ان من السنة وضع اليمين على الشمال تحت السرة دونوں کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حضرت علی رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ نے فرمایا کہ نماز میں دائیں ہاتھ کا بائیں ہاتھ پر رکھنا مسنون ہے۔ یہاں یہ بات قابل ذکر ہے کہ ہدایہ کے اصل نسخہ میں یہ عبارت یوں تھی لقول على ان من السنة التا لیکن نادان لکھنے والوں نے اس کو اقولہ علیہ السلام کر دیا۔ اور ابوداؤد میں ہے عن ابن مسعود انه كان يصلى فوضع يده اليسرى على اليمني فراه النبي فوضع يده المنى على اليسرى - ابن مسعود رضی اللہ تعالی عنہ سے روایت ہے کہ وہ نماز پرھتے تھے ہیں انہوں نے اپنا بایاں ہاتھ دائیں پر رکھا حضور نے دیکھا تو ابن مسعود کا دایاں ہاتھ بائیں پر رکھ دیا۔ بہر حال ان روایات سے ثابت ہوا کہ مسنون دا نہیں ہاتھ کا بائیں پر رکھنا ہے ہیں یہ احادیث امام مالک کے خلاف حجت ہوں میں اور جا راندیب ثابت ہوتا۔
Chapter on description of prayer. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume two. First issue: The statement of our three scholars is that in prayer, placing the right hand on the left is sunnah. Imam Malik said: leaving them loose (i.e., leaving hands down in prayer) and if one wishes, one may fold them. So according to Imam Malik, leaving loose is the 'azima (primary ruling) and folding is a rukhsa (concession). The proof of our scholars: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) persisted upon this, and he said: 'We, the company of prophets, have been commanded to take hold of our left hands with our right hands in prayer.' And Sayyiduna Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'It is from the sunnah that the worshipper places his right hand on his left below the navel in prayer.' The author of Hidayah mentioned this effect with these words: 'Indeed it is from the sunnah to place the right on the left below the navel.' The summary of both is that Sayyiduna Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) said that placing the right hand on the left in prayer is sunnah. Here it is worth noting that in the original copy of Hidayah, this phrase was 'li qawli 'Ali anna min al-sunnah...' but ignorant scribes changed it to 'aqwaluhu 'alayhi al-salam'. And in Abu Dawud: from Ibn Mas'ud that he was praying and he placed his left hand on his right; the Prophet saw him and placed Ibn Mas'ud's right hand on his left. In any case, from these narrations it is established that the sunnah is to place the right hand on the left. These hadiths are evidence against Imam Malik, and it is thus proven.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam Malik regarding the ruling on folding hands in prayer. The Hanafi position (Hanafi, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that it is sunnah to place the right hand on the left during prayer. Imam Malik considers leaving hands loose as the primary sunnah (azima) and folding as a concession. The Hanafi proof includes: (1) The Prophet's perpetual practice (fi'l) and his explicit statement that prophets are commanded to hold left with right. (2) The statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) affirming it as sunnah. (3) The incident of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet corrected his hand placement. The commentator notes a textual correction: the original Hidayah read 'li qawli 'Ali' (referencing Ali's statement) but was mistakenly altered to 'aqwaluhu 'alayhi al-salam' (the Prophet's statement). The correct attribution is to Ali, which suffices as a companion's practice. These narrations conclusively establish the sunnah against Imam Malik's view.

Key Terms
مسنون (masnun): An act established by the Prophet's practice, recommended but not obligatory.
ارسال (irsal): Leaving the hands loose at the sides during prayer.
عزیمت (azimat): The primary, stronger ruling in a matter where there is also a concession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi ruling on folding hands in prayer?
A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah (recommended).
C) It is makruh (disliked).
D) It is mubah (permissible).

Key Takeaway
Folding the right hand over the left during prayer is a confirmed sunnah in the Hanafi school, supported by the Prophet's command and practice.
